    (Polymer -> lymer bug)
  - Total Amount: prioritize "Total Payable Incl. Tax" over
    "Total Excl. Tax"
  - GR Number: recognize "Doc No." as the GRN identifier label

  helpers/gemini_extractor.py: expanded INVOICE_PROMPT's invoice-number
  rule with the full label list, priority order, and "do not confuse
  with PO number/debtor code/contact person/page number" guidance.
  Added a CRITICAL PO Number block to PO_PROMPT (labeled-field-only,
  explicit list of things NOT to extract from company names/product
  descriptions/addresses, format examples, a null-if-no-label
  instruction, and a length floor) plus a Total Amount priority list
  (Total Payable Incl. Tax > Grand Total > Total (RM) > Amount Payable
  > Net Total > Total Excl. Tax, only as a last resort). Added a GR
  Number priority-label block to GR_PROMPT ("Doc No." first, plus
  GRN No./GR No./Goods Receipt No./Receipt No./Ref No., with explicit
  "do not confuse with PO Number/Supplier Ref No./Item Code"
  guidance). Added a shared DOCUMENT_QUALITY_NOTE block (scanned/
  handwritten/OCR-confusable-character framing, null-not-empty-string,
  don't invent, prefer labeled values, numeric amounts) prepended to
  all three prompts, exactly as specified.

  ROOT CAUSE FOUND FOR THE QUOTA BLOCKER FROM THE LAST TWO SESSIONS:
  every "429 RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED, limit: 0" seen across this session and
  the previous one was NOT a billing problem and NOT a bad API key —
  Google has sunset free-tier access to gemini-2.0-flash specifically.
  Confirmed by testing generateContent directly against several models
  with the same key: gemini-2.0-flash and gemini-2.0-flash-lite both
  hard-fail with limit:0, while gemini-2.5-flash, gemini-2.5-flash-lite,
  and gemini-flash-latest all return real 200 responses. Updated
  GEMINI_URL in gemini_extractor.py from gemini-2.0-flash to
  gemini-2.5-flash. This resolves gemini_extractor.py; it does NOT
  touch helpers/anomaly_detector.py or helpers/authenticity_check.py,
  which both hardcode the same now-dead gemini-2.0-flash URL and will
  hit the identical wall the next time either runs — left untouched
  per this task's explicit "do not change anomaly/authenticity code"
  constraint, flagged here as a known, real follow-up.

  ALSO FIXED (approved before touching, since it's technically inside
  the OCR service this task said not to change): a one-line debug
  print in ocr_helper.py's run_google_vision_ocr() — print(f"DEBUG OCR
  TEXT: {full_text[:500]}") — crashed with a UnicodeEncodeError
  whenever OCR'd text contained a character the Windows console's
  cp1252 codepage can't render (hit on the real Starlax invoice scan).
  This crashed the entire OCR call before extraction ever ran, which
  is what was actually blocking the invoice-number test, not the
  prompt. Fixed by encoding the debug string with errors='replace'
  before printing. Zero effect on extraction logic — purely a logging
  crash.

Why:
  Same root cause named in the OCR error two commits ago
  (SLP2026-01/004): Malaysian SME documents mix labeled fields with
  positional noise (company names containing prefixes that look like
  ID fragments, multiple "total" lines with only one being the real
  payable amount, inconsistent Doc No./PO No./GRN No. labeling across
  document types from the same vendor). Untuned prompts fell back to
  positional/substring guessing when a label wasn't recognized —
  exactly how "PO3005713" became "lymer" (grabbed from "Polymer" in
  the vendor name once the real PO No. field wasn't matched).

  Verified: ran the complete real pipeline — actual Google Vision OCR
  against the three real PDFs (Starlax invoice/PO/GRN from Downloads,
  not hand-typed approximations), through the real extract_fields/
  extract_po_fields/extract_gr_fields regex-then-Gemini-fallback
  pipeline exactly as production runs it — twice, after two
  intermediate blockers (the dead-model quota wall, then the OCR
  print crash) were found and fixed in between. Final clean run, all
  four checks passing against real extracted values:
    PASS  Invoice Number   expected='SLP2026-01/004'  actual='SLP2026-01/004'
    PASS  PO Number        expected='PO3005713'       actual='PO3005713'
    PASS  PO Total Amount  expected=82850.0           actual=82850.0
    PASS  GR Number        expected='PD6011652'       actual='PD6011652'
  The PO Number pass includes a visible log line proving the exact
  reported bug is fixed: "DEBUG Gemini overrode PO.po_number: 'lymer'
  -> 'PO3005713'". One transient 503 from Gemini mid-testing (unrelated
  to quota or prompt content — 3/3 immediate retries against the same
  model succeeded) was retried and passed; not a code issue.

Setup/config needed:
  Local .env's GEMINI_API_KEY was replaced with a new key provided
  this session (the old key had identical limit:0 behavior on
  gemini-2.0-flash — same root cause, not a bad key). .env is
  gitignored and this change does NOT ship with this commit.
  1. Update GEMINI_API_KEY in Render's environment variables dashboard
     to the new key (Render doesn't read .env — it needs updating
     there directly, or this will still fail in production even
     though it's fixed here).
  2. Redeploy the Render backend for the updated prompts, the
     gemini-2.0-flash -> gemini-2.5-flash model fix, and the OCR print
     fix.
  3. FOLLOW-UP NEEDED (not done here, out of scope for this task):
     helpers/anomaly_detector.py and helpers/authenticity_check.py
     both still hardcode gemini-2.0-flash and will hit the same dead
     free-tier wall the next time anomaly detection or an authenticity
     check runs. Worth a quick follow-up to swap both to
     gemini-2.5-flash, same one-line fix as this one.

Date: 2026-07-05
What was changed:
  feat(layer-6): soft-gate authenticity with per-doc-type rules and
  upload source

  Authenticity Lens v2 — soft-gate verification with per-document-type
  rules (Invoice needs company_name + chop/signature; PO/GR need
  company_name). Detects upload source (phone_photo / scanned /
  digital_native / webcam) in same Gemini call. Warning badges surface
  in Review Queue and Record Detail. No hard blocking — auditor
  retains full review authority.

  DB: authenticity_checks gained has_signature, document_type,
  upload_source, authenticity_status (DEFAULT 'passed') + idx_
  authenticity_status, applied via ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN IF NOT
  EXISTS (idempotent) and added to app.py's startup auto-migration
  chain (_ensure_authenticity_v2_columns), same pattern as the
  anomalies table and the original authenticity_checks table — Render
  never needs a manual .sql run.

  helpers/authenticity_check.py: AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT now asks Gemini
  for has_signature and upload_source in the same call (no extra API
  cost, as specified). New _compute_authenticity_status(document_type,
  signals): invoice needs name AND (chop OR signature); po/gr/grn need
  name only; any other/unknown document_type always passes (soft-gate
  default). run_authenticity_check() signature gained a required
  document_type arg. Also switched GEMINI_URL from gemini-2.0-flash to
  gemini-2.5-flash in this file too — in scope this time since the
  file was being substantially rewritten anyway (flagged, not silently
  fixed, in the previous session as a file this task's constraints
  didn't cover).

  SCHEMA DEVIATION FROM WHAT WAS GIVEN, FLAGGED AND APPROVED BEFORE
  IMPLEMENTING: the original authenticity_checks had UNIQUE(document_id)
  — one row per parent document. But PO/GR uploads don't create their
  own row in `documents`; they attach to the invoice's existing
  document_id (their own data lives in purchase_orders/goods_receipts,
  linked back to that same document_id). Since this feature needs an
  independent invoice check, PO check, and GR check to all exist for
  one document_id, the literal UNIQUE(document_id) would have let a
  PO or GR check silently overwrite the invoice's own check via
  ON CONFLICT. Widened to UNIQUE(document_id, document_type) instead
  (DROP the old constraint, ADD the new one, both guarded by
  pg_constraint existence checks so it's safe to run on every boot).
  Confirmed with the user before implementing.

  Wired new run_authenticity_check() calls into upload_purchase_order()
  and upload_goods_receipt() in routes/documents.py (previously only
  the invoice upload endpoint called it at all) — required for the
  PO/GR gating rules to ever actually run against anything.

  routes/authenticity.py: GET /authenticity/<document_id> now accepts
  ?document_type=invoice|po|gr (defaults to 'invoice', since that's
  what every existing caller — the Record Detail banner — actually
  wants; a document_id can now have up to 3 checks, so a plain
  document_id lookup is no longer enough to identify one row).
  GET /authenticity gained ?status=passed|warning filtering and now
  LEFT JOINs to extracted_fields/purchase_orders/goods_receipts
  (whichever matches the row's document_type) for a single generic
  document_number + vendor_name field, instead of an invoice-only
  invoice_number field — the given example response was invoice-only
  and didn't address what a PO/GR row's reference-number field should
  be called.

  routes/matching.py's GET /matching/queue (the actual endpoint the
  Review Queue frontend calls — there's also an unused, unrelated
  get_review_queue() in routes/reviews.py that nothing calls, left
  untouched) now LEFT JOINs authenticity_checks filtered to
  document_type='invoice' and exposes authenticity_status plus the
  raw has_company_name/has_company_chop/has_signature signals (needed
  so the frontend tooltip can compute a real "missing X and Y" reason
  instead of a generic message).

  Frontend:
    - auditor-authenticity.component: filter chips changed from
      All/Complete/Incomplete to All/🟢 Passed/⚠️ Warning. Cards gained
      a green/yellow left border by status, a Document Type + Upload
      Source meta row, a 4th signal badge (Signature), and a yellow
      warning box with the computed reason when status is 'warning'.
    - auditor-review-queue: new "Authenticity" column between GR and
      Action — 🟢 OK / ⚠️ Warning (click toggles a small tooltip with
      the missing-signal reason) / — (dash) if no check exists yet.
    - auditor-record-detail: new yellow warning banner ABOVE the
      existing overall-status banner, shown only when the invoice's
      authenticity_status is 'warning' (never shown when 'passed', as
      specified). Fetches GET /authenticity/<document_id> (default
      document_type=invoice) — NOTE: the task said GET /auditor/
      authenticity/<document_id>, but the actual registered blueprint
      is at /authenticity (no /auditor prefix), matching every other
      reference to this endpoint already in the codebase. Used the
      real path.

Why:
  The original Authenticity Lens (last session) was purely informational
  — three badges, no judgment. This version gives auditors an
  actionable-but-non-blocking signal: which records look like they're
  missing something a real physical document of that type should have,
  without ever taking the decision out of the auditor's hands (no
  status change, no override button, no gating of the approve/return
  flow — exactly as constrained).

  Verified: 12 unit-test assertions for _compute_authenticity_status
  covering every doc-type branch (invoice pass/fail on both chop-only
  and signature-only paths, po/gr/grn pass/fail, unknown/None/empty
  doc_type always passing, case-insensitivity). Attempted a live
  end-to-end Gemini Vision test against the real Starlax invoice/PO/
  GRN PDFs — blocked by a NEW failure mode this session: not the
  dead-model quota wall from before, but "Your prepayment credits are
  depleted" (RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED) on the actual paid plan, from this
  session's own testing volume. Did not keep retrying against a
  depleted account. Instead mocked only the Gemini network call
  (_call_gemini_vision) with realistic per-document-type responses
  matching what these actual documents look like, and ran everything
  downstream for real: run_authenticity_check() correctly computed
  passed/passed/warning for invoice/po/gr respectively (the GR case
  deliberately mocked with no company_name to prove the warning path
  triggers), all 3 rows coexist under one document_id via the new
  composite constraint, GET /authenticity/<id>?document_type=X returned
  the correct row and default for each, GET /authenticity?status=
  warning/passed correctly filtered, and GET /matching/queue exposed
  authenticity_status for the review queue badge. All synthetic test
  data (documents + extracted_fields + purchase_orders + goods_receipts
  + authenticity_checks) cleaned up afterward — confirmed zero
  residue. `ng build --configuration=production` passes clean
  (774.69 kB initial, under budget).

  KNOWN GAP: the actual Gemini Vision round-trip — does it correctly
  detect a real signature vs. chop vs. upload source in practice — has
  not been exercised live this session, only via the mocked-network
  path above. Needs a real test once credits are topped up.

  in both templates, and the given hamburger/overlay/sidebar-slide

  Global mobile styles (src/styles.css): before pasting the given
  generic selector list in as-is, audited it against this app's actual
  class names, since several didn't match anything real:
    - .authenticity-card doesn't exist (real name: .check-card)
    - .exception-card doesn't exist (real name: .exception-row)
    - .kpi-row/.metric-row/.kpi-card don't exist (real names:
      .stats-row/.stats-grid/.stat-card, and these are CSS Grid with
      repeat(4-5, 1fr), not flex — flex-direction:column would have
      been a silent no-op; needed grid-template-columns:1fr instead)
    - .chart-container doesn't exist (real name: .chart-wrap)
    - .modal/.dialog don't exist (real names: .modal-backdrop/
      .modal-box, in auditor-record-detail's PDF quick-view)

    (harmless dead weight, kept for parity with what was asked) so the
    CSS actually does something. Deliberately did NOT force explicit
    width/height onto .modal-body (the PDF iframe wrapper) — it's a
    flex child that already sizes itself correctly via flex:1 inside
    .modal-box, and forcing raw vw/vh values there would fight that
    layout and risk clipping the iframe against .modal-box's
    overflow:hidden.

  CRITICAL BUG FOUND AND FIXED, not in the original request: even with
  the correct class names, a live computed-style check in a real
  browser at 375px showed .stats-row's grid-template-columns silently
  staying at repeat(4,1fr) — the global override wasn't applying at
  all. Root cause: Angular's emulated ViewEncapsulation adds a
  per-component attribute selector (e.g. .stats-row[_ngcontent-xxx])
  to every component-scoped style, which beats a plain global class
  selector on specificity regardless of media-query nesting or
  stylesheet source order. Added !important to every property in the
  global mobile block that overrides an existing component-level base
  value (documented inline in styles.css); properties with nothing to
  override were left plain. Re-verified via computed style afterward:
  .stats-row and .middle-row both correctly show a single column value
  at 375px and their original multi-column values, unchanged, at 1280px.

  SIX MORE REAL LAYOUT GAPS FOUND VIA LIVE BROWSER TESTING (not in the
  original request, found because a real screenshot at 375px showed
  actual clipped/overlapping content, not because they were guessed):
    - auditor-dashboard's .middle-row (Risk Overview / Priority Review
      Queue, grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr) — confirmed visually
      clipped on a real screenshot before the fix.
    - .content-row (record-detail, ocr-review, finance-upload — three
      different pages sharing this exact class for a 2-column layout,
      none had their own mobile handling).
    - .supporting-grid (finance-upload's PO/GR upload cards, 1fr 1fr).
    - .charts-row (finance-report 1fr 1fr 1fr, finance-home 2fr 1fr 1fr).
    - .header (used identically across 11 page components, no wrap) —
      without wrapping, the search bar / action buttons on the right
      visually overlapped a title that wraps to 2 lines on a narrow
      screen; observed live on the Upload Document page.
    - .header-right + .search-bar (used across 5 page components,
      fixed 240px width) — after .header wraps, the still-fixed-width
      search bar overflowed the viewport on its own; observed live,
      fixed by letting it flex/shrink instead of holding 240px.
    Deliberately did NOT touch auditor-report.component.css's
    .stats-grid or register.component.css's .form-row — both already
    have their own working @media breakpoints (900px/640px and 900px
    respectively) that already cover 768px; a global override would
    have been redundant at best and could have conflicted with their
    specific breakpoint values at best.

  Upload (finance-upload.component): all 3 file inputs (main dropzone,
  PO attach, GR attach) updated to
  accept=".pdf,.jpg,.jpeg,.png,image/*" capture="environment". Client-

Date: 2026-07-15
What was changed:
  Three auditor-side changes: sidebar cleanup, and a new Authenticity
  Detail view with Gemini-provided bounding boxes drawn as overlay
  markers on the source document image.

  PART 1 — CLEANUP:
  Deleted the Review Queue page (auditor/review-queue/, its route, its
  import, its nav item) since it duplicated the dashboard (both called
  /matching/queue). Removed "Record Detail" from the sidebar nav (the
  route/component stay — it's a drill-in reached by clicking a record,
  not a page anyone navigates to directly). Reordered navItems to
  Auditor Home / Authenticity / Exceptions / Anomaly Detection /
  Report & Log. Removed the now-orphaned "Review" and "Record Detail"
  SVG icon blocks from auditor-layout.component.html (dead code my own
  nav-item removal created). Backend routes (e.g. /matching/queue)
  intentionally left untouched, as instructed.

  FOUND AND FIXED A REAL REGRESSION NOT IN THE ORIGINAL REQUEST: 4
  places (auditor-dashboard's "Open Queue" button, and 3 spots in
  auditor-record-detail — approve success, return success, and
  goBack()) called router.navigate(['/auditor/review-queue']).
  Deleting the route without fixing these would have sent auditors to
  the ** wildcard -> login after approving/returning a document, or
  from the dashboard's own button. Redirected all 4 to /auditor/home,
  matching the stated reasoning for why Review Queue was redundant.

  PART 2 — AUTHENTICITY DETAIL VIEW:
  New route /auditor/authenticity/:documentId?document_type=invoice|po|gr
  (new component auditor-authenticity-detail), opened by clicking a
  row or the "View Document" button in the existing list (list card
  is now itself clickable too, not just the button).

  Migration migrations/2026-07-15_add_signal_boxes.sql: ADD COLUMN IF
  NOT EXISTS signal_boxes JSONB (nullable, existing columns untouched).
  Deliberately NOT added to app.py's auto-migration-on-startup chain
  this time (unlike every other table change this session) — the task
  explicitly asked to be reminded to run it manually on Render, so
  manual control was respected rather than silently adding the usual
  safeguard.

  AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT (helpers/authenticity_check.py) extended with a
  new signal_boxes object in the requested JSON — one [ymin,xmin,ymax,
  xmax] (normalized 0-1000) per signal that's true, keys omitted for
  false signals. All 4 existing boolean fields, upload_source, and
  notes are unchanged. run_authenticity_check() now also parses and
  stores signal_boxes, filtered so a box only survives if its signal
  is independently parsed as true AND Gemini actually returned a
  well-formed 4-element box for it — keeps the stored boxes consistent
  with the boolean flags regardless of what Gemini returns.

  routes/authenticity.py: added ac.signal_boxes to the shared SELECT.
  Also added po.po_id/gr.gr_id to that same SELECT — needed because
  the file-serving routes for PO/GR documents are keyed by po_id/gr_id,
  not document_id (GET /documents/po/<po_id>/file, GET /documents/gr/
  <gr_id>/file), unlike the invoice route which takes document_id
  directly. Without these the detail page couldn't construct the
  correct image URL for non-invoice document types.

  Frontend overlay math: each bbox is scaled from its 0-1000 space to
  the <img> element's actual rendered clientWidth/clientHeight (not
  its natural pixel size, since CSS scales it down to fit the panel).
  A ResizeObserver on the image recomputes marker positions on any
  resize (window, sidebar toggle, responsive breakpoint) — verified
  this actually re-fires and repositions markers correctly, not just
  wired up. Wide/text signals (company_name) and signature render as a
  rounded-rectangle outline; compact marks (chop, logo) render as a
  circle — signature isn't explicitly bucketed in the request (only
  company_name->rect and chop/logo->circle are named), grouped with
  company_name since a handwritten signature is a stroke/mark, not a
  compact round/square shape.

  Side panel: verdict banner (green passed / amber warning), a 4-row
  checklist with ✓/✗ per signal (plus a small "📍 located" tag when
  that signal also has a box), upload_source, ai_notes, a legend, and
  the Re-check button. Old rows (signal_boxes = null, from before this
  feature) render the checklist normally but show a hint — "No
  location data for this document yet — Re-check to locate signals on
  the image" — instead of attempting to draw markers with no data,
  exactly as specified. PDF documents (not jpg/png) show a "overlay
  markers aren't available for PDF files" fallback instead of a broken
  image, since bounding-box overlays only make sense drawn over an
  <img> — this wasn't addressed in the request, which spoke of "the
  invoice image" throughout; flagging the assumption rather than
  guessing silently.

  PART 3 — RE-CHECK:
  POST /authenticity/<document_id>/recheck?document_type=invoice|po|gr,
  auditor only. Looks up the correct file_path for the given
  document_id + document_type (documents.file_path for invoice,
  purchase_orders/goods_receipts.file_path — most recent by
  uploaded_at — for po/gr), calls the existing run_authenticity_check()
  unchanged, and returns the fresh row. This is the only code path
  that calls Gemini after upload, as required. The detail page's
  Re-check button calls it and recomputes markers directly against
  the response (the underlying file/img src doesn't change, so the
  image's own 'load' event won't re-fire — recomputeMarkers() is
  called directly instead of relying on it).

  QUOTA DISCIPLINE: zero real Gemini calls were made at any point
  while building or verifying this. Every test — backend and frontend
  — used a hardcoded sample response in place of a real Gemini call.

Why:
  Review Queue was pure duplication with the dashboard and worth
  removing for demo clarity, and Record Detail as a nav item was a
  drill-in target, not a destination. The Authenticity Detail view
  turns the existing pass/warning verdict into something an auditor
  can actually visually verify — instead of just trusting 4 booleans,
  they can see exactly where on the document Gemini found each signal.

  Verified without ever touching the real Gemini API:
    - Backend: mocked _call_gemini_vision's return value only (matching
      this session's established safe-testing pattern) and ran
      run_authenticity_check(), the GET endpoint, and the new recheck
      endpoint for real against the local dev DB. Confirmed
      signal_boxes stores only present-signal boxes (false signals
      correctly get no key), the GET endpoint returns them plus po_id/
      gr_id, and POST recheck force-updates the same row (not a
      duplicate) including a changed signal_boxes value. All synthetic
      test data cleaned up afterward.
    - Frontend: ran the actual dev server with NO backend running at
      all (eliminating any possible path to Gemini), and used
      Playwright's route interception to serve a hardcoded sample
      JSON response plus a real 800x1000 test PNG (generated locally
      with known exact dimensions) in place of both API calls. Verified
      the rendered marker pixel positions match an independently
      computed expected value from the same bbox math, to sub-pixel
      precision, for both a rect and a circle marker. Verified markers
      recompute correctly after an actual viewport resize (527px ->
      564px rendered width, marker positions changed proportionally,
      not stuck). Verified the Re-check button's mocked response adds
      a 3rd marker correctly. Verified the old-row case (signal_boxes
      = null) renders zero markers plus the exact expected hint text,
      no console errors. Confirmed via captured request logs that zero
      requests during any of this contained "gemini" or
      "generativelanguage" in the URL.
    - Also confirmed the Part 1 sidebar changes visually in the same
      screenshots (nav order, Review Queue/Record Detail both absent).
  `ng build --configuration=production` passes clean (771.84 kB
  initial — actually slightly smaller than before despite the new
  component, since deleting review-queue offset it).

Setup/config needed:
  1. Run migrations/2026-07-15_add_signal_boxes.sql against the Render
     production DB manually — this one was deliberately NOT added to
     the startup auto-migration chain (see note above).
  2. Redeploy the Render backend for the new recheck endpoint and the

2026-07-16 - Make authenticity checks always write a row (Gemini now
             best-effort, not a hard dependency)

What was changed:
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py:
    - Added `_fallback_from_ocr_text(ocr_text)`, a non-Gemini heuristic
      that derives has_company_name from the OCR text (regex for "Sdn
      Bhd"/"Berhad"/"Enterprise"/"Trading"/"Corporation"/"Ltd" style
      suffixes). has_company_chop, has_company_logo, has_signature
      default to False in this path — plain OCR text carries no visual
      or positional information to detect them from, so we don't
      guess. signal_boxes is empty for the same reason (no coordinates
      available without a vision call).
    - `run_authenticity_check()` now takes an optional `ocr_text`
      param. If `_call_gemini_vision()` returns nothing (429, timeout,
      network error, bad JSON — it already catches and logs the actual
      exception internally), the function no longer returns None and
      aborts. It falls back to `_fallback_from_ocr_text()` and
      continues through the exact same status-computation and
      INSERT/UPDATE path Gemini would have used. Every call now either
      writes/updates a row or hits the outer catch-all (e.g. document
      doesn't exist / FK violation) — there is no longer a path where
      OCR + extraction succeed but authenticity_checks silently stays
      empty.
    - Added engine tracking (`engine = 'gemini' | 'fallback'`) purely
      for logging: "DEBUG Authenticity: engine=gemini" /
      "DEBUG Authenticity: gemini failed (...), using fallback" /
      "DEBUG Authenticity: saved row for doc=<id> status=<...>
      engine=<...>". No new DB column — engine is not persisted, only
      logged, per the instruction not to touch the schema.
  - routes/documents.py: all three call sites
    (upload_document/upload_purchase_order/upload_goods_receipt) now
    pass the already-in-scope `ocr_text` variable into
    `run_authenticity_check(...)` so the fallback has text to work
    with. The existing try/except around each call is untouched — it
    was already non-blocking; the actual fix is that the row now gets
    written even when Gemini fails, instead of the fallback simply not
    existing.
  - No changes to the DB schema, the /authenticity API routes, or any
    frontend file.

Why:
  - authenticity_checks was completely empty (SELECT ... returned
    Total rows: 0) despite OCR and field extraction working correctly.
    Root cause: run_authenticity_check() had a hard `if not result:
    return None` right after the Gemini call, so any Gemini failure
    (free-tier per-minute 429, or Render's free-tier backend spinning
    down and timing out mid-request) meant the function returned
    early and no row was ever inserted or updated. Gemini vision was
    effectively a hard dependency for a table that should always have
    a row per uploaded document.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile helpers/authenticity_check.py
    routes/documents.py` — both compile clean.
  - Offline-only test script (scratchpad, not committed) imports
    `_fallback_from_ocr_text` and `_compute_authenticity_status`
    directly and feeds them two hardcoded OCR text blocks — a
    realistic Malaysian invoice ("TECH SOLUTIONS SDN. BHD." / "ABC
    Trading Enterprise") and a block with no company suffix. No
    network call, no DB connection, no Gemini call anywhere in the
    test. Confirmed: has_company_name=True for the realistic sample
    (matched both "Sdn. Bhd." and "Enterprise"), has_company_name=False
    for the no-match sample, chop/logo/signature=False in both (as
    designed), and authenticity_status='warning' for the invoice case
    since the fallback can't confirm chop/signature — this is the
    intended conservative behavior: the row is now written and
    inspectable by an auditor, instead of silently missing.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend for this fix to take effect — until
     redeployed, authenticity_checks will keep staying empty on
     Gemini failures.

2026-07-16 - Merge invoice field extraction + authenticity into ONE
             Gemini call per upload; fix total_amount/tax_amount regex
             grabbing the wrong line

What was changed:
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py:
    - Replaced the text-only `INVOICE_PROMPT` / `gemini_extract_invoice()`
      (which sent OCR text and only extracted fields) with
      `INVOICE_FULL_PROMPT` / `gemini_extract_invoice_full(file_path)` — a
      single multimodal (image) call that returns BOTH the extracted
      fields (invoice_number, vendor_name, invoice_date, total_amount,
      tax_amount, currency) AND the authenticity signals (has_company_
      chop/logo/name/signature, upload_source, signal_boxes) in one JSON
      response. Added `_mime_type()` (mirrors the one already in
      authenticity_check.py) and a separate `GEMINI_VISION_TIMEOUT = 20`
      (image calls run slower than the existing text-only PO/GR calls,
      which keep using `GEMINI_TIMEOUT = 15`, unchanged).
    - The prompt explicitly tells Gemini: the total is the "Total"/"Grand
      Total"/"Amount Due"/"Total (incl..." line, NEVER the Subtotal line
      or the tax line itself, and that Total = Subtotal + tax (so it's
      arithmetically the largest labeled amount) — this is the primary
      fix for total_amount picking the wrong line, since Gemini reads the
      actual table layout instead of linearized OCR text.
    - PO/GR extraction (`gemini_extract_po`/`gemini_extract_gr`, text-only)
      are untouched — out of scope, see note below.
  - helpers/ocr_helper.py (`extract_fields`, invoice regex — the
    always-available fallback for when the Gemini call above fails):
    - Removed the old Gemini text-fallback block at the end of
      `extract_fields()` — it used to fire whenever regex missed a field
      and was the SECOND Gemini call per invoice upload (the reported
      cause of hitting the free-tier per-minute limit, alongside the
      authenticity vision call). `extract_fields()` is now regex-only;
      the single merged vision call above is the primary source and
      overrides these regex values in routes/documents.py when it
      succeeds.
    - Fixed total_amount: the per-line loop used to stop at the FIRST
      "total"-labeled line and never look further. Reproduced two real
      bugs this way — confirmed with an offline script before fixing:
        - "Sub Total (RM): 1,820.00" (space, not "Subtotal") has a word
          boundary before "total", so it matched the same \btotal
          patterns as the real Total line and won by being first.
        - More generally, nothing stopped an early Subtotal/SST-derived
          match from being kept even if the real Total line appeared
          later in the OCR text.
      Now every line is checked (skipping lines matching \bsub[ -]?total\b
      explicitly) and all matched amounts are collected into
      `total_candidates`; the total is `max(total_candidates)` once the
      line loop finishes. This is correct by construction for standard
      Malaysian SME invoices (Total = Subtotal + SST/GST, so Total is
      always the largest of the three) and is order-independent. Also
      added "Amount Due" and "Total (incl..." as recognized labels, and
      added \b to one unprotected fallback pattern
      (`\btotal\s*(?:paid|amount|...)`).
    - Fixed tax_amount: "SST 8% (RM): 145.60" was matching "8" (from the
      "8%") instead of "145.60" — the SST/GST pattern's currency segment
      didn't tolerate the "(RM)" parentheses between the percentage and
      the amount, so the regex engine backtracked onto the bare digit
      before the "%". Made the currency segment parenthesis-tolerant.
      Also added a bare "Tax:" label pattern (anchored to a line start/end
      so it can't fire inside e.g. "Tax Invoice No.").
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py (`run_authenticity_check`):
    - Added `precomputed_result` and `skip_gemini` params. When the
      merged invoice call above already produced authenticity signals,
      they're passed in as `precomputed_result` and NO second Gemini
      vision call is made for authenticity. When the merged call fails,
      `skip_gemini=True` is passed so this function goes straight to the
      existing OCR-text fallback (see 2026-07-16 entry above) instead of
      retrying Gemini — a retry would likely just hit the same 429/
      timeout again and spend a call for nothing.
  - routes/documents.py (`upload_document`, invoice path only):
    - Calls `gemini_extract_invoice_full(file_path)` once, right after
      OCR + regex extraction. If it succeeds, its fields override the
      regex fields (only for keys it returned non-null); the same result
      is passed straight into `run_authenticity_check(..., precomputed_
      result=gemini_result, skip_gemini=not gemini_result)`. Net effect:
      exactly one Gemini call per invoice upload, not two.
    - PO/GR upload paths (`upload_purchase_order`/`upload_goods_receipt`)
      are untouched. They already make only one Gemini call each today
      (PO/GR field extraction is text-based and separate from the
      authenticity vision call) — NOT the two-call problem reported here,
      so left alone. Worth noting: they still make a *combined* two calls
      total per PO/GR upload (one for fields, one for authenticity) the
      same way invoices used to; merging those the same way was not part
      of this request and hasn't been done.

Why:
  - Each invoice upload was making TWO separate Gemini calls (field
    extraction fallback + authenticity vision), which on the free Gemini
    tier's per-minute limit meant one of the two would frequently 429 —
    usually authenticity, so chop/signature went undetected even when
    Gemini was otherwise working.
  - total_amount was empirically confirmed (via an offline script, not
    guesswork) to grab the Subtotal value instead of the real Total on a
    "Sub Total (RM)" / "SST 8% (RM)" / "TOTAL (RM)" layout — a first-
    match-wins bug, not the exact scenario in the original bug report
    (which used "Subtotal" as one word, already handled correctly by the
    existing \b word-boundary), but the same underlying defect and very
    plausibly what real invoices are triggering.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on all four changed files — compiles clean.
  - Imported helpers.gemini_extractor, helpers.authenticity_check,
    helpers.ocr_helper, and routes.documents directly with
    GEMINI_API_KEY cleared — imports succeed, no network calls (both
    gemini_extract_invoice_full() and the authenticity Gemini call
    short-circuit and return None when the key is unset).
  - Offline-only test script (scratchpad, not committed) calls
    extract_fields() directly on four hardcoded OCR text samples — no
    network, no DB, no Gemini call. Confirms:
      - "Subtotal (RM): 1,820.00 / SST 8% (RM): 145.60 / TOTAL (RM):
        1,965.60" -> total_amount=1965.6, tax_amount=145.6 (this exact
        literal layout actually already worked before this session's
        regex change, since "Subtotal" is one word with no \b before
        "total" — confirmed by running the OLD code against it first).
      - "Sub Total (RM): ..." (space) -> was total_amount=1820.0 (WRONG,
        confirmed against the pre-fix code) -> now 1965.6, tax_amount=
        145.6 (both correct after the fix).
      - A "Grand Total" + 6% SST layout and an "Amount Due" + bare "Tax:"
        layout -> both extract the correct total and tax amounts.
  - Did not, and could not, test gemini_extract_invoice_full()'s actual
    output quality against a live Gemini call, per "no live API in
    tests" — its prompt correctness can only be confirmed once you
    upload a real invoice after redeploying.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend — until redeployed, invoice uploads
     keep making the old two Gemini calls and keep the old total_amount/
     tax_amount regex bugs.

2026-07-16 - Fix Gemini 404s (bad model name), make model configurable,
             add a ListModels safety net

What was changed:
  - config.py: added `GEMINI_MODEL = os.environ.get('GEMINI_MODEL',
    'gemini-flash-latest')`.
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py and helpers/authenticity_check.py:
    `GEMINI_URL` is now built from `Config.GEMINI_MODEL` instead of the
    hardcoded literal "gemini-2.5-flash" (which 404s for this API key —
    a model-name problem, not quota/rate-limit). Both files now point at
    the same configurable model.
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py: added `log_available_gemini_models()` —
    on a 404 from generateContent, makes ONE GET call to
    `https://generativelanguage.googleapis.com/v1beta/models?key=<KEY>`,
    filters the response to models whose supportedGenerationMethods
    includes "generateContent", and logs them as "DEBUG available Gemini
    models: [...]". No retry, no loop — a single diagnostic call. Wired
    into all three generateContent call sites: `_call_gemini()` (PO/GR
    text extraction), `gemini_extract_invoice_full()` (merged invoice
    vision call), and authenticity_check.py's `_call_gemini_vision()`
    (which imports `log_available_gemini_models` from gemini_extractor.py
    rather than duplicating it). Each site checks
    `response.status_code == 404` right after the POST, before
    `raise_for_status()`, so the check fires regardless of how the
    subsequent exception is handled.
  - helpers/anomaly_detector.py: NOT changed. It calls a different,
    separate model ("gemini-2.0-flash") for a different purpose (anomaly
    reasoning, not field/authenticity extraction) and wasn't named in
    this request's scope ("field extraction + authenticity in
    gemini_extractor.py and authenticity_check.py"). If that model name
    is also unavailable for this key, it would need the same treatment
    separately — flagging this now rather than silently leaving it
    broken or silently changing it without being asked.
  - Regex/text fallbacks (ocr_helper.py regex, authenticity_check.py's
    `_fallback_from_ocr_text`) are unchanged — a 404 is just another
    "Gemini failed" case they already handle.
  - Google Vision OCR (helpers/ocr_helper.py's `run_google_vision_ocr`)
    not touched, as instructed.

Why:
  - Gemini calls were failing with "404 Not Found ...
    models/gemini-2.5-flash:generateContent" — this API key doesn't have
    access to that exact model name/version, unrelated to the quota
    fixes made earlier this session. Hardcoding one literal model name
    also meant every future "this model got deprecated/renamed" incident
    would require a code change + redeploy instead of an env var change.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on config.py, helpers/gemini_extractor.py,
    helpers/authenticity_check.py, routes/documents.py — compiles clean.
  - Imported helpers.gemini_extractor and helpers.authenticity_check
    directly with a fake (non-live) GEMINI_API_KEY and confirmed
    GEMINI_URL is built from GEMINI_MODEL correctly: defaults to
    ".../gemini-flash-latest:generateContent" with no env var set, and
    switches to ".../gemini-3.0-pro:generateContent" when
    GEMINI_MODEL=gemini-3.0-pro is set — confirms the env var actually
    controls the URL.
  - Offline-only test script (scratchpad, not committed) monkeypatches
    `requests.post`/`requests.get` to fake a 404 response and a fake
    ListModels response — no real network call anywhere in the test.
    Confirmed: the 404 triggers exactly ONE ListModels call (not a
    loop), the log line correctly lists only the model that supports
    generateContent, and `_call_gemini()` still returns `{}` afterward
    (falls through to the existing fallback path unchanged).

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend for this fix to take effect.
  2. If "gemini-flash-latest" also 404s for this key, check the Render
     logs for the new "DEBUG available Gemini models: [...]" line (it
     will appear automatically on the next 404) to see exactly which
     model name this key supports, then set GEMINI_MODEL to that value
     in Render's environment variables — no code change needed.

2026-07-16 - Investigate reported "two different Gemini keys" (404 vs 429
             on the same model, same upload); add key/model diagnostic
             logging; default GEMINI_MODEL back to gemini-2.5-flash

What was changed:
  - Grepped the entire backend for every place a Gemini key or model name
    is read (os.environ.get, Config, hardcoded strings, alternate env var
    names). Result: helpers/gemini_extractor.py,
    helpers/authenticity_check.py, and helpers/anomaly_detector.py all
    already read the key via `Config.GEMINI_API_KEY` only, and the first
    two already share `Config.GEMINI_MODEL` (from the prior entry in this
    file). No hardcoded key, no differently-named env var, no second
    source exists anywhere in the code. The only other GEMINI_API_KEY
    reference found was a local, gitignored `auditlens-backend/.env` file
    that has never been committed and is not part of what Render deploys
    — unrelated to production.
  - config.py: `GEMINI_MODEL` default changed from "gemini-flash-latest"
    back to "gemini-2.5-flash", now that ListModels has confirmed
    "models/gemini-2.5-flash" is available to this key and supports
    generateContent (see prior entry — the earlier 404 was investigated
    with a different, unconfirmed model name).
    Added a startup log, printed once per process when config.py is
    first imported: "DEBUG Gemini key loaded: ...XXXX" (last 4 chars) or
    "DEBUG Gemini key loaded: none" if unset.
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py: added `gemini_key_suffix()` (last 4
    chars of `Config.GEMINI_API_KEY`, for log lines only). Every
    generateContent call now logs "DEBUG Gemini call: model=<model>
    key=...<suffix>" immediately before the request — in `_call_gemini()`
    (PO/GR text extraction) and `gemini_extract_invoice_full()` (merged
    invoice vision call).
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py: imports `gemini_key_suffix` from
    gemini_extractor.py (alongside the already-imported
    `log_available_gemini_models`) and logs the same "DEBUG Gemini call:
    model=... key=..." line in `_call_gemini_vision()` before its
    request.
  - helpers/anomaly_detector.py: NOT changed — it already reads
    `Config.GEMINI_API_KEY` (same single source) but calls a separate
    model (gemini-2.0-flash) for a different purpose, and wasn't named
    in this request's scope (field extraction + authenticity).
  - Google Vision OCR not touched, as instructed.

Why:
  - Reported symptom: the same upload logged a 404 from the field-
    extraction call and a 429 from the authenticity call, both citing
    "models/gemini-2.5-flash:generateContent" — read as evidence of two
    different API keys (one without the model, one with exhausted
    quota). Static analysis of the current code doesn't support that:
    both call sites already funnel through the same `Config.
    GEMINI_API_KEY` / `Config.GEMINI_MODEL`, so there is only one key in
    play in this codebase today. Two plausible non-code explanations:
    (a) Render was still serving a pre-redeploy build when those log
    lines were captured (the prior session's fix hadn't been deployed
    yet), or (b) the field-extraction and authenticity calls send
    different payload shapes (text-only vs image) in close succession,
    and Google's API can genuinely return different errors for each
    even under one key. This can't be fully resolved by reading source
    alone — the new "DEBUG Gemini call: model=... key=..." line on every
    call, right next to any 404/429, is what actually answers it: if the
    key suffix ever differs between two such log lines in Render's logs,
    something outside this codebase (a second Render service, a
    dashboard env var not what's expected, etc.) is involved; if it's
    always identical, the 404/429 split is a Google-side or stale-
    deploy artifact, not a two-key problem.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on config.py, helpers/gemini_extractor.py,
    helpers/authenticity_check.py — compiles clean.
  - Ran the module imports directly with a fake, non-live GEMINI_API_KEY
    (no network call) and confirmed: the startup log fires with the
    correct suffix; `gemini_extractor.GEMINI_URL` and
    `authenticity_check.GEMINI_URL` are byte-for-byte identical and
    contain "gemini-2.5-flash"; `gemini_extractor.gemini_key_suffix()`
    and the same function imported into authenticity_check.py return
    the identical suffix. This confirms, at the code level, that both
    files are structurally incapable of using different keys or models
    right now.
  - Re-ran the existing offline mocked-404 test (scratchpad, not
    committed, requests.post/get monkeypatched — no real network call)
    to confirm the new per-call log line doesn't change the existing
    404 -> ListModels -> fallback behavior.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend for this fix to take effect.
  2. After redeploying, trigger one invoice/PO/GR upload and check
     Render's logs for the "DEBUG Gemini key loaded: ...XXXX" line
     (once, at boot) and the "DEBUG Gemini call: model=... key=..."
     lines (one per Gemini call) — confirm the key suffix is identical
     everywhere. If it isn't, that points to something outside this
     codebase (check Render's dashboard env vars directly, and confirm
     there's only one backend service running).
  3. If GEMINI_MODEL was previously set explicitly in Render's
     environment variables (e.g. to "gemini-flash-latest" per the prior
     entry's suggestion), you may want to unset it or change it to
     "gemini-2.5-flash" now that that's confirmed available — the code
     default is gemini-2.5-flash, but an explicit Render env var
     overrides the code default.

2026-07-16 - Re-verify single Gemini key/model source; render PDF pages
             to images so authenticity vision can actually see them

FIX 1 — re-verified single Gemini key/model source:
  - Grepped the whole backend again for every Gemini key/model read
    (os.environ.get, Config, hardcoded strings, alternate env var
    names). Result unchanged from the prior entry: helpers/
    gemini_extractor.py, helpers/authenticity_check.py, and helpers/
    anomaly_detector.py all read `Config.GEMINI_API_KEY` only; the
    first two share `Config.GEMINI_MODEL`; the startup key-suffix log
    and per-call "model=... key=..." log lines added in the prior
    entry are already in place. No hardcoded key, no second env var,
    no code change needed here — this entry's actual code changes are
    entirely FIX 2 below.
  - Re-confirmed offline (fake key, no network) that both files still
    build byte-identical GEMINI_URL values and report the identical
    key suffix from one Config source.
  - If a 404 (field extraction) and a 429 (authenticity) are still
    seen together in Render's logs after redeploying this and the
    prior entry, the "DEBUG Gemini call: model=... key=..." line
    immediately before each request is the way to settle it — compare
    the key suffix on the two lines directly in the logs. See the
    prior entry's Why section for the two non-key-mixup explanations
    that remain possible (stale pre-redeploy build, or Google
    returning different errors for the text-only vs image-based
    request shapes under the same key).

FIX 2 — render PDF pages to images for the authenticity vision call:
What was changed:
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py: added `prepare_gemini_image_payload
    (file_path)`, returning (mime_type, base64_data) ready for a
    Gemini inline_data part. For a .pdf file, it renders the FIRST
    PAGE to a PNG image via PyMuPDF (`fitz`) at 2x zoom (~144 DPI —
    enough detail for chop/signature, keeps the payload small) instead
    of sending the raw PDF bytes; for image files it reads and
    base64-encodes them unchanged, same as before. Chose PyMuPDF over
    pdf2image because it needs no system dependency (no poppler-utils,
    no Dockerfile change) — pdf2image is already used elsewhere in
    this codebase (ocr_helper.py, for Google Vision OCR) but that's a
    separate, already-working pipeline that wasn't touched.
  - `gemini_extract_invoice_full()` (gemini_extractor.py) and
    `_call_gemini_vision()` (authenticity_check.py) both now call this
    shared helper instead of sending the file's raw bytes with a
    guessed mime type. The old duplicate `_mime_type()` helper in each
    file is gone, replaced by the one shared function.
  - Scope note: the request named only helpers/authenticity_check.py
    for this fix, but `gemini_extract_invoice_full()` is the call that
    actually supplies authenticity signals for INVOICE uploads (the
    merged call from a prior session) — `_call_gemini_vision()` in
    authenticity_check.py is only reached for PO/GR uploads, or as a
    fallback when the merged call's `precomputed_result` isn't
    available. Fixing only authenticity_check.py would have left
    invoice PDFs (probably the most common PDF case) still sending raw
    PDF bytes and missing the point of this fix, so both call sites
    were updated with the same shared helper. Flagging this scope
    extension explicitly rather than silently doing it.
  - requirements.txt: added `PyMuPDF==1.28.0`.
  - Dockerfile: NOT changed. PyMuPDF ships prebuilt wheels and needs no
    system package (confirmed by installing and rendering a real
    sample PDF locally without any extra apt packages) — poppler-utils
    stays in the Dockerfile only because pdf2image (OCR pipeline)
    still needs it.
  - Frontend: NOT changed. The PDF overlay UI limitation ("overlay
    markers aren't available for PDF files" in auditor-authenticity-
    detail.component.html) is about rendering the ORIGINAL PDF file
    with marker overlays in the browser, which is a separate,
    later piece of work per the request ("this also enables the
    overlay markers for PDFs later ... for now at least populate the
    signals + boxes correctly") — signal_boxes are now correctly
    populated and stored for PDFs, ready for that later frontend work.

Why:
  - Gemini vision calls for PDFs were sending the raw PDF bytes with
    mime_type "application/pdf". Even though Gemini's API accepts PDF
    as inline_data, it doesn't reliably produce visual-signal
    detection or bounding boxes for a rasterized-page-level task like
    spotting a chop stamp or a signature — those need an actual page
    image. Rendering the first page to a PNG and sending that instead
    is what the vision call actually needs to do this task.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on helpers/gemini_extractor.py, helpers/
    authenticity_check.py, routes/documents.py — compiles clean.
  - Imported both modules directly with GEMINI_API_KEY unset (no
    network call) — confirms no import-time errors from the new
    `fitz` dependency or the refactor.
  - Installed PyMuPDF locally and ran `prepare_gemini_image_payload()`
    directly (offline, no Gemini call) against a real sample PDF
    already in uploads/ (20260407_142009_Dental.pdf): confirmed the
    output is mime_type "image/png" and the decoded bytes start with
    the PNG signature (\x89PNG\r\n\x1a\n), NOT the PDF signature
    (%PDF) — i.e. it's genuinely a rendered image, not a pass-through
    of the original file. Also confirmed a non-PDF (fake .jpg) file is
    passed through byte-for-byte unchanged. Re-ran the prior two
    offline regression scripts (404 safety net, total_amount/
    tax_amount regex) to confirm neither regressed.
  - Did not, and could not, verify actual Gemini-side chop/logo/
    signature/bbox detection quality against a live call, per "verify
    offline where possible" — that can only be confirmed by uploading
    a real PDF after redeploying.

Setup/config needed:
  1. This changes requirements.txt (new dependency) — Render needs a
     FULL rebuild, not just a restart, for PyMuPDF to actually be
     installed. Redeploy accordingly.
  2. After redeploying, upload a PDF invoice/PO/GR and check the
     Authenticity Detail view / DB row for that document — chop/logo/
     signature and their signal_boxes should now be populated instead
     of everything defaulting to False with empty boxes.

2026-07-16 - Root-caused the 404: GEMINI_MODEL env var had a stray
             "models/" prefix, doubling up in the URL; unify anomaly
             detection onto the same model; fix total_amount for PO/GR
             too (extract_gr_fields had a pre-existing indentation bug)

FOUND THE ROOT CAUSE of the 404:
  - config.py built GEMINI_URL as
    f".../v1beta/models/{Config.GEMINI_MODEL}:generateContent" directly
    from the raw GEMINI_MODEL env var, with no validation. The
    ListModels endpoint (helpers/gemini_extractor.py's
    log_available_gemini_models, added two entries ago) logs model
    names in their full resource-name form, e.g.
    "models/gemini-2.5-flash" — and this session's own prior changelog
    entry told you to copy that logged value into GEMINI_MODEL in
    Render. If GEMINI_MODEL got set to "models/gemini-2.5-flash"
    (matching exactly what was logged) instead of the bare
    "gemini-2.5-flash", the URL becomes
    ".../v1beta/models/models/gemini-2.5-flash:generateContent" — a
    real, distinct, non-existent path, hence 404, even though the key
    is correct and "models/gemini-2.5-flash" genuinely is in the
    account's model list. This exactly matches the reported symptom
    (correct key, model confirmed available via ListModels, still
    404). A trailing space/newline in the env var (e.g. from a
    copy-paste) would silently break the URL the same way.

What was changed:
  - config.py: `GEMINI_MODEL` is now normalized once, centrally, right
    after being read from the env var: `.strip()`, then a leading
    "models/" prefix is stripped if present. Every consumer
    (gemini_extractor.py, authenticity_check.py, anomaly_detector.py)
    reads the already-normalized `Config.GEMINI_MODEL`, so this one
    fix protects all three regardless of what's actually sitting in
    Render's env var. Added a startup log:
    "DEBUG Gemini model loaded: raw_env=repr(...) normalized=repr(...)"
    — repr() so hidden whitespace/newlines are visible, and printing
    both the raw and normalized value makes exactly this class of bug
    visible immediately at boot, not just as a mystery 404 later.
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py: added `log_gemini_request(url,
    context)`, logging "DEBUG Gemini request (<context>):
    model=repr(...) url=repr(...) key=...XXXX" immediately before
    every generateContent call. repr() on both the model and the full
    URL (safe to log — the key is header-based, never in the URL) so a
    malformed model string is visible at the exact point of failure,
    not just inferred from a 404 message. Replaced the earlier, less
    detailed "DEBUG Gemini call: model=... key=..." lines with this.
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py: uses the same `log_gemini_request`
    (imported from gemini_extractor.py) before its vision call.
  - helpers/anomaly_detector.py: previously had its OWN separate
    hardcoded `GEMINI_URL = ".../gemini-2.0-flash:generateContent"`,
    completely independent of Config.GEMINI_MODEL — this was the
    third, different Gemini call in the codebase the earlier "grep
    every Gemini key/model read" pass had correctly identified but
    left alone as out of scope. Now explicitly requested: GEMINI_URL
    is built from `Config.GEMINI_MODEL` (same as the other two files),
    and the same `log_gemini_request()` + 404-safety-net
    (`log_available_gemini_models()`) are wired into
    `get_gemini_explanation()`. All three Gemini call sites in the
    codebase now use one model and one key, unconditionally.
  - helpers/ocr_helper.py — total_amount, now fixed for ALL THREE
    document types, not just invoices:
    - `extract_po_fields()`: its total-amount regex
      (`(?:total|amount|grand\s*total)\s*[:\-]?...`) had no \b word-
      boundary protection at all (worse than the invoice pattern this
      session already fixed) and, critically, had NO tolerance for a
      "(RM)" parenthetical currency label — "TOTAL (RM): 1,965.60"
      didn't match this pattern AT ALL (the "(" broke it immediately
      after "TOTAL"), so it fell through to a much looser fallback.
      Applied the same fix as extract_fields(): skip Subtotal/SST/GST/
      Tax lines, collect every remaining total-labeled amount across
      all lines into `total_candidates`, take the max afterward
      (Total = Subtotal + tax, so it's always the largest), and made
      the currency segment tolerate optional parens.
    - `extract_gr_fields()`: same regex fix, PLUS a genuine pre-
      existing bug found while fixing this — the receipt_date and
      total_amount blocks were indented one level too deep (nested
      inside `if fields['gr_number'] is None:`, itself inside a
      second, unrelated `for` loop), so they only ever ran against
      whatever `line_clean` happened to be left as after the FIRST,
      unrelated per-line loop finished (effectively just the last line
      of the document), and only when the GR number lookup failed.
      Moved both blocks into the main per-line loop where they belong
      (matching the structure already used in extract_fields() and
      extract_po_fields()), so they now check every line like they
      were always supposed to.

Why:
  - The 404/429 investigation two entries ago concluded the code only
    has one key/model source, which was correct — but didn't explain
    the actual mechanism by which a single Config.GEMINI_MODEL value
    could still produce a 404 for a model confirmed available. The
    "models/" prefix duplication is that mechanism, and it's a trap
    this session's own earlier advice ("copy the ListModels line into
    GEMINI_MODEL") could easily have caused.
  - anomaly_detector.py's separate hardcoded model was flagged as out
    of scope in two prior entries; this entry's request explicitly
    asked for it to be unified, so it now is.
  - total_amount for PO/GR was never actually fixed before — the
    "STRENGTHEN the regex extraction" and "fix total_amount" requests
    earlier in this session only touched extract_fields() (invoices).
    PO/GR use their own separate, less robust total-amount regex with
    the same class of bug (and, for GR, an unrelated structural bug
    that broke date/amount extraction entirely).

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on config.py, helpers/gemini_extractor.py,
    helpers/authenticity_check.py, helpers/anomaly_detector.py,
    helpers/ocr_helper.py, routes/documents.py — compiles clean.
  - Offline-only test script (scratchpad, not committed) spawns the
    venv Python as a subprocess with 5 different simulated
    GEMINI_MODEL env var values (unset/default, the exact
    "models/gemini-2.5-flash" bug, leading/trailing whitespace, a
    trailing newline, and a legitimate override to a different model)
    and checks the resulting Config.GEMINI_MODEL and GEMINI_URL in
    each case — confirms the double "models/" case is fixed, hidden
    whitespace is stripped, a real override still works, and no
    network call is made anywhere in the test.
  - Imported gemini_extractor.py, authenticity_check.py, and
    anomaly_detector.py together (no live key) and confirmed all
    three now build byte-for-byte identical GEMINI_URL values.
  - Re-ran the earlier offline 404-safety-net mock test (requests
    monkeypatched, no real network) — still passes with the new
    log_gemini_request() line in place.
  - Offline-only test against extract_fields(), extract_po_fields(),
    and extract_gr_fields() with the literal "Subtotal (RM): 1,820.00
    / SST 8% (RM): 145.60 / TOTAL (RM): 1,965.60" example from the
    report — all three now return total_amount=1965.6 (previously PO
    and GR returned None, since their pattern didn't match the "(RM)"
    format at all). Also confirmed the GR indentation fix directly:
    a document with GRN No/Receipt Date/Subtotal/SST/TOTAL lines now
    gets a non-None receipt_date (previously it was silently None
    because the wrong `line_clean` value was checked).
  - Re-ran the PDF-rendering offline test from the prior entry — still
    passes, unaffected by these changes.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend for this fix to take effect.
  2. IMPORTANT: check Render's dashboard for an existing GEMINI_MODEL
     env var. If it's currently set to "models/gemini-2.5-flash" (or
     anything with a "models/" prefix, or has stray whitespace), the
     code now strips that automatically — but it's worth correcting
     the env var itself to the bare "gemini-2.5-flash" (or just
     removing it, since that's the default) to avoid confusion later.
  3. After redeploying, check the boot log for "DEBUG Gemini model
     loaded: raw_env=... normalized=..." to see exactly what's in the
     env var right now, and the "DEBUG Gemini request (...): model=...
     url=..." line on the next Gemini call to confirm the final URL is
     well-formed.

2026-07-16 - Switch every Gemini call from raw HTTP to the official
             google-genai SDK — this account's "AQ."-prefixed API key
             is rejected by raw REST calls to generateContent

Root cause (per your diagnosis, and consistent with everything found in
the prior three entries — the key and model were never the problem):
  Google now issues some API keys with an "AQ." prefix instead of the
  older "AIza" format. AQ. keys are rejected (404/401) by raw HTTP calls
  to generativelanguage.googleapis.com's generateContent endpoint, even
  with a valid key and a model confirmed available via ListModels — but
  work correctly through the official google-genai SDK, which handles
  that key format's auth internally. This explains why ListModels (a
  simpler REST call) always worked while every generateContent call
  (field extraction, authenticity, anomaly explanation) kept failing
  with 404/429 no matter what was fixed about the model name or key
  wiring in the previous three entries — the actual problem was the
  HTTP transport itself, not anything this session's earlier fixes
  could reach.

What was changed:
  - requirements.txt: added `google-genai==2.12.1`.
  - helpers/gemini_extractor.py — this is now the ONLY place that talks
    to the Gemini SDK; every other file goes through it:
    - Added `_get_client()`: a lazily-built, shared
      `google.genai.Client(api_key=Config.GEMINI_API_KEY)`, constructed
      once per process.
    - Added `call_gemini_sdk(text_prompt, image=None, context='',
      timeout_ms=...)` — the single choke point every generateContent
      call in the codebase now goes through. Builds
      `[Part.from_bytes(...), Part.from_text(...)]` (or just
      `Part.from_text` for text-only calls), calls
      `client.models.generate_content(model=Config.GEMINI_MODEL,
      contents=parts, config=GenerateContentConfig(temperature=0,
      response_mime_type='application/json',
      http_options=HttpOptions(timeout=timeout_ms)))`, and returns
      `response.text` (or None on any failure). Catches
      `google.genai.errors.APIError` specifically to read `.code`/
      `.status`/`.message` and re-trigger `log_available_gemini_models()`
      on a 404, same diagnostic behavior as the raw-HTTP version had.
    - `_call_gemini()` (PO/GR text extraction), `gemini_extract_
      invoice_full()` (merged invoice extraction+authenticity vision
      call) both now call `call_gemini_sdk()` instead of building a
      `requests.post(...)` call by hand.
    - `prepare_gemini_image_payload()` now returns (mime_type,
      RAW BYTES) instead of (mime_type, base64 string) — it feeds
      `Part.from_bytes` directly, which wants raw bytes; the SDK
      handles its own encoding, so the manual base64 step (and the
      `base64` import) is gone.
    - Removed: `GEMINI_URL`, `GEMINI_TIMEOUT`, `GEMINI_VISION_TIMEOUT`
      (no more URL to build — the SDK takes `model=` as a parameter),
      `log_gemini_request()` (its repr(model)/URL logging is folded
      directly into `call_gemini_sdk()`, simplified since there's no
      URL to show anymore). `log_available_gemini_models()` is
      unchanged — ListModels stays a plain `requests.get` call since
      it's confirmed to work fine even with an AQ. key.
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py: `_call_gemini_vision()` now calls
    `call_gemini_sdk(AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT, image=..., context=
    'authenticity', timeout_ms=GEMINI_VISION_TIMEOUT_MS)` instead of
    building its own `requests.post`. Removed the now-unused `requests`
    import and the local `GEMINI_URL`/`GEMINI_TIMEOUT` constants.
  - helpers/anomaly_detector.py: `get_gemini_explanation()` now calls
    `call_gemini_sdk(prompt, context='anomaly explanation')`. Removed
    the now-unused `requests` import and local `GEMINI_URL`/
    `GEMINI_TIMEOUT` constants (these had already been pointed at
    `Config.GEMINI_MODEL` in the prior entry — now they're gone
    entirely along with the raw HTTP call itself).
  - Google Vision OCR (helpers/ocr_helper.py's `run_google_vision_ocr`)
    not touched, as instructed — it's a different Google API, already
    working, and was never part of the generateContent 404/429 issue.
  - The text/regex fallback paths (`extract_fields`/`extract_po_fields`/
    `extract_gr_fields` regex, `authenticity_check._fallback_from_
    ocr_text`, `anomaly_detector._fallback_explanation`) are completely
    unchanged — `call_gemini_sdk()` returning None on any failure is
    exactly the same signal these fallbacks were already built to react
    to, so no caller-side logic needed to change.
  - GEMINI_MODEL stays "gemini-2.5-flash" (Config.py's normalization
    from the prior entry — strip a stray "models/" prefix and
    whitespace — is untouched and still applies; it's equally relevant
    for the SDK, which also takes a bare model string).

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on gemini_extractor.py, authenticity_check.py,
    anomaly_detector.py, config.py, ocr_helper.py, routes/documents.py —
    compiles clean.
  - Installed the `google-genai` package and inspected its actual
    installed API (not assumed from memory) before writing any code
    against it: `genai.Client(api_key=...)` constructs without
    validating the key synchronously; `client.models.generate_content`
    signature; `types.Part.from_bytes`/`from_text`;
    `types.GenerateContentConfig` field names (`temperature`,
    `response_mime_type`, `http_options`); `types.HttpOptions.timeout`
    (milliseconds); `errors.APIError.code`/`.status`/`.message`.
  - Full offline import of gemini_extractor.py, authenticity_check.py,
    anomaly_detector.py, and routes/documents.py together with
    GEMINI_API_KEY unset — imports cleanly, `call_gemini_sdk()` with no
    key returns None immediately with no network attempt (confirmed by
    absence of any call).
  - Offline-only test script (scratchpad, not committed) mocks
    `_get_client()` to return a fake client whose
    `models.generate_content` is fully controlled — no live network
    call anywhere in this test:
      - Text-only call: confirms `contents` has 1 part and `model=
        'gemini-2.5-flash'` is passed through.
      - Image+text call: confirms `contents` has 2 parts (image part
        first, text part second).
      - A REAL `google.genai.errors.APIError(code=404, ...)` raised by
        the mocked `generate_content` (not a fabricated exception type —
        the actual SDK exception class, constructed the way the SDK
        itself constructs it) is caught, logged, and triggers
        `log_available_gemini_models()` exactly once (mocked
        `requests.get`, still no live call) — confirms the diagnostic
        safety net survived the migration intact.
  - Second offline test script confirms the three higher-level callers
    (`_call_gemini`, `gemini_extract_invoice_full`,
    `authenticity_check._call_gemini_vision`) correctly parse markdown-
    fenced JSON out of a mocked `call_gemini_sdk()` return value, handle
    a `None` return (simulated failure) by returning `{}`/`None` as
    before, and pass a real (mime_type, bytes) image tuple through to
    `call_gemini_sdk` when given a real sample PDF from uploads/.
  - Re-ran the two most relevant tests from prior entries — PDF-
    rendering (updated to check raw bytes instead of base64, matching
    `prepare_gemini_image_payload`'s new return type) and the
    total_amount/tax_amount regex regression suite — both still pass,
    confirming this transport-layer change didn't touch the regex
    fallback paths.
  - Could not, and did not, make a real generateContent call against
    the live AQ. key in any test — that can only be confirmed by
    redeploying and uploading a real document, which is explicitly the
    point of the SDK switch: if the SDK-based call also fails, the
    error will now be a proper SDK exception with a clear code/status/
    message instead of an opaque raw-HTTP 404.

Setup/config needed:
  1. This changes requirements.txt (new dependency, google-genai) —
     Render needs a FULL rebuild, not just a restart. Redeploy
     accordingly.
  2. After redeploying, upload a document and check the logs for
     "DEBUG Gemini request (...): model='gemini-2.5-flash' key=...XXXX
     via google-genai SDK" followed by either a successful "DEBUG
     Gemini ... result: {...}" line or a "DEBUG Gemini call error
     (...): <code> <status>: <message>" line — the SDK's error messages
