2026-07-16 - Show the rendered PDF page + overlay markers in Authenticity
             Detail instead of "overlay markers aren't available for PDF
             files"

What was changed:

BACKEND:
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py:
    - Added `save_rendered_authenticity_image(document_id, document_type,
      file_path)`: if file_path is a PDF, renders its first page the
      same way prepare_gemini_image_payload() does for the Gemini vision
      call, and saves it to
      `uploads/authenticity/<document_id>_<document_type>.png`
      (AUTHENTICITY_IMAGE_DIR constant). Deterministic filename,
      overwritten on every re-check — deliberately NOT a DB column,
      so no migration/schema change was needed for this feature at all.
      For an image upload (jpg/png), this is a no-op — the original
      file already is the image to show, served directly (see below).
      Never raises; a render/save failure here must not break the
      authenticity row write.
    - Called unconditionally at the top of `run_authenticity_check()`,
      before the Gemini/fallback branching — runs regardless of whether
      Gemini itself succeeds, since the rendered page is useful to show
      either way (with or without overlay markers).
  - routes/authenticity.py: added
    `GET /authenticity/<document_id>/image?document_type=invoice|po|gr`
    (auditor only). Serves the saved rendered PNG if one exists for this
    document_id+document_type; otherwise falls back to the original
    uploaded file directly (the image-upload case) via the existing
    `_lookup_file_path()` helper (already used by the recheck route).
    Returns 404 with a "try Re-check" message if the original is itself
    still a PDF and no rendered image was ever saved (e.g. an
    authenticity check that predates this feature). document_type is
    validated against VALID_DOC_TYPES before being used in the file
    path, since it now feeds into a filename (path-traversal guard).
  - signal_boxes: NO backend change needed — already selected and
    returned by the existing `GET /authenticity/<document_id>` endpoint
    (`_SELECT_WITH_JOINS` already includes `ac.signal_boxes`, confirmed
    by reading the current route code before assuming otherwise).

FRONTEND (auditor-authenticity-detail component):
  - The overlay-marker math, ResizeObserver-driven recompute-on-resize,
    marker CSS (.marker/.marker-rect/.marker-circle), and the legend
    were ALL ALREADY BUILT (from an earlier session, evidently written
    in anticipation of this exact follow-up) — the component's own
    comment literally said "Bounding boxes only make sense drawn over
    an <img>. A raw PDF blob can't be rendered as one, so overlays are
    skipped for PDFs." The only thing missing was a backend endpoint
    that actually served an <img>-renderable file for PDFs. So the
    frontend change ended up much smaller than the request implied:
    - `fileUrl()`: now always returns
      `${apiUrl}/authenticity/${documentId}/image?document_type=...`
      instead of branching between `/documents/{id}/file`,
      `/documents/po/{po_id}/file`, `/documents/gr/{gr_id}/file` — the
      new backend endpoint takes document_id + document_type uniformly
      for all three types, so the po_id/gr_id branching (and the null
      fallback when they weren't present on the check row) is gone.
    - `loadImage()`: removed the `blob.type === 'application/pdf' ?
      'pdf' : 'image'` branch — the new endpoint always returns a real
      image (rendered page or original), so success always means
      `imageLoadState = 'image'`.
    - Removed the `'pdf'` value from the `imageLoadState` type union
      (now just `'idle' | 'loading' | 'image' | 'error'`) and the
      corresponding HTML fallback block ("This document is a PDF —
      overlay markers aren't available for PDF files.").
    - `recomputeMarkers()`, the legend, and all CSS: untouched, no
      changes needed — already correct.

Why:
  - The Gemini vision call already renders a PDF's first page to an
    image and returns bounding boxes normalized against THAT rendered
    image (not the original PDF) — but nothing persisted that render,
    so the detail page had no image to draw markers on for a PDF and
    fell back to a "not available for PDF" message, even though the
    signals + boxes were already correctly detected and stored.

Bbox scaling math — verified, not just re-used blindly:
  The existing `recomputeMarkers()` formula is
  `scaleX = renderedWidth / 1000; scaleY = renderedHeight / 1000`, then
  `left = xmin * scaleX`, etc. This is correct BY CONSTRUCTION for both
  document kinds, not by coincidence: Gemini's [ymin,xmin,ymax,xmax]
  boxes are normalized 0-1000 against whatever image it was actually
  shown. For a PDF, that's the exact PNG saved by
  `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` (PyMuPDF rasterization is
  deterministic — same PDF + same 2x zoom matrix always produces
  byte-identical output, confirmed by re-rendering the same sample PDF
  twice in this session and comparing bytes). For an image upload,
  `prepare_gemini_image_payload()` reads the original file's raw bytes
  unchanged, and the new endpoint's fallback serves that same original
  file. Either way, the frontend now always displays the literal same
  image Gemini scored the boxes against, so `renderedWidth`/
  `renderedHeight` (the *displayed* pixel size, which changes on
  resize) correctly scale the fixed 0-1000 space regardless of the
  image's native resolution or the document's original PDF page size.
  This exact formula and its resize-responsiveness were also
  end-to-end verified against real rendered pixel positions with
  Playwright in an earlier session (scratchpad test_overlay.js,
  sub-pixel precision, confirmed markers move correctly on an actual
  viewport resize) — not repeated this session since neither the
  formula nor the CSS changed, only the image source feeding it.

Design note — redundant PDF renders, accepted tradeoff:
  For an invoice PDF, the first page now gets rendered up to twice per
  upload: once inside `gemini_extract_invoice_full()` for the Gemini
  call itself, and once more inside `save_rendered_authenticity_image()`
  for saving to disk (PO/GR uploads: same doubling, inside
  `_call_gemini_vision()` + the save call). Threading a single
  pre-rendered image through both call paths across two files was
  possible but would have meant changing several function signatures
  for a marginal gain — PyMuPDF rendering a single page is fast
  (~confirmed under 100ms against a real sample PDF earlier this
  session) and fully deterministic, so the simpler "just render twice"
  approach was chosen instead. Flagging this rather than silently
  picking it.

Storage note: reuses the existing uploads/ directory mechanism (already
gitignored wholesale, so uploads/authenticity/ needed no .gitignore
change) — no new persistence characteristics introduced beyond what
already applies to originally-uploaded files on Render.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on helpers/authenticity_check.py,
    routes/authenticity.py, app.py — compiles clean.
  - Imported app.py directly (real DB connection available in this
    session) and confirmed the new route registers:
    `/authenticity/<int:document_id>/image` alongside the existing
    `/authenticity/<int:document_id>` and `.../recheck` routes, with
    GET/HEAD/OPTIONS methods.
  - Called `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` directly (offline, no
    Gemini call — GEMINI_API_KEY unset) against a real sample PDF
    already in uploads/: confirmed a real PNG (correct signature bytes)
    was written to uploads/authenticity/999999_invoice.png, then
    cleaned up the test file.
  - `ng build --configuration=production` passes clean (771.30 kB
    initial bundle) after the frontend edits — no type errors from
    removing the 'pdf' state or changing fileUrl()'s return type.
  - Did not do a full authenticated HTTP round-trip against the new
    Flask route (would require either a real JWT against a live DB
    user or non-trivial auth mocking) — verified by direct code
    reading instead: the file-existence check, the VALID_DOC_TYPES
    guard before path construction, and the fallback logic were all
    read through line-by-line rather than executed live. A true
    end-to-end check (upload a PDF, open Authenticity Detail, confirm
    the image and markers actually render in a browser) can only
    happen after redeploying.

Setup/config needed:

     that already has a passed/warning check — if it predates this

     automatically on first upload.

2026-07-17 - Color-code overlay markers: green for present/detected
             signals, red for missing signals that still have a
             plausible location; legend updated to show both

What was changed:

BACKEND:
  - helpers/authenticity_check.py (`run_authenticity_check`): the
    signal_boxes retention filter used to require `is_present` (drop
    any box belonging to a signal marked false) before keeping it —
    that meant a missing signal could NEVER have a location even if
    Gemini identified one. Now keeps ANY well-formed
    [ymin,xmin,ymax,xmax] Gemini returns, for a present OR missing
    signal; presence/absence stays a separate concern (the has_company_
    chop/logo/name/signature booleans), independent of whether a box
    exists.
  - AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT (authenticity_check.py) and INVOICE_FULL_PROMPT
    (gemini_extractor.py) — both had an identical instruction: "Only
    include a key in signal_boxes for a signal that is true... If a
    signal is false, omit its key entirely." Softened to: if false, you
    MAY still include a box if there's a specific, plausible location
    (e.g. a blank signature line, an empty area where a chop/logo would
    typically appear) — otherwise omit it, same as before. Without this
    prompt change, the code-side fix above would rarely have anything
    to keep, since Gemini would keep obeying the old "always omit"
    instruction.
  - No DB/schema change — signal_boxes is unchanged JSONB, this only
    changes which keys end up in it.

FRONTEND (auditor-authenticity-detail component):
  - OverlayMarker interface: added `present: boolean`.
  - `recomputeMarkers()`: no longer filters markers by presence — draws
    a marker for every signal that HAS a box in signal_boxes (present
    or missing), tagging each with `present: !!this.check[key]`. Shape
    (rect vs circle) is unchanged, still from the existing SHAPE_MAP —
    only color/meaning changes between present and missing, not shape.
  - Template: marker div now gets a second class
    (`marker-present`/`marker-missing`) alongside the existing shape
    class, via an ngClass array.
  - Legend: replaced the old "✗ Missing (checklist only)" text-only
    entry with a proper red swatch, "Missing & located" — matching the
    new marker meaning (a checklist-only ✗ with no location still shows
    no swatch/marker at all, same as before; this legend is specifically
    about the two marker colors now visible on the image).
  - CSS: `.marker`'s hardcoded green border/background moved into a new
    `.marker-present` rule; added `.marker-missing` (red, #DC2626,
    matching the app's existing error-red). Same split for
    `.legend-swatch`: base sizing/shape stays, color moved into
    `.legend-green` (this class was referenced in the HTML from an
    earlier session but never actually defined — now it is) and the new
    `.legend-red`. Removed `.legend-text-red`, now unused after the
    legend HTML changed to use a swatch instead of colored ✗ text.

Why:
  - A missing signal (no chop, no signature, etc.) is often exactly
    what an auditor needs to SEE on the document — e.g. a blank
    signature line — not just read as a checklist ✗. Gemini can often
    point at that blank spot; the code was discarding that location
    unconditionally before this change.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on both changed backend files — compiles
    clean.
  - Offline (no Gemini/network call): isolated the exact retention
    filter logic and confirmed a box for a FALSE signal (has_signature)
    is now kept, while a signal with no box at all stays correctly
    absent. Also ran `run_authenticity_check()` directly with a fake
    precomputed_result containing a mix of present/missing-with-box/
    missing-without-box signals against a real sample PDF (confirmed
    the image-save side-effect still works); the DB write itself hit an
    expected FK violation (test used a non-existent document_id) —
    unrelated to the logic being tested, and the filter behavior was
    separately confirmed correct in isolation before the DB write was
    reached.
  - `ng build --configuration=production` passes clean (771.54 kB
    initial) after the TS/HTML/CSS changes.
  - Full browser-level verification with Playwright against the actual
    dev server (scratchpad, not committed): a hardcoded, fully mocked
    check response with 2 present signals (chop, name) and 1 MISSING
    signal that still has a signal_boxes entry (signature) — no real
    backend or Gemini call anywhere in the test (network intercepted
    with route.fulfill(), same technique as the original overlay
    verification from an earlier session). Confirmed: exactly 3 markers
    render (not 4 — has_company_logo correctly gets none, since it has
    no box); 2 are tagged marker-present with computed border-color
    rgb(16, 185, 129) (#10B981 green); 1 is tagged marker-missing with
    computed border-color rgb(220, 38, 38) (#DC2626 red); the legend
    shows exactly 2 items ("Present & located" / "Missing & located")
    with correctly colored swatches matching the marker colors.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy both the backend (prompt + filter change) and the
     frontend (marker/legend changes) together.
  2. Existing authenticity_checks rows keep whatever signal_boxes they
     already have (built under the old "omit if false" behavior, so

     to get Gemini to (optionally) supply a location for a missing
     signal under the new prompt.

2026-07-17 - GET /authenticity/<id>/image now renders on demand for
             older records that never got a saved image — no Gemini
             call, ever

What was changed:
  - routes/authenticity.py (`get_authenticity_image`): previously, a
    PDF with no cached rendered PNG (i.e. any record from before the
    image-saving feature existed, or one where the save silently
    failed) returned a 404 telling the auditor to "try Re-check" — the
    only way to get an image was to trigger a full Gemini re-analysis.
    Now, on a cache miss for a PDF, the endpoint calls the existing
    `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` helper (already used at upload
    time) directly from the route to render page 1 from the ORIGINAL
    uploaded file and cache it under the same deterministic path
    (`uploads/authenticity/<document_id>_<document_type>.png`) — so the
    very next request for the same document is an instant cache hit.
    Non-PDF (jpg/png) uploads are unaffected — still served directly,
    as before. If the original file itself no longer exists on disk,
    returns a clean 404 ("Original file unavailable for this
    document") instead of the old generic message.
  - No new function was added — this reuses
    `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` from helpers/authenticity_check.py
    exactly as-is (imported into routes/authenticity.py alongside the
    existing `run_authenticity_check`/`AUTHENTICITY_IMAGE_DIR`
    imports). That helper was already pure PyMuPDF rendering with zero
    Gemini/network calls (confirmed again this session, not just
    assumed — see Testing below); the only change is calling it from a
    second place (the image GET route, not just the upload/authenticity
    flow).
  - Added the requested log line, printed only on an actual successful
    on-demand render: "DEBUG authenticity image: rendered from original
    for doc=<id> (no Gemini)".
  - signal_boxes / circle overlays: NOT touched, as instructed — still
    served exactly as stored in the DB from the existing
    `GET /authenticity/<document_id>` endpoint. A record with no
    signal_boxes still shows the image + checklist with no circles;
    this change never calls Gemini to backfill them.

Why: older records (uploaded before the image-saving feature existed)
  had signal_boxes in the DB but no cached image to draw them on top
  of, so the detail page showed "Could not load the document file" for
  every pre-existing PDF record even though everything needed to
  display it (the original file) was still sitting in storage the
  whole time.

Confirmed this path never calls Gemini (per explicit request to verify,
not just assert):
  - Read `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` and its only dependency,
    `prepare_gemini_image_payload()` (gemini_extractor.py) — the entire
    call chain is `fitz.open()` / `get_pixmap()` / `tobytes()` (PyMuPDF,
    local rendering) or a plain `open(file_path, 'rb').read()` for
    non-PDFs, plus local file I/O to save the result. No `requests`,
    no `call_gemini_sdk`, no `genai.Client`, no network call of any
    kind anywhere in this chain.
  - Offline test (scratchpad, not committed): monkeypatched
    `gemini_extractor.requests.post/get`, `gemini_extractor._get_client`,
    and `authenticity_check.call_gemini_sdk` to all raise
    AssertionError if called — a real (non-empty) GEMINI_API_KEY was
    also set, so if anything in the render path had silently reached
    for the network, it would have hit one of these poisoned functions
    instead of quietly succeeding or quietly no-op'ing on a missing
    key. Then ran `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` against a real
    sample PDF from uploads/ for a fake document_id with no pre-existing
    cached image: it rendered and cached a real PNG (confirmed PNG
    signature bytes) with none of the poisoned functions ever firing —
    proof, not assumption, that this path makes zero Gemini/network
    calls.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on routes/authenticity.py,
    helpers/authenticity_check.py — compiles clean.
  - See the Gemini-call verification above (same test also exercises
    the actual render+cache+serve logic end to end).

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend for this to take effect.
  2. After redeploying, open Authenticity Detail for any older PDF
     record that previously showed "Could not load the document file"
     — it should now render the image on the first load (a little
     slower, since it's rendering) and be instant on every load after
     that (cached). Circles only appear if that record already has
     signal_boxes stored; this change does not add or refresh boxes for
     old records — only Re-check does that (and only Re-check ever
     calls Gemini).

2026-07-17 - Root cause of persistent "Could not load the document file":
             Render's free-tier disk is EPHEMERAL. Store uploaded file
             bytes in Postgres instead of relying on local disk.

Root cause: Render's free tier filesystem is wiped on every redeploy/
  restart. The previous fixes in this file (on-demand PDF rendering,
  etc.) all assumed the original uploaded file was still sitting at its
  file_path on disk — true only until the next restart. That's why even
  BRAND NEW uploads eventually showed "Could not load the document
  file": the disk copy they were rendered from was gone as soon as the
  dyno restarted, and there was nothing left to render from.

What was changed:

1. New migration (auditlens-backend/migrations/2026-07-17_add_file_bytes.sql),
   applied to documents, purchase_orders, AND goods_receipts (not just
   documents — PO/GR each have their own file_path/file_bytes today,
   same as the existing per-table file_path pattern; a single side
   table keyed by document_id alone couldn't have distinguished
   multiple PO/GR rows per document_id, which this app already
   supports):
     ALTER TABLE <table> ADD COLUMN file_bytes BYTEA, ADD COLUMN file_mime VARCHAR(100);
   This ALSO runs automatically at app startup
   (app.py's new `_ensure_file_bytes_columns()`), matching this
   session's established pattern for 3 of the 4 prior migrations (no
   migration runner exists in this repo, so Render never gets a .sql
   file run against it unless startup does it itself) — confirmed
   working this session: booting the app actually added the columns
   to the connected database. The .sql file is kept for local dev /
   documentation parity with the rest of migrations/, same dual
   pattern as the others.

2. Upload endpoints (routes/documents.py — upload_document/
   upload_purchase_order/upload_goods_receipt): after saving to local
   disk (still done, still needed for the OCR/Gemini calls later in
   the SAME request), the file is also read back into bytes and stored
   in the new file_bytes/file_mime columns. A file over
   Config.MAX_DB_FILE_BYTES (new config.py constant, 8MB — invoices/
   POs/GRs are small scanned documents) still uploads and processes
   completely normally; it just isn't persisted to the DB, so it won't
   survive a restart. Logged when this happens.

3. File-serving endpoints (routes/documents.py's
   serve_document_file/serve_po_file/serve_gr_file, via a rewritten
   `_send_document_file`) and the authenticity image/recheck endpoints
   (routes/authenticity.py) now read the original file from Postgres
   (file_bytes) FIRST — that's the durable source going forward — and
   only fall back to the local disk file_path if bytes weren't stored
   (the size-guard case, or a pre-existing record) AND the disk file
   still happens to exist in the current process. This degrades
   gracefully for the size-guard case without weakening the DB as the
   primary source of truth.

4. `helpers/gemini_extractor.py`'s `prepare_gemini_image_payload()` and
   `gemini_extract_invoice_full()`, and `helpers/authenticity_check.py`'s
   `_call_gemini_vision()`/`save_rendered_authenticity_image()`/
   `run_authenticity_check()` all changed from taking a file_path to
   taking (file_bytes, file_name) — PDFs are now opened directly from
   in-memory bytes via `fitz.open(stream=file_bytes, filetype='pdf')`
   (verified this works identically to opening from a path) instead of
   `fitz.open(file_path)`, so the entire rendering chain has zero
   dependency on the local filesystem. Every call site across
   routes/documents.py (3 upload endpoints) and routes/authenticity.py
   (image + recheck endpoints) updated accordingly.

5. The local PNG cache in helpers/authenticity_check.py
   (AUTHENTICITY_IMAGE_DIR, from two entries ago) is UNCHANGED — it's
   still on Render's ephemeral disk, but that's now fine, exactly as
   you noted: it's just a same-process speedup, always rebuildable from
   the DB-stored bytes in milliseconds after a restart. Did NOT persist
   rendered image bytes to a DB column (your point 3, marked optional)
   — re-rendering from the now-always-available DB bytes is fast
   (confirmed ~sub-100ms per an earlier session's benchmark) and this
   keeps the change smaller; flagging this as a deliberate scope
   decision rather than silently skipping it.

6. Fixed a knock-on issue this change would otherwise have caused:
   several existing endpoints do `SELECT po.*`/`SELECT gr.*`/
   `SELECT d.*, ef.*`/`SELECT *` and jsonify the result directly (PO
   list, GR list, document list, document detail, supporting
   documents). Once file_bytes existed, these would have either thrown
   (Flask's JSON encoder can't serialize bytes/memoryview) or leaked
   entire file contents into list responses. Added `row.pop('file_bytes',
   None)` at each of these 5 call sites in routes/documents.py, right
   next to their existing per-row post-processing loop. Checked every
   other `SELECT *`-style query against these 3 tables across the rest
   of the backend (routes/matching.py, routes/reviews.py) — those only
   ever read specific fields out of the row (never jsonify the whole
   dict), so they were already safe and left untouched.

Why: this closes the loop the last several entries were working
  around — every previous fix (on-demand PDF rendering, the local PNG
  cache, etc.) was still ultimately reading from a file_path on disk,
  which Render's free tier doesn't guarantee exists past the current
  process's lifetime. Storing the actual bytes in Postgres removes
  that assumption entirely.

Existing records: as you noted, records uploaded before this change
  have no file_bytes stored and their disk files are already gone —
  they'll still show "Original file unavailable for this document".
  Only NEW uploads after this deploy get bytes persisted and survive
  future restarts.

Testing (all against the actual connected database this session has
access to — real INSERTs were wrapped in a transaction and rolled back,
never committed, so nothing in the real DB was permanently changed):
  - `python -m py_compile` on every changed file — compiles clean.
  - Booted the app for real: `_ensure_file_bytes_columns()` ran and
    added the columns; confirmed via `information_schema.columns` that
    file_bytes (bytea) and file_mime (character varying) now exist on
    all three tables.
  - Inserted a real test `documents` row with a real sample PDF's bytes
    (existing user_id, read-only lookup), read it back, confirmed the
    round-tripped bytes are byte-for-byte identical to the original —
    then ROLLED BACK the transaction (never committed).
  - Ran `_lookup_file_info()` (routes/authenticity.py) against a second
    rolled-back test row whose file_path pointed at a file that does
    NOT exist on disk — it still returned the correct bytes, sourced
    from the database, proving the fix directly against the exact
    failure mode being fixed (disk file gone, DB bytes intact).
  - Confirmed `fitz.open(stream=..., filetype='pdf')` renders
    identically to `fitz.open(file_path)` against a real sample PDF.
  - Re-ran the same network/Gemini-call poisoning test from two entries
    ago (monkeypatched requests.post/get, _get_client, and
    call_gemini_sdk to raise if touched, real-looking API key set) —
    confirmed `prepare_gemini_image_payload()` and
    `save_rendered_authenticity_image()` both work correctly from pure
    bytes with zero Gemini/network calls.
  - Directly tested the rewritten `_send_document_file()` inside a
    Flask request context (no live HTTP round-trip, but exercises the
    real function and a real send_file response): confirmed all 3
    branches — DB bytes present (served correctly, byte-for-byte,
    correct mimetype), no DB bytes but disk file still exists
    (fallback correctly serves from disk), neither present (clean 404).
  - Checked every remaining `SELECT *`/`.* ` query against documents/
    purchase_orders/goods_receipts across the whole backend (not just
    documents.py) to confirm nothing else could leak file_bytes into a
    JSON response.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend — the migration runs automatically at
     startup (no manual SQL needed, confirmed this session), but the
     code changes still require a deploy to take effect.
  2. Upload a NEW test document after redeploying, then trigger a
     redeploy/restart (or just wait for Render's next natural restart)
     and confirm that same document's file and authenticity image still
     load — that's the actual test of what this fixes. Records uploaded
     before this deploy will still show unavailable, as expected.

2026-07-17 - Redesign the Field Comparison table (Invoice vs PO vs GR):
             PO Ref / Item / Quantity as real 3-way comparisons, Date
             row removed, Quantity mismatches flagged prominently

What was changed:

BACKEND — new regex-extracted fields, no Gemini call:
  - helpers/ocr_helper.py: `extract_fields()` (invoice), `extract_po_
    fields()`, `extract_gr_fields()` each gained new fields:
    - `po_reference` (invoice + GR only — the PO number each document
      references, e.g. an OCR'd "PO No: PO-2026-0042" line; the PO's
      own po_number is already its anchor identity, so it doesn't need
      a separate po_reference).
    - `item_description` (all three) — best-effort: looks for a
      "Description"/"Particulars"/"Item" label, either an inline value
      or the next line.
    - `quantity` (all three) — best-effort: "Qty"/"Quantity" label
      followed by a number. Same single-value simplification this app
      already uses for total_amount (not itemized line-by-line).
    All regex-only, verified offline against realistic synthetic OCR
    text before wiring into the DB — see Testing below.
  - New migration (migrations/2026-07-17_add_3way_comparison_fields.sql),
    applied to extracted_fields/purchase_orders/goods_receipts, also
    auto-applied at startup (app.py's new
    `_ensure_3way_comparison_columns()`, matching this session's
    established pattern — no migration runner in this repo) — confirmed
    working by booting the app against the connected DB and checking
    information_schema.
  - routes/documents.py: all three upload endpoints now persist the new
    fields in their INSERT statements (previously extracted but
    silently discarded).
  - routes/auditor.py `_build_comparison()`:
    - SELECTs now include the new columns for all three document types.
    - New helpers `_normalize_ref()` (PO number: uppercase, strip
      whitespace), `_normalize_text()` (item description: lowercase,
      collapse whitespace), `_three_way_match()` (true if every present
      value is identical, None if fewer than 2 present to compare),
      `_quantities_match()` (same, numeric with 0.01 tolerance).
    - `po_reference_match`: now a REAL comparison across invoice.
      po_reference / po.po_no / gr.po_reference — previously hardcoded
      to `None` because these fields didn't exist before this change.
    - New `item_match`, `quantity_match` in `match_result`.
    - `quantity_match` is included in the `overall_status`/FAIL
      computation (alongside vendor_match/amount_match/date_order_
      valid) and in `_classify_exception()` (new "Quantity Mismatch"
      exception, e.g. "PO 100.0 vs GR 90.0 vs Invoice 100.0") — a
      deliberate scope decision, see Why below. `po_reference_match`/
      `item_match` are NOT wired into overall_status/exceptions —
      kept display-only in the table, since best-effort OCR text/PO-
      number extraction is more prone to false mismatches than the
      already-mature vendor/amount/date checks, and wiring them into
      the system that drives the approve/exception workflow risked
      false FAILs from imperfect regex extraction.
    - `date_order_valid` computation is UNCHANGED and still feeds
      `overall_status` — only the Field Comparison table's Date ROW is
      removed (see frontend below), not the underlying chronological
      sanity check, which remains a useful signal independent of
      whether it's displayed as a row.

FRONTEND (auditor-record-detail component) — new row order:
  1. Vendor / Supplier (label text updated; matching logic UNCHANGED —
     still the existing pairwise Invoice→PO / PO→GR client-side pills,
     left alone since it already worked correctly).
  2. PO Ref — REDESIGNED from a raw-value-only placeholder (server used
     to hardcode po_reference_match to null) to a real 3-way match: one
     Match/Mismatch pill for the whole row (from match_result.po_
     reference_match), shown once next to the field label — not
     per-cell pairwise pills, since this is a genuine 3-way comparison,
     not two pairwise ones. Same new pattern for:
  3. Item / Description (new row).
  4. Quantity (new row) — the row itself, plus a NEW `row-quantity-
     alert` CSS class (thicker red border, stronger background, bold
     red numbers) applied ONLY when quantity_match is false, layered on
     top of the standard row-mismatch highlight, so this specific
     exception can't be missed scanning the table.
  5. Amount — UNCHANGED logic (Invoice-vs-PO pairwise pill, "No amount
     on GR" for GR — GR carries no monetary total by design), just
     repositioned after Quantity per the request.
  6. Doc No — UNCHANGED, still identification-only with no match pill.
     Deliberately NOT given a Match/Mismatch indicator: doc numbers are
     supposed to differ across Invoice/PO/GR (each document has its own
     number), so a blanket "compare the three values" treatment here
     would always show a nonsensical "Mismatch" for something that
     isn't actually wrong — kept consistent with how this row already
     behaved (no pill) before this change.
  - Removed: the Date row entirely, per the request (dates naturally
    differ between PO/GR/Invoice, so a "should match" framing was
    misleading — the old row didn't even compute a real comparison, it
    showed a hardcoded "< Before" pill regardless of actual date order).
  - New TS helpers: `rowMatchClass/rowMatchPillClass/rowMatchIcon/
    rowMatchText` (the new row-level 3-way indicator, reading directly
    from match_result — simpler than replicating 3-way comparison logic
    in TypeScript when the server already computed it) and
    `formatQuantity()`.

Why:
  - Only fields that genuinely exist in and should match across all
    three document types belong in a "should these agree" comparison —
    dates are expected to differ (PO date < GR date < Invoice date is
    the correct pattern, not equality), so showing them as a mismatch-
    style row was actively misleading.
  - Quantity (PO ordered vs GR received vs Invoice billed) is the
    single most important 3-way audit signal — a shortfall or overbill
    is exactly the kind of thing this whole comparison exists to catch,
    which is why it's the one new field wired into the overall FAIL/
    Exceptions system rather than staying table-only: a banner still
    reading "PASS" while a real quantity shortage sits in the table
    would fail to "flag it clearly" in any way an auditor scanning
    banners across many records would actually notice.

Testing:
  - `python -m py_compile` on every changed backend file — compiles
    clean.
  - Offline (no Gemini/DB call): ran the three regex extractors
    directly against realistic synthetic OCR text for an invoice/PO/GR
    sharing the same PO-2026-0042 reference and Industrial Widget
    Assembly item, with the GR intentionally receiving 90 instead of
    100 — confirmed po_reference/item_description/quantity all extract
    correctly per document type, AND confirmed the pre-existing fields
    (total_amount, tax_amount, invoice_number, po_number) still extract
    correctly (no regression from inserting the new extraction blocks
    into the same per-line loops).
  - Offline (mocked psycopg2 cursor, no real DB call): ran the real
    `_build_comparison()` function directly against three scenarios —
    (1) full 3-way match with a quantity mismatch: confirmed vendor/
    amount/po_reference/item all match True, quantity_match is False,
    and overall_status is FAIL; (2) PO missing (invoice+GR only):
    confirmed po_reference_match still correctly compares the two
    present values; (3) invoice-only (nothing else present): confirmed
    every 3-way field correctly returns None (not a false match or
    false mismatch) when fewer than 2 values exist to compare. Also
    directly called `_classify_exception()` on the mismatch scenario
    and confirmed it produces a "Quantity Mismatch" exception with the
    exact "PO 100.0 vs GR 90.0 vs Invoice 100.0" detail text.
  - `ng build --configuration=production` passes clean (775.59 kB
    initial) — no type errors from the new TS helpers or template
    changes.
  - Full browser-level verification with Playwright against the live
    dev server (scratchpad, not committed): a hardcoded, fully mocked
    /auditor/record/1/comparison response with the exact "ordered 100 /
    received 90 / billed 100" scenario — no real backend call anywhere
    (network intercepted with route.fulfill()). Confirmed: exactly 6
    rows in the exact order Vendor/Supplier → PO Ref → Item/Description
    → Quantity → Amount → Doc No (no Date row); PO Ref and Item both
    show a green Match pill with correct values; the Quantity row has
    BOTH row-mismatch AND row-quantity-alert CSS classes, a red
    pill-differ "⚠ Mismatch" pill, and all three values (100/100/90)
    visible; the Amount row's existing "No amount on GR" handling is
    unchanged; the overall banner correctly reads "❌ Mismatch
    Detected" (confirming quantity_match's effect on overall_status
    end-to-end, not just in isolation). Screenshot taken and visually
    reviewed — the quantity row is unmistakably prominent against the
    rest of the table.

Note (not fixed, out of scope): while building the offline regex test,
noticed `extract_gr_fields()`'s gr_number pattern doesn't match a GR
labeled "GRN No:" (a common Malaysian abbreviation) — it matches "GR
No:"/"Goods Receipt No:" but "GRN" partially matches "GR" then fails on
the "N" before "No:". Pre-existing, unrelated to this change, flagging
rather than silently fixing since it wasn't part of the request.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend AND frontend together — they depend on
     each other for this feature (new API fields + new table markup).
  2. The migration runs automatically at startup, same as recent prior
     entries — no manual SQL needed, confirmed this session.
  3. Existing invoice/PO/GR records uploaded before this deploy have no
     po_reference/item_description/quantity stored (those columns will
     be NULL) — their Field Comparison table will show "-" for those
     rows and match indicators will show "N/A" (fewer than 2 values
     present). Only new uploads after this deploy populate the new
     fields. There's no bulk re-extraction from existing raw_ocr_text in
     this change; let me know if you'd like that as a follow-up.

2026-07-17 - Fix 3 bugs in the new comparison fields: po_reference false
             mismatch (prefix inconsistency), item_description grabbing
             a table column header instead of the real item, quantity
             extracting nothing for tabular invoices/POs/GRs

Root cause of BUG 2 & 3: the previous item_description/quantity regexes
only handled a "Description: X" / "Qty: N" LABEL:VALUE layout. This
project's actual invoices/POs/GRs use a TABLE instead — a header row
("No | Description | Qty | Unit Price (RM) | Amount (RM)", which Google
Vision OCR often emits as one label per line) followed by data rows like
"1  Aluminium Bracket A100  120  8.00  960.00". Neither table shape was
handled before.

What was changed:

BUG 1 — po_reference false mismatch (routes/auditor.py `_normalize_ref`):
  - Previously only uppercased and stripped whitespace. Now also strips
    a leading "PO-"/"PO" prefix, so "PO-2026-0087" (however the source
    document phrases its "PO No:" line) and "2026-0087" (a source that
    happens to extract without the prefix) normalize to the identical
    "2026-0087" and compare equal, per the explicit fix given in the
    request.

BUG 2 & 3 — item_description/quantity (helpers/ocr_helper.py, all
three of extract_fields/extract_po_fields/extract_gr_fields):
  - New `LINE_ITEM_ROW_RE`: matches a tabular data row directly —
    leading row number (discarded), description, a whole-number qty,
    then two decimal amounts (unit price, total) through end of line.
    Tried FIRST, before any label-based fallback, and pulls
    item_description AND quantity from the SAME matched row so they're
    always internally consistent (never description from one row,
    qty from a different one).
  - New `HEADER_WORD_RE`: a denylist of table-header words (No,
    Description, Qty, Unit Price (RM), Amount (RM), Total (RM), etc.).
    This is the actual BUG 2 fix — when OCR emits each column header on
    its own line ("Description" then, on the very next line, "Qty"),
    the OLD label-based fallback saw the bare "Description" line, found
    no inline value, and grabbed the NEXT line ("Qty") as if it were
    the description. The label-based fallback is now guarded by this
    denylist on both the inline value and the next-line value, so it
    can never mistake the next column header for real data. The
    label-based patterns themselves are UNCHANGED and kept as a
    fallback for simpler non-tabular invoices (a genuine "Description:
    Widget XYZ" / "Qty: 100" layout) — verified this still works.

Why: these are exactly the three bugs reported against this project's
  actual invoice/PO/GR layout, reproduced and fixed against realistic
  synthetic OCR text matching that exact layout before considering
  either bug closed.

Testing (all offline, no Gemini/network/DB call):
  - `python -m py_compile` on both changed files — compiles clean.
  - Verified `_normalize_ref()` treats 'PO-2026-0087', '2026-0087',
    'PO 2026-0087', and 'po-2026-0087' as identical after normalization.
  - Built realistic synthetic OCR text for the exact table layout
    described (header lines one-per-line, then a
    "1  Aluminium Bracket A100  <qty>  8.00  <amount>" data row) for
    four scenarios: three MATCH sets (qty 120, 200, and 300, each
    internally consistent across invoice/PO/GR, with the invoice/PO
    using "PO-2026-0087" and the GR deliberately using the un-prefixed
    "2026-0087" to specifically re-exercise BUG 1) and one MISMATCH set
    (PO/Invoice qty=100, GR qty=90). For every scenario, confirmed:
    item_description = 'Aluminium Bracket A100' (not 'Qty' or any other
    header word) for all three document types; quantity = the correct
    integer per document; po_reference normalizes equal across all
    three via `_normalize_ref`/`_three_way_match` for the match sets;
    `_quantities_match()` correctly returns False for the 100/100/90
    mismatch set. Also re-ran the existing total_amount/tax_amount
    regression suite (unaffected, still passes) and a simple
    "Description:"/"Qty:" label-style (non-tabular) invoice to confirm
    the fallback path used by simpler documents still works correctly
    after adding the table-row pattern and the header-word guard.
  - Caught and fixed a bug in my OWN test script along the way (an
    unformatted integer amount that failed to match the "must have a
    decimal point" requirement in LINE_ITEM_ROW_RE) — worth noting
    since it's a reminder that the regex's amount/price format
    requirement is strict by design (distinguishing a whole-number qty
    from decimal prices, per the request), not a bug in the extractor.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend.
  2. Re-upload (or Re-check, where applicable) a sample invoice/PO/GR
     set from your test data to confirm item_description/quantity now
     extract correctly against your real documents, not just the
     synthetic text used in this session's offline testing — synthetic
     text can't perfectly replicate whatever line-breaking Google
     Vision OCR actually produces for your specific PDFs' table layout.

2026-07-17 - Rewrite line-item extraction for the REAL Google Vision
             table structure: every cell on its own line, not one
             space-separated row per item

Root cause: the previous fix (LINE_ITEM_ROW_RE, one prior entry) assumed
  a data row looked like "1  Aluminium Bracket A100  120  8.00  960.00"
  all on one line. Real Google Vision output for this app's tables looks
  nothing like that — it emits ONE CELL PER LINE:
    No / Description / Qty / Unit Price (RM) / Amount (RM) / 1 /
    Aluminium Bracket A 100 / 120 / 8.00 / 960.00 / 2 / ...
  That old regex could never match this, so item_description fell
  through to the label-based fallback (which grabbed "Qty" — the next
  column header — since "Description" appeared as a bare header line
  with nothing after it) and quantity found nothing at all.

What was changed (helpers/ocr_helper.py):
  - New `_extract_first_line_item(lines)`: the primary method now.
    Locates the table by finding 4 CONSECUTIVE standalone lines matching
    "Description" / "Qty" / "Unit Price (RM)" / "Amount (RM)"
    (`_TABLE_HEADER_LINE_RES`), then walks forward from there: skips a
    leading row-number line ("1"), takes the next non-header, non-
    numeric line as the description, then continues scanning forward
    for the first bare INTEGER line (no decimal point) as the quantity
    — skipping over the decimal unit-price/amount lines in between, per
    the exact algorithm given in the request. Returns (None, None)
    rather than guessing if the structure doesn't hold up (no header
    block found, or a number appears where the description should be).
  - Safety net added after reproducing an edge case myself while
    testing: if the "description" candidate line itself contains a
    decimal number (e.g. "8.00"), it's actually an unsplit combined row
    (this document's cells landed on one line after all, not one-per-
    line), not a clean single cell — bails out to (None, None) instead
    of swallowing the whole row as "the description", so the existing
    LINE_ITEM_ROW_RE / label-based fallbacks (both kept, unchanged) get
    a chance to parse it correctly instead.
  - Wired into all three of extract_fields/extract_po_fields/
    extract_gr_fields: `_extract_first_line_item()` now runs ONCE over
    the whole line list, before each function's main per-line loop
    (which still runs afterward and only fills in item_description/
    quantity via LINE_ITEM_ROW_RE or the label-based fallback if the
    new primary method didn't find anything) — necessary because,
    unlike every other field in this file, locating a 4-line header
    block requires looking across multiple lines at once, which doesn't
    fit the existing single-line-at-a-time loop.
  - HEADER_WORD_RE (from the prior entry) is reused as-is as the
    denylist for what a description/quantity value is never allowed to
    be — no changes needed there, it already covered the right words.

Testing (all offline, no Gemini/network/DB call):
  - `python -m py_compile` — compiles clean.
  - Built OCR text with the EXACT line-by-line structure given in the
    request (every header and every cell on its own line) for: a MATCH
    set (qty=120, identical across invoice/PO/GR, two line items per
    document to confirm only the FIRST is taken) and a MISMATCH set
    (PO/Invoice qty=100, GR qty=90). Confirmed for every document type:
    item_description = "Aluminium Bracket A 100" exactly (never "Qty"
    or any other header word), quantity is the correct integer, and the
    mismatch set correctly fails `_quantities_match()`.
  - Also called `_extract_first_line_item()` directly against the
    LITERAL line list pasted verbatim in the request (not a
    reconstruction) — confirmed it returns exactly
    ("Aluminium Bracket A 100", 120.0).
  - While building this test, hit the edge case above for real (my own
    earlier "one-line-row" test script's synthetic text has a data row
    all on one line, right after per-line headers) — this is what led
    to adding the decimal-number safety net, then re-verified that
    script's scenarios all pass again with the fallback taking over
    correctly, rather than just deleting the now-inconvenient test.
  - Re-ran the total_amount/tax_amount regression suite and the simple
    non-tabular "Description:"/"Qty:" label-style test — both still
    pass, confirming no regression to the existing fields or the
    simpler fallback path.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend.
  2. Re-upload (or Re-check) a real invoice/PO/GR set to confirm against
     actual Google Vision output — this fix was built directly against
     the real OCR structure you provided this time, so confidence is
     higher than the previous entry, but your real PDFs are still the
     authoritative test.

2026-07-17 - Fix a "perfect match" record wrongly showing "Mismatch
             Detected": date_order_valid, an invisible check no longer
             shown in the table, could flip the whole banner alone

Investigated per the request: your hypothesis (GR's missing amount
  causing a false mismatch) does NOT hold, verified by code review —
  amount_match only ever compares Invoice vs PO, it never even looks at
  GR's amount; and both `_amounts_equal()` and `_quantities_match()`
  already correctly return None ("not applicable") rather than False
  whenever fewer than 2 real values exist to compare — confirmed with a
  new offline test where GR's quantity is entirely missing (None) and
  quantity_match still correctly comes out True from the two values
  that ARE present (invoice + PO). None of the checks visible in the
  Field Comparison table were the bug.

Root cause (found by reconstructing the record's field values in a
  mocked comparison and printing the per-check breakdown, i.e. doing
  exactly what the request asked for): `date_order_valid` — PO date <=
  GR date <= Invoice date — was still one of the checks feeding
  `overall_status`, even though the Field Comparison table stopped
  showing a Date row two entries ago (dates naturally differ between
  PO/GR/Invoice, so a "should match" row was misleading — but the
  underlying order check was deliberately left wired into the banner
  logic at the time, reasoned then as "still a useful signal"). That
  reasoning was wrong in practice: an invisible check silently failing
  the whole banner, with no row anywhere for the auditor to see why, is
  indistinguishable from a bug. For INV-2026-0087, every check actually
  shown in the table (vendor/PO Ref/item/quantity/amount) was a real,
  correct Match — only the invisible date-order check was False,
  flipping the banner to "Mismatch Detected" for a record with nothing
  wrong that an auditor could find by reading the table.

What was changed (routes/auditor.py `_build_comparison()`):
  - `checks` (the list that drives `overall_status`) no longer includes
    `date_order_valid` — now `[vendor_match, amount_match,
    quantity_match]` only, i.e. exactly the checks with a visible row in
    the Field Comparison table. `date_order_valid` is still computed,
    still returned in `match_result`, and still adds supplementary
    detail text in `_classify_exception()` when another check has
    already triggered a FAIL — it just can no longer single-handedly
    fail a record with nothing else wrong.
  - Added the requested per-check debug log, printed on every call:
    "DEBUG comparison doc=<id>: vendor_match=... amount_match=...
    po_reference_match=... item_match=... quantity_match=...
    date_order_valid=... -> overall_status=...". This is now the first
    thing to check in Render's logs any time overall_status looks wrong
    for a record — every `None` was correctly skipped as not-applicable
    (a missing/absent value on one side), not a mismatch; only an
    explicit `False` is a genuine disagreement.

Testing (all offline, mocked cursor, no DB/Gemini/network call — this
session's local DB turned out to be empty/disconnected from the
production record in the screenshot, so the bug was reproduced by
reconstructing the record's field values directly rather than querying
it):
  - Reproduced the exact reported bug: a mocked record with
    vendor_match/amount_match/po_reference_match/item_match/
    quantity_match all True, but a GR receipt_date (17 Jul) after the
    invoice_date (14 Jul) — before this fix, that combination gave
    `overall_status='FAIL'` (matching the screenshot); after the fix,
    the same input now correctly gives `overall_status='PASS'`.
  - Re-verified the real quantity-mismatch scenario (PO/Invoice=100,
    GR=90) still correctly gives `overall_status='FAIL'`.
  - New test: GR quantity entirely missing (None) — confirmed
    quantity_match is True (from the invoice/PO values that ARE
    present, not skipped-as-mismatch) and overall_status is PASS,
    directly closing out the original hypothesis.
  - Re-ran the existing `_build_comparison()` test suite from two
    entries ago (PO-missing scenario, invoice-only scenario) — both
    still pass unchanged.
  - `python -m py_compile` — compiles clean.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend.
  2. Re-open INV-2026-0087 (or any other record currently showing an
     unexplained "Mismatch Detected" with every table row green) after
     redeploying — it should now correctly show PASS. Check the new
     "DEBUG comparison doc=..." log line if any record's banner still
     looks wrong, to see exactly which check is False.

2026-07-18 - Gemini is now the PRIMARY field extractor for invoice/PO/GR
             (not just invoice), with real-document label tolerance and
             multi-currency total handling; currency stored + shown
             next to every amount so USD is never silently read as RM

Context: this app's clean standard PDFs already worked, but real Coilcraft/
EMITS-style documents use non-standard labels regex can't handle ("INVOICE:
IX107587" instead of "Invoice No", "Doc No. PD6011823" instead of "GR No")
and multi-currency totals (an original US$ total alongside a converted RM
total via an exchange rate) that a naive "take the largest total" regex
would get backwards — returning the bigger converted RM number instead of
the real US$ transaction amount.

What was changed:

BACKEND — Gemini as PRIMARY extractor for PO/GR too (helpers/gemini_
extractor.py, routes/documents.py):
  - PO/GR previously made TWO Gemini calls per upload: a TEXT-based field-
    extraction call inside extract_po_fields()/extract_gr_fields() (via the
    old gemini_extract_po()/gemini_extract_gr(), which sent OCR text, not
    the image) plus a SEPARATE vision call for authenticity. Only invoice
    used the single merged vision call pattern. Replaced PO/GR's old
    TEXT_PROMPT-based functions with `PO_FULL_PROMPT`/`GR_FULL_PROMPT` +
    `gemini_extract_po_full()`/`gemini_extract_gr_full()`, mirroring
    `gemini_extract_invoice_full()` exactly: ONE vision call returns fields
    AND authenticity signals together. `upload_purchase_order()`/
    `upload_goods_receipt()` in routes/documents.py now call these once and
    pass `precomputed_result=gemini_result, skip_gemini=not gemini_result`
    into `run_authenticity_check()` (same pattern already used for
    invoice), so a PO/GR upload now spends exactly one Gemini call, same as
    invoice — closing the "still ONE Gemini call per document upload"
    requirement, which wasn't actually true for PO/GR before this change.
  - Removed the now-dead `PO_PROMPT`, `GR_PROMPT`, `_call_gemini()`,
    `gemini_extract_po()`, `gemini_extract_gr()`.
  - Factored the identical ~40-line "PART 2: AUTHENTICITY SIGNALS" prompt
    text and JSON schema tail (previously only in the invoice prompt) into
    shared `AUTHENTICITY_SIGNALS_BLOCK`/`AUTHENTICITY_JSON_TAIL` constants,
    reused by all three of invoice/PO/GR prompts instead of duplicating it
    three times.
  - New shared `DOCUMENT_NUMBER_NOTE` (all 3 prompts): explicitly instructs
    Gemini to treat a bare label immediately followed by a value (e.g.
    "INVOICE:  IX107587", "Doc No.  PD6011823") as valid, and to ignore
    similar-looking nearby noise (Co.Reg.No, Tel, Fax, page numbers,
    account codes) that is never the actual document number.
  - New shared `CURRENCY_NOTE` (all 3 prompts): explicitly instructs Gemini
    to detect the currency of the primary total, and — when a document
    shows both an original-currency total and an exchange-rate-converted
    local total (the exact "TOTAL (US$) 8,020.00" + "EXCHANGE RATE=1.2670
    ... TOTAL= 10,161.34 (RM)" pattern from the request, and the PO's
    "Total Payable Incl. Tax (RM) 32,946.16" alongside "USD 8,020") —
    return the ORIGINAL-currency amount as total_amount and the ORIGINAL
    currency in the new `currency` field, never the converted value.
  - Invoice prompt's JSON schema gained `po_reference`, `item_description`,
    `quantity` (it already had a `currency` key, but no instructions on how
    to determine it — now it does). `upload_document()`'s Gemini-override
    loop extended from 5 keys to include these plus `currency` — previously
    Gemini never actually overrode these fields even though the DB columns
    existed, an oversight from the prior session's 3-way comparison work.
  - `extracted_fields` (invoice) gained a `currency` column (purchase_
    orders/goods_receipts already had one) — new migrations/2026-07-18_
    add_invoice_currency.sql + app.py's `_ensure_invoice_currency_column()`
    (same auto-migration-at-startup pattern as every other _ensure_
    function, since this repo has no migration runner).

BACKEND — regex FALLBACK strengthened to match (helpers/ocr_helper.py):
  Gemini is primary now, but the regex fallback still needs to do a
  reasonable job when Gemini is unavailable, and this is also the only
  part of this change testable fully offline.
  - `extract_fields()` (invoice): added a bare "INVOICE:" label pattern
    (`\binvoice\s*:\s*(...)`, requires the colon right after the word so
    "Invoice No:"/"Invoice Date:" never match it) alongside the existing
    "Invoice No."-style patterns.
  - `extract_gr_fields()`: reordered the gr_number label alternation so
    `doc\.?` is tried before the shorter `gr`/`do` — otherwise "do" would
    partial-match inside "Doc No." and capture only the trailing "c",
    silently failing to extract the number at all (regex alternation
    takes the first alternative that lets the match succeed, not the
    longest, so order matters here).
  - `extract_po_fields()`: same "doc" fallback added for po_number.
  - `extract_fields()`/`extract_po_fields()`: new currency-tagged total
    handling — a `"total (US$)"`/`"total (USD)"`-style match (or a bare
    "USD 8,020" for PO) is collected into a separate `usd_total_candidates`
    list and takes unconditional priority over the existing MYR/RM
    candidates once the line loop finishes; a line containing "exchange
    rate" is also excluded from ALL total candidates as an extra guard.
    Both functions now set `fields['currency']` ('USD' when a USD total
    won, 'MYR' otherwise) instead of invoice's fields dict never having a
    currency key at all before this change.
  - Bug found and fixed while testing the above: `extract_po_fields()`'s
    primary po_number regex (`p\.?o\.?\s*(?:no\.?|number|#)?\s*[:\-]?\s*
    (...)`) would self-match on a PO number that itself starts with "PO"
    (the common "PONNNNNNN" Malaysian SME format, e.g. "PO3005713") even
    when the actual label on that line was "Doc No." — "PO" got treated as
    the label and only "3005713" got captured, silently dropping the "PO"
    prefix. Fixed by requiring SOME real separation (a "No"/"Number"/"#"
    word, a colon/dash, or at least one space) between the label match and
    the captured value.

BACKEND — currency-aware comparison (routes/auditor.py `_build_comparison`):
  - Invoice/PO SELECTs now include `currency`, returned on both the
    `invoice` and `po` dicts.
  - `amount_match`: if both invoice and PO have a known currency and they
    DIFFER (e.g. invoice in USD, PO in RM), the check now returns `None`
    ("not applicable") instead of doing a raw numeric comparison — a
    same-numbers-different-units comparison would be meaningless and could
    produce a false match or false mismatch either way.
  - `_classify_exception()`'s amount-mismatch detail text ("Amount differs:
    Invoice RM... vs PO RM...") no longer hardcodes "RM" — uses each
    document's actual currency (falling back to "RM" only if unset).

FRONTEND (auditor-record-detail component):
  - `formatAmount()` no longer hardcodes `'RM ' + ...` — takes an optional
    currency parameter and uses it (still defaulting to 'RM' when unset,
    for old records with no currency stored). This was a real bug: an
    invoice actually in USD would previously have displayed as "RM
    8,020.00", exactly the "USD vs RM silently mixed" problem the request
    was about.
  - `amountSymbol()` (drives the Amount row's Match/Differ pill) now also
    takes both documents' currencies — if they're both known and differ,
    returns 'na' instead of doing a raw numeric compare, mirroring the
    same fix on the backend's `amount_match`. This was a second instance
    of the same bug: the pill was computed client-side from raw numbers
    with no currency awareness at all.
  - All three call sites (Field Comparison table's Amount row + Amount
    match pill, and the side-panel Document Info Amount line) updated to
    pass `comparison.invoice.currency`/`comparison.po.currency` through.

Why: the goal was specifically to support real, messy invoices/POs/GRs —
  clean standard PDFs already worked. Non-standard labels and multi-
  currency totals are exactly what regex structurally can't reason about
  (it has no understanding that "INVOICE:" and "Invoice No." mean the same
  thing, or that a number following "EXCHANGE RATE=" is a converted value,
  not the real total), which is why Gemini becomes primary and regex
  becomes fallback-only for these fields — the reverse of the previous
  invoice-only arrangement.

Testing (all offline, no live Gemini/network call — per this session's
strict rule):
  - `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on every changed backend file

    two entries (line-item table extraction, po_reference normalization,
    quantity mismatch detection) — all still pass, no regression from the
    new patterns inserted into the same per-line loops.

even though it wasn't asked for — the `extract_gr_fields()` "GRN No:"
label gap noted in the 2026-07-17 entry above is still NOT fixed by this
change (the new "doc" alternative only covers the "Doc No." label
specifically; "GRN" still partial-matches "GR" then fails on the "N"
before "No:", same as before).

  2. The extracted_fields.currency migration runs automatically at
     startup, same as recent prior entries — no manual SQL needed.
  3. Existing invoice records uploaded before this deploy have no
     currency stored (NULL) — the Field Comparison table will fall back to
     showing "RM" for those until they're re-uploaded or Re-checked. Only
     new uploads (or explicit Re-check, which re-runs the merged Gemini
     call and can now populate currency retroactively for that one field
     set) get real currency detection.
  4. Since Gemini is now PRIMARY for PO/GR fields (previously regex was
     primary with a text-based Gemini override), re-upload or Re-check a

     output, not just this session's offline regex-fallback tests — the
     Gemini prompt changes themselves are not exercised by any offline
     test (no live API calls are made in this codebase's test discipline).

2026-07-18 - Fix 3 bugs found testing against REAL Coilcraft/EMITS
             documents: invoice total picked the converted RM value
             instead of the original USD, currency showed RM for USD
             documents, GR number picked up the referenced PO instead
             of its own Doc No.

Context: the previous entry's multi-currency handling was written and
  tested against a same-line assumption ("TOTAL (US$) 8,020.00" all on one
  line). Testing against the actual Coilcraft invoice showed Google Vision
  OCR splits this onto SEPARATE lines ("TOTAL (US$)" then "8,020.00" on the
  next line) — the same one-cell-per-line behavior already established for
  this app's line-item tables, just not accounted for in the currency fix.
  The previous same-line-only regex never matched, so the fallback path
  fell through to the exchange-rate-converted "TOTAL" line instead.

FIX 1 (priority) — invoice total_amount picking the converted RM value
(helpers/ocr_helper.py `extract_fields()`):
  - New two-line detection: a line that is EXACTLY "TOTAL (US$)" (or
    "TOTAL (USD)"), value taken from the next line — mirrors the existing
    bare "TOTAL" -> next-line pattern already used for the plain-total
    case, now added for the currency-tagged case too.
  - New document-level `seen_exchange_rate` flag: once a line containing
    "exchange rate" is seen ANYWHERE earlier in the document, every
    subsequent generic "Total"/"Sub Total" line (same-line pattern list
    AND the bare "TOTAL" + next-line fallback) is suppressed entirely,
    not just the one line that literally contains "exchange rate" text
    (the previous fix only excluded that single line — the converted
    "SUB TOTAL"/"TOTAL" lines that typically follow it on their OWN
    lines were never covered). The original-currency USD total is
    detected independently and unconditionally wins when present, so
    this suppression only ever removes candidates that would otherwise
    incorrectly compete with it.
  - Applied the identical CURRENCY_NOTE strengthening (below) to the
    Gemini prompt — Gemini is PRIMARY now, so the regex fix alone isn't
    sufficient; both paths needed the fix.

FIX 2 — currency shown as RM for USD documents (helpers/gemini_extractor.py,
routes/documents.py, helpers/ocr_helper.py):
  - CURRENCY_NOTE (shared by all 3 Gemini prompts) gained an explicit
    "currency MUST match the currency of the total_amount you actually
    return" rule, with a worked example matching the exact reported
    failure mode (returning 8020 as total_amount but "RM" as currency,
    because "(RM)" also appears elsewhere on the page in an unrelated
    field) — the previous prompt explained WHICH amount to prefer but
    never explicitly tied total_amount and currency together as one
    linked decision, which is the most likely reason Gemini could get the
    amount right while still returning the wrong currency tag.
  - Also strengthened to cover the label/value visual-separation case
    (the "(US$)" tag may be visually apart from its number) and to name
    "SUB TOTAL"/repeated "Total" wording inside an exchange-rate block
    explicitly, matching the real document's exact structure.
  - GR previously had NO currency/total_amount handling at all in the
    Gemini path (GR_FULL_PROMPT's JSON schema didn't include either key,
    and routes/documents.py's GR override loop didn't include them) —
    most GRNs carry no monetary total, but the request explicitly asked
    for currency to flow for GR too. Added `total_amount`/`currency` to
    GR_FULL_PROMPT's schema (documented as usually null) and to the
    override loop in `upload_goods_receipt()`. Added the same USD-total
    regex fallback used by extract_po_fields() to extract_gr_fields(), so
    a GR that DOES show a monetary value gets the same original-currency
    preference.
  - The invoice and PO paths already correctly stored/overrode currency
    from a working extraction (per this entry's regression tests) — the
    fix here is entirely about GR gaining the same support, and about the
    Gemini prompt no longer being able to decouple total_amount from
    currency.

FIX 3 — GR number picking up the referenced PO instead of its own Doc No.
(helpers/ocr_helper.py `extract_gr_fields()`, helpers/gemini_extractor.py
GR_FULL_PROMPT):
  - Root cause: the gr_number regex's `doc\.?` alternative does an
    unanchored substring search, so it matched "Doc No." inside "From Doc
    No.: PO3006000" just as readily as inside the GR's own "Doc No.
    PD6011823" line — nothing distinguished "Doc No." from "From Doc
    No.", so whichever line the loop reached first won, silently
    returning the wrong document number when "From Doc No." happened to
    appear before the real "Doc No." line.
  - Fix: lines matching `\bfrom\s+doc` are now skipped entirely for
    gr_number extraction (regardless of document order — verified with a
    dedicated order-independence test, see Testing below).
  - The referenced PO is now captured correctly instead of being
    dropped: extract_gr_fields()'s existing po_reference regex (which
    already handled "PO No:"/"PO Ref:") gained "From Doc No." as another
    recognized label, so "From Doc No.: PO3006000" now correctly
    populates po_reference = 'PO3006000' rather than being lost.
  - GR_FULL_PROMPT already told Gemini to route "From Doc No."/"PO Ref"
    into po_reference (added in the previous entry) — strengthened
    further with the exact "From Doc No.: PO3006000" example and an
    explicit rule that a label STARTING WITH "From" is always the
    referenced PO, never the GR's own number, even though it contains
    the words "Doc No."

Why: real Coilcraft/EMITS documents are the actual target for this
  feature (per the original request), so testing against them — not just
  synthetic text built from a paraphrased description — is what surfaced
  all three of these gaps. Two of the three (Fix 1 and Fix 3) came from
  the same underlying pattern: a previous fix's regex correctly handled
  the CONCEPT (original-currency preference, "Doc No." label tolerance)
  but was validated against a hand-built same-line test string that
  didn't match how Google Vision actually splits real document text
  across lines/labels.

Testing (all offline, no live Gemini/network call):
  - `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on every changed backend
    file — compiles clean.
  - New offline test (scratchpad, not committed) built directly from the
    real document patterns in this request:
    - Invoice with "TOTAL (US$)" and "8,020.00" on SEPARATE lines (the
      realistic split), followed by "EXCHANGE RATE = 1.2670" then "SUB
      TOTAL"/"10161.34" then "TOTAL"/"10161.34" each as their own
      bare-label-then-next-line pair — confirmed total_amount == 8020.00
      and currency == 'USD' (not 10161.34/RM).
    - Repeated with the same-line variant ("TOTAL (US$) 8,020.00" all on
      one line) to confirm the original fix still works — no regression.
    - Repeated again with just a bare "TOTAL" + next-line "10161.34"
      after "EXCHANGE RATE=1.2670" (no "SUB TOTAL" in between) — the
      most direct reproduction of the suppression logic — confirmed
      8020.00/USD still wins.
    - PO regression: "Doc No. PO3006000" + "USD 8,020" + "Total Payable
      Incl. Tax (RM) 32,946.16" — confirmed total_amount == 8020.00,
      currency == 'USD' (unchanged from the previous entry, PO logic
      wasn't touched by this fix).
    - GR with "Doc No.  PD6011823" followed by "From Doc No.:
      PO3006000" — confirmed gr_number == 'PD6011823' (not 'PO3006000')
      and po_reference == 'PO3006000'. Repeated with the two lines in
      REVERSED order (From Doc No. line first) to confirm the fix isn't
      order-dependent — same correct result both ways.
    - Regression: a plain single-currency (no "exchange rate" text
      anywhere) RM-only invoice still extracts total_amount/currency
      correctly — confirms the new seen_exchange_rate suppression only
      activates when an actual exchange-rate marker is present.
  - Re-ran all three pre-existing offline regex test suites from prior
    entries (line-item table extraction, po_reference normalization/
    quantity mismatch, and the previous entry's real-document regex
    test) — all still pass, no regression from the changes to the same
    per-line loops.

Note (not fixed, out of scope): the `extract_gr_fields()` "GRN No:" label
gap flagged two entries ago is still not fixed (unrelated to this
request's 3 fixes).

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend — this is a backend-only change (no
     frontend files touched).
  2. Re-upload or Re-check the same real Coilcraft/EMITS documents used
     to find these bugs, to confirm against actual Gemini vision output
     — the Gemini prompt strengthening (Fix 1/2's CURRENCY_NOTE update,
     Fix 3's GR_FULL_PROMPT update) is not exercised by any offline test,
     only the regex fallback is. If Gemini still returns the wrong
     currency/amount/gr_number after redeploying, the regex fallback
     should now catch it correctly as long as Gemini's vision call fails
     or is unavailable — but a live-document check against Gemini itself
     is the real confirmation this request asked for.
