2026-07-18 - Fix 3 bugs found testing a matched Malaysian invoice/PO/GR
             set (Megatech supplier -> Oriontech buyer): PO vendor_name
             returned the buyer instead of the supplier, PO item/
             quantity came back empty, and authenticity permanently
             degraded to text-only after a Gemini rate limit

Context: unlike an invoice (where the letterhead company IS the vendor),
  a PO's letterhead is the BUYER issuing the order, and a GR's letterhead
  is the RECEIVING company — the actual vendor is named under a separate
  "Supplier"/"Vendor"/"Received From" section further down the page. This
  is a structurally different extraction problem per document type, not a
  regex tuning issue.

BUG 1 — PO/GR vendor_name returned the letterhead (buyer/receiver)
instead of the supplier (helpers/ocr_helper.py, helpers/gemini_extractor.py):
  - Root cause: `extract_po_fields()`/`extract_gr_fields()`'s vendor
    regex was UNCONDITIONAL — it matched the FIRST line with a company
    suffix (Sdn Bhd, Berhad, etc.) anywhere in the document, which is
    almost always the letterhead at the top, with no awareness that a PO/
    GR's letterhead is the WRONG company entirely (unlike an invoice,
    where taking the first/letterhead company IS correct — confirmed via
    regression test, left unchanged).
  - Fix: new `PO_SUPPLIER_HEADING_RE` ("Supplier"/"Vendor"/a bare "To:"
    label — NOT "Ship To"/"Deliver To"/"Bill To", which are different
    recipient fields) and `GR_SUPPLIER_HEADING_RE` ("Received From"/
    "Supplier"/"Delivered By"). Vendor extraction now tracks a
    document-level "seen a supplier heading yet" flag and refuses to
    match ANY company name until that heading has actually been seen —
    the letterhead can structurally never be picked up, since it always
    appears before the heading. If no supplier heading is found at all,
    vendor_name stays null rather than defaulting to the (wrong)
    letterhead — matches this codebase's existing "return null over a
    guess" convention. The vendor-match regex itself changed from
    anchored (`^...`) to unanchored so a same-line label like "Supplier:
    MEGATECH COMPONENTS (M) SDN. BHD." still matches starting at the
    company name (the anchor previously required the company suffix to
    appear with nothing but word characters between it and the start of
    the line, which "Supplier: " — containing a colon — breaks).
  - PO_FULL_PROMPT/GR_FULL_PROMPT (Gemini, primary extractor) already
    had SOME vendor guidance from an earlier entry, but evidently not
    forceful enough — strengthened both with an explicit "COMMON
    MISTAKE, read carefully" framing and the EXACT worked example from
    this bug report (Oriontech letterhead vs Megatech supplier), mirroring
    the CURRENCY_NOTE worked-example pattern that fixed a similar
    "correct concept, Gemini still got it wrong" issue in the previous
    entry. Also instructed to return null rather than default to the
    letterhead if no supplier section is found.
  - Invoice's vendor extraction (letterhead = vendor) was NOT touched —
    confirmed already correct per the request, verified unchanged by a
    regression test below.

BUG 2 — PO item_description/quantity came back empty (helpers/ocr_helper.py
`_extract_first_line_item()`, shared by all three of extract_fields/
extract_po_fields/extract_gr_fields):
  - `extract_po_fields()` already called `_extract_first_line_item()`
    identically to the invoice/GR extractors — the bug wasn't a missing
    wire-up, it was a false trigger inside the shared function itself.
  - Root cause: the "is this actually an unsplit combined row, not a
    clean single-cell description?" safety net bailed out (returned
    `(None, None)`) whenever the candidate description line contained
    ANY decimal-shaped number ANYWHERE in it (`re.search(r'\d+\.\d+',
    line)`). A real component description very often legitimately
    contains one — e.g. "MTC-IND-4R7M Power Inductor 4.7uH 20% SMD" —
    which was being mistaken for evidence that the whole row (number +
    description + price + amount) had landed on one line instead of
    being split one-cell-per-line, silently discarding a perfectly
    valid description.
  - Reproduced directly (offline, no OCR/network involved) against the
    exact description text before fixing: confirmed
    `_extract_first_line_item()` returned `(None, None)` for it.
  - Fix: narrowed the check to require the line to actually END with
    TWO decimal-shaped numbers separated by whitespace
    (`r'\d+\.\d+\s+[\d,]+\.\d+\s*$'` — unit price then amount, the real
    shape of an unsplit combined row like "...  8.00 960.00"), instead
    of matching any decimal substring anywhere. Verified both the fix
    (decimal-bearing description now parses correctly) and the original
    safety net's own purpose still works (a genuine unsplit row like "1
    Aluminium Bracket A100 120 8.00 960.00" still correctly bails so the
    LINE_ITEM_ROW_RE/label-based fallbacks can take over).
  - This is a shared-function fix, not PO-specific — it benefits
    invoice/GR too for any real description containing a decimal value,
    even though it was only reported against the PO.

BUG 3 — authenticity permanently fell back to text-only after a Gemini
free-tier rate limit (helpers/gemini_extractor.py `call_gemini_sdk()`,
helpers/authenticity_check.py):
  - New `GEMINI_RATE_LIMIT_RETRY_DELAYS = (20, 10)`: `call_gemini_sdk()`
    (the single choke point every Gemini call in the codebase goes
    through) now detects a 429/RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED specifically and
    retries automatically with backoff (20s, then 10s) before giving up
    — transparent to every existing caller (invoice/PO/GR merged
    extraction, authenticity, anomaly explanation), no interface change
    needed for the retry itself, since it happens fully inside the
    existing str-or-None return contract. A non-rate-limit error (e.g.
    500, timeout, bad model) is NOT retried — only 429 gets the backoff
    treatment.
  - New `GeminiRateLimitError` exception + `on_rate_limit='raise'`
    opt-in parameter on `call_gemini_sdk()` (default stays
    `'return_none'`, so the other 4 existing call sites are completely
    unaffected): when the caller opts in and retries are still
    exhausted, this is raised instead of silently returning None, so
    `run_authenticity_check()`'s fallback can tell "temporarily
    rate-limited, will likely succeed on Re-check in a minute or two"
    apart from a permanent failure — only `authenticity_check.py`'s
    `_call_gemini_vision()` opts in.
  - `_fallback_from_ocr_text()` gained a `rate_limited` parameter: when
    true, the `ai_notes` text now explicitly says this is temporary and
    names "Re-check" as the fix, instead of the previous wording ("Gemini
    unavailable") which read as a permanent condition with no clear next
    step.
  - DB caching behavior is unchanged — a successful analysis is still
    stored permanently, Re-check is still the only manual re-call
    (neither the retry nor the rate-limit signaling touches that path).
  - Tradeoff, flagged rather than hidden: a document that actually hits
    the rate limit now takes up to ~30s longer to upload (the backoff
    wait) before falling back, since this happens synchronously inside
    the upload request. This is the explicit tradeoff requested — "a
    burst of uploads doesn't permanently degrade results" — and only
    affects the (hopefully rare) case where a call is actually
    rate-limited; a normal, unthrottled call is unaffected.

Why: "Verify this stays correct" (from the request, re: GR's vendor
  extraction) turned out to reveal the SAME bug GR shares with PO —
  empirically, before this fix, extract_gr_fields() ALSO returned the
  letterhead (Oriontech) instead of the supplier (Megatech) for a
  realistic GR text structure, even though the request's own test case
  apparently didn't trigger it. Fixed rather than left as "unverified but
  probably fine," consistent with this session's practice of fixing a
  concretely-reproduced bug even when only asked to "verify."

Testing (all offline, no live Gemini/network call):
  - `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on every changed backend
    file — compiles clean.
  - Reproduced BUG 2 directly before fixing: called
    `_extract_first_line_item()` with the exact reported description
    text and confirmed it returned `(None, None)` — then confirmed the
    fix resolves it and the original unsplit-row case still bails
    correctly (added as an explicit regression check).
  - New consolidated test (scratchpad, not committed) covering BUG 1+2
    together against a realistic Oriontech/Megatech PO and GR text
    structure: confirmed po.vendor_name/gr.vendor_name both correctly
    return 'MEGATECH COMPONENTS (M) SDN. BHD' (not 'ORIONTECH ELECTRONICS
    SDN. BHD'), po.item_description/po.quantity and gr.item_description/
    gr.quantity all populate correctly with the decimal-bearing
    description. Also tested: an inline "Supplier: <name>" label (not
    just a bare heading line), a bare "To:" heading, and confirmed "Ship
    To:"/"Deliver To:" are correctly NOT treated as a supplier heading
    (vendor_name stays null rather than picking up the wrong address).
    Regression: invoice's vendor_name still correctly returns the
    letterhead (unchanged behavior), and a final 3-way check confirms
    invoice/po/gr all agree on the same vendor name for this matched set.
  - Re-ran all four pre-existing offline regex test suites from prior
    entries — all still pass, no regression from the vendor-gating or
    line-item safety-net changes.
  - New offline test for BUG 3 (scratchpad, not committed) using a
    mocked google-genai client (no real network call) with `time.sleep`
    patched out for speed: (1) 429 twice then success — confirmed
    `call_gemini_sdk()` retries with the exact [20, 10] backoff and
    returns the eventual success; (2) 429 on every attempt with the
    default `on_rate_limit='return_none'` — confirmed it gives up after
    exactly 1 initial + 2 retries and returns None, not an infinite loop;
    (3) same persistent-429 case with `on_rate_limit='raise'` — confirmed
    `GeminiRateLimitError` is raised; (4) a non-rate-limit 500 error —
    confirmed NO retry happens and `time.sleep` is never called, proving
    the backoff is scoped to 429 only. Also directly called
    `run_authenticity_check()` with `_call_gemini_vision` mocked to raise
    `GeminiRateLimitError` and confirmed the DB row's `ai_notes` mentions
    "Re-check" and "temporary" and does NOT say "unavailable" — then
    repeated with a normal (non-rate-limit) failure and confirmed the
    notes text is unchanged from before ("unavailable", no "Re-check"
    mention), proving the two failure modes are now distinguishable
    without changing behavior for the common non-rate-limit case.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend — backend-only change, no frontend
     files touched.
  2. Re-upload or Re-check the same real Megatech/Oriontech PO/GR used to
     find these bugs to confirm against live Gemini vision output — the
     Gemini prompt strengthening for Bug 1 is not exercised by any
     offline test, only the regex fallback is.
  3. Bug 3 is best confirmed by uploading 3+ documents in quick
     succession (the scenario that originally triggered it) and checking
     that authenticity results no longer permanently degrade to
     text-only for the later ones — a genuinely rate-limited upload will
     now visibly take longer (up to ~30s) before either succeeding via
     retry or falling back with the new "temporary, use Re-check" notes
     text, rather than failing immediately.

2026-07-18 - Fix 2 bugs in the record-detail comparison: banner said "All
             Fields Match" while a row showed Mismatch, and MYR vs RM
             (the same currency) showed "N/A" instead of "Match"

BUG A (critical, logic contradiction) — banner could say "All Fields
Match — Ready for approval" (green, PASS) while a row was visibly showing
"⚠ Mismatch" (routes/auditor.py `_build_comparison()`):
  - Root cause: `overall_status` was computed from only 3 of the 5 checks
    that actually have a visible row/pill in the Field Comparison table
    (`checks = [vendor_match, amount_match, quantity_match]`) —
    `po_reference_match`/`item_match` were deliberately excluded by an
    earlier entry (reasoned then as "more prone to false positives, keep
    display-only"). That reasoning produced exactly the bug this request
    reports: a real PO Ref mismatch (invoice "PO-ORT-26-0741" vs PO's own
    number "PO-ORT-26-0471" — genuinely different, not a normalization
    artifact) has a visible "✗ Mismatch" pill in the table, but couldn't
    flip `overall_status` away from PASS since `po_reference_match`
    wasn't in the `checks` list at all — the exact "auditor could approve
    a record with a visible mismatch" danger described in the request.
  - Fix: new invariant, stated and enforced directly — the banner is
    PASS (green, "All Fields Match") if and only if NONE of the 5
    displayed checks (vendor/amount/PO Ref/Item/Quantity) is False.
    `vendor_match`/`amount_match`/`quantity_match` stay "hard" checks
    (any False -> FAIL, red, unchanged from before). `po_reference_match`/
    `item_match` become "soft" checks: a False among these no longer
    stays invisible to the banner, but also doesn't escalate all the way
    to FAIL (still best-effort OCR fields, more prone to false positives
    than the mature hard checks) — instead a NEW third state, `REVIEW`
    (amber, "Review Required — some fields differ — see highlighted
    rows"), sits between PASS and FAIL. `PARTIAL` (missing PO/GR
    document) is unchanged and still takes lower priority than either
    FAIL or REVIEW.
  - `_classify_exception()` gained a matching `REVIEW` branch (rank 2,
    between `low_confidence` rank 1 and `sent_back`/`missing_document`
    rank 3) so a record showing the new amber banner also shows up as an
    exception in whatever list/queue consumes `_classify_exception` —
    without this, a soft-mismatch record would only be visible if an
    auditor happened to open that specific record's detail page,
    reintroducing a version of the same "danger" in a different place.
    Flagging this as a scope decision: the request described the
    detail-page contradiction specifically, but leaving the exceptions
    list silent on a record the detail page now (correctly) flags as
    "Review Required" seemed like the same class of gap left half-fixed.
  - Verified vendor_match/amount_match's backend computation is
    logically equivalent to "does any pairwise cell pill shown in the
    table disagree": `vendor_match` is a 3-way set-equality check (`len(
    set(normalized)) <= 1`), which is mathematically the same as "every
    pair of present values is equal" — and the frontend's per-cell
    `vendorSymbol()` uses the IDENTICAL normalization logic as the
    backend's `_normalize_vendor()` (confirmed by direct comparison,
    unchanged). `amount_match` is explicitly Invoice-vs-PO only, matching
    the ONE amount pill actually shown (GR's amount cell is hardcoded
    "No amount on GR", never a pill). This is why extending
    `overall_status` to include the two previously-excluded checks is
    sufficient to satisfy the stated invariant, without needing to
    duplicate the invariant-checking logic in the frontend.
  - Frontend (auditor-record-detail component): `getBannerText()`/
    `getBannerSubtitle()` gained a `REVIEW` branch ("Review Required" /
    "Some fields differ — see highlighted rows"). `getBannerClass()`
    reuses the existing `banner-partial` CSS class (amber) for `REVIEW`
    rather than adding new CSS — PARTIAL and REVIEW are both "needs
    attention, not a hard failure" states and were already using the
    exact amber the request asked for; only the banner TEXT needed to
    distinguish "documents incomplete" from "some fields differ".

BUG B — MYR vs RM (the same currency, different notation) showed "N/A"
instead of "Match" (routes/auditor.py `_build_comparison()`):
  - Root cause: the currency-difference guard added in an earlier entry
    (to stop USD being silently compared against RM as if they were the
    same unit) did a bare string-equality check on the raw currency
    values — "MYR" and "RM" are the SAME Malaysian Ringgit (just
    different notations: the regex fallback defaults to 'MYR', Gemini
    sometimes returns 'RM'), but compared as literally different
    strings, so a genuinely equal amount in the same currency fell into
    the "different currency, not applicable" branch instead of being
    compared.
  - Fix: new `_normalize_currency()` — recognizes 'RM'/'MYR'/'MYR (RM)'
    (and similar compound notations) as the same canonical 'RM' via a
    word-boundary match (`\b(?:RM|MYR)\b`), NOT a naive strip-then-
    equality check — an earlier draft of this fix stripped all
    non-letters before comparing, which turned "MYR (RM)" into the
    unrecognizable "MYRRM" and still failed to match; caught by a test
    case for exactly this compound notation before treating the fix as
    done. A genuinely different currency (e.g. "USD") still normalizes
    to itself and is NOT folded into 'RM', so the original USD-vs-RM
    "not applicable" guard this same entry is built on top of still
    works correctly (verified by regression test).
  - Applied at the SAME point the invoice/PO dicts are built in
    `_build_comparison()`, so the normalized ('RM') value is both what's
    used for the equality comparison AND what's returned to the frontend
    for display — invoice/PO now always show the same representation
    ('RM') for the same underlying currency instead of whichever variant
    that particular document's extractor happened to return, per the
    request's "normalize the displayed currency consistently" ask. No
    frontend changes were needed for this part: since the values arrive
    already-normalized, the frontend's existing currency-aware
    `amountSymbol()` equality check (`fromCurrency.toUpperCase() !==
    toCurrency.toUpperCase()`) now naturally sees 'RM' === 'RM' without
    any code change there.

Why: "the invariant to enforce and test: banner green 'All Fields Match'
  <=> zero rows displaying Mismatch" (quoted directly from the request)
  is exactly what BUG A's fix implements and BUG B's fix doesn't
  interfere with — a currency-normalization false-negative (N/A instead
  of Match) isn't itself a Mismatch, so it wasn't contributing to BUG A,
  but both were reported together against the same record and both
  needed fixing for that record's comparison to be trustworthy.

Testing (all offline, mocked cursor, no real DB/Gemini/network call):
  - `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on the changed backend file
    — compiles clean. `npx ng build --configuration=development` on the
    frontend — passes clean, confirming the new REVIEW banner branch and
    reused CSS class don't break compilation.
  - New test (scratchpad, not committed) built directly from the
    reported scenario (Oriontech Electronics, invoice PO ref
    "PO-ORT-26-0741" vs PO's own number "PO-ORT-26-0471", invoice amount
    "MYR 6,253.20" vs PO amount "RM 6,253.20"):
    - Confirmed `po_reference_match` is `False` (a real mismatch) while
      `vendor_match`/`amount_match`/`quantity_match` are all `True`, and
      `overall_status` is the new `'REVIEW'` state — NOT `'PASS'`. This
      is requested test (1): a PO-ref mismatch must not show green "All
      Fields Match".
    - Swept 6 scenarios (all-match baseline plus one deliberate mismatch
      each for vendor/amount/quantity — hard — and po_reference/item —
      soft) and asserted the invariant directly:
      `overall_status == 'PASS'` is never true at the same time as "any
      of the 5 displayed checks is False", across every scenario.
    - Regression: a genuine hard mismatch (vendor) still escalates all
      the way to `'FAIL'`, not just `'REVIEW'` — confirms severity
      ordering (hard vs soft) survived the fix.
    - Regression: a fully-matching record (PO's number corrected to
      match the invoice's po_reference) still correctly shows `'PASS'`
      — confirms the fix didn't make PASS unreachable.
    - This is requested test (2): confirmed `amount_match` is `True`
      (not `None`/N/A) for invoice `currency='MYR'` vs PO `currency='RM'`
      with equal amounts, and that both sides display the normalized
      `'RM'` in the response.
    - Regression: a GENUINELY different currency (USD vs RM) with the
      same numeric amount still correctly returns `amount_match=None`
      (not silently treated as a match) — confirms the original
      currency-mismatch guard this fix builds on still works.
    - Regression: `'MYR (RM)'` compound notation also normalizes to
      `'RM'` and compares correctly — the exact case that caught the
      naive strip-then-equality bug in an earlier draft of this fix,
      kept as a permanent regression check.
  - Re-ran all six pre-existing offline test suites from prior entries
    (regex fallback, line-item table extraction, quantity mismatch
    detection, the Coilcraft/EMITS 3-fixes test, the Megatech/Oriontech
    vendor/item-line test, and the Gemini rate-limit retry test) — all
    still pass, no regression from the overall_status/currency changes.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend AND frontend together — the frontend's
     new REVIEW banner text/class depends on the backend actually
     returning the `'REVIEW'` overall_status value.
  2. Re-open the record from the screenshot (or any record with a PO
     Ref/Item mismatch but otherwise-matching vendor/amount/quantity)
     after redeploying — it should now show the amber "Review Required"
     banner instead of green "All Fields Match", and the Amount row
     should show "✓ Match" instead of "— N/A" wherever both sides are
     genuinely the same currency (MYR/RM) with equal amounts.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
2026-07-19 - Upgrade 3-way matching from single-field to LINE-ITEM LEVEL:
             every row of the goods/services table is now extracted and
             matched across Invoice/PO/GR, not just the first item

Context: the Field Comparison table only ever compared item_description/
  quantity from the FIRST line item per document — an invoice with 3 items
  only ever checked item #1; items 2 and 3 were never compared at all.
  Summing quantities across items was explicitly ruled out (different
  products/units, and it would mask tampering: 5000+8000 vs 4000+9000 both
  total 13000). Each line item now has to be matched individually.

EXTRACTION — every row, not just the first (helpers/ocr_helper.py,
helpers/gemini_extractor.py):
  - New `_extract_all_line_items()`: generalizes the existing
    `_extract_first_line_item()` (kept UNCHANGED, zero risk to its
    tested behavior) into a loop over the SAME confirmed real Google
    Vision OCR table structure (one cell per line: row number,
    description, integer qty, decimal unit price, decimal amount,
    repeating) — collecting every row until a totals/footer line
    (Subtotal/Grand Total/Total/Amount Due) or end of document. The
    first item's parsing mirrors the single-item version's "never
    guess" bail-out exactly (a malformed first row -> empty list); a
    malformed row AFTER at least one item has already been found just
    ends scanning, keeping what was cleanly parsed rather than
    discarding it. Capped at `MAX_LINE_ITEMS = 50` (Render free tier is
    512MB — a garbled document must not produce an unbounded result).
  - Wired into all three of extract_fields()/extract_po_fields()/
    extract_gr_fields() as a NEW `fields['line_items']` list, running
    alongside (not replacing) the existing `_extract_first_line_item()`
    call — item_description/quantity stay exactly as before for
    backward compatibility, per the request.
  - New shared `LINE_ITEMS_NOTE` added to all three merged Gemini
    prompts (invoice/PO/GR) — Gemini (already the primary extractor,
    already making exactly one vision call per upload) now ALSO returns
    a `line_items` array in the SAME response: `{item_code, description,
    quantity, unit_price, amount}` per row, capped at 50, empty array if
    no table is found. No additional Gemini call is made anywhere in
    this change — the array rides along in the existing merged call.
  - routes/documents.py's Gemini-override loop (all 3 upload handlers)
    gained special handling for line_items: unlike the other fields
    (overridden whenever Gemini's value `is not None`), an EMPTY list
    from Gemini means "no table found", not "override with nothing" —
    only replaces the regex fallback's items when Gemini actually found
    some (`if gemini_result.get('line_items'):`), so a Gemini table-read
    failure doesn't silently wipe out a working regex extraction.

PERSISTENCE — new `document_line_items` table (app.py, migrations/,
routes/documents.py):
  - New table: `id, document_id, document_type, line_no, item_code,
    description, quantity, unit_price, amount`. `document_id` points at
    the SAME invoice document_id used across purchase_orders/
    goods_receipts (not po_id/gr_id) — matches how those tables already
    key off it. New `_ensure_document_line_items_table()` in app.py
    (auto-creates the table + an index at startup, same pattern as
    every other `_ensure_` function — no migration runner in this
    repo) + matching migrations/2026-07-18_add_document_line_items.sql
    for local-dev/documentation parity.
  - New `_sanitize_line_items()`/`_save_line_items()` helpers in
    routes/documents.py: sanitize coerces Gemini's (or the regex
    fallback's) line_items into a clean, bounded, correctly-typed list
    (caps at 50, drops any entry with no description, coerces quantity/
    unit_price/amount to float or None) before it ever reaches the DB —
    never trusts Gemini's JSON shape blindly. save DELETE-then-INSERTs
    per (document_id, document_type): PO/GR can be re-uploaded onto the
    SAME document_id (the existing `ORDER BY uploaded_at DESC LIMIT 1`
    pattern elsewhere in this codebase confirms re-upload support), so
    a stale previous upload's line items must not linger mixed in with
    the new ones.

MATCHING — by item_code or normalized description (routes/auditor.py):
  - New `_line_item_key()`: item_code when present (normalized:
    uppercase, strip non-alphanumerics) else normalized description
    (case-insensitive, collapsed whitespace, via the existing
    `_normalize_text()`) — same "tolerate minor OCR differences via
    normalization, not fuzzy matching" philosophy as `_normalize_vendor`/
    `_normalize_ref` elsewhere in this file. No Levenshtein/fuzzy
    matching — out of scope, not requested beyond case/whitespace
    tolerance.
  - New `_match_line_items()`: unions the distinct keys across all three
    documents' line items (invoice-then-PO-only-then-GR-only order),
    and for each key compares quantity (all present values equal ->
    Match, differ -> HARD Mismatch) and amount (all present values
    equal -> Match, differ -> SOFT Mismatch — see "Scope decision"
    below for why amount, not unit_price, was chosen), plus flags an
    item present in one document but absent from another document that
    WAS actually uploaded ("missing_on_po"/"missing_on_gr" — a HARD,
    "critical audit finding" per the request, same severity as a
    quantity mismatch).
  - Deliberate defensive guard: a document that WAS uploaded but
    produced ZERO line items (a total extraction failure, not a real
    "nothing was ordered") is treated the SAME as "not uploaded" for
    missing-item purposes — otherwise one failed extraction would flag
    EVERY invoice item as "missing" on that document, a false signal
    about extraction, not a real audit finding. Verified with a
    dedicated regression test.
  - Scope decision (flagged rather than silently narrowed): the request
    asked to compare "quantity (and unit_price/amount where present)".
    Implemented as a SINGLE `amount_match` per item rather than two
    separate unit_price_match/amount_match checks — amount is the more
    meaningful "does this line's total agree" audit signal (if quantity
    and unit price both agree, amount agrees too; if amount disagrees,
    something in the line total is wrong), and a second full comparison
    dimension would need its own visible UI indicator per item, adding
    real clutter to an already-dense table for a check redundant with
    the quantity+amount checks already present.

overall_status / Field Comparison table wiring (routes/auditor.py):
  - `line_items_match` (any line item hard-mismatched or missing)
    REPLACES the old single-value `quantity_match` (first item only) as
    a HARD check (FAIL, red) — closes the "3-item invoice only ever
    checks item #1" gap directly. `line_items_price_match` (any
    matched item's amount disagrees) REPLACES the old single-value
    `item_match` as a SOFT check (REVIEW, amber).
  - The OLD single-value `item_match`/`quantity_match` are STILL
    computed and returned in `match_result` (backward compatibility,
    per the request), but — like `date_order_valid` before them —
    deliberately EXCLUDED from the checks driving `overall_status`: the
    Field Comparison table no longer has a single "Item / Description"/
    "Quantity" row for them (replaced by the Line Items section), so
    letting them still drive the banner would be an invisible check
    silently affecting a green/amber/red state with no matching visible
    row for an auditor to investigate — exactly the `date_order_valid`
    bug fixed in an earlier entry, which would have been reintroduced
    here for a different pair of fields if left wired in.
  - Bug caught and fixed WHILE verifying the invariant, before treating
    this as done: `line_items_price_match` (soft, drives the amber
    REVIEW state) initially had NO visible per-item indicator in the
    table at all — an item's `amount_match` was computed and could flip
    the banner to REVIEW, but nothing in the rendered row showed WHY.
    This is the exact same class of bug as the `date_order_valid`/
    `po_reference_match` issues fixed in earlier entries, just
    reintroduced for a new field in this same change. Fixed by adding a
    visible "💲 Amount/unit price differs" note under the item
    description whenever `amount_match === false`, and giving that row
    standard `row-mismatch` (amber-ish) styling — without the extra
    `row-quantity-alert` red stripe, which stays reserved for hard
    quantity mismatches/missing items. Caught this by explicitly
    checking the invariant against a REVIEW-only scenario, not by
    assumption.
  - `_classify_exception()`'s FAIL branch: the old "Quantity differs:
    PO X vs GR Y vs Invoice Z" single-value detail text is replaced
    with a per-line-item breakdown ("Line item mismatch: \"Widget A\":
    PO 8000 vs GR 7500 vs Invoice 8000; \"Widget C\" missing on PO"),
    capped at 3 items in the detail text (+N more) to keep it readable.
    The REVIEW branch's old `item_match`-based text is replaced with a
    `line_items_price_match`-based one. Reuses the existing 'mismatch'/
    'review' exception types per the request ("reuse/extend the
    existing quantity-mismatch exception type") rather than adding new
    ones.

FRONTEND (auditor-record-detail component): the old single "Item /
Description" and "Quantity" `<tr>` rows are replaced with a Line Items
section — a header row ("📦 Line Items (N)") followed by one `<tr>` per
`comparison.line_items` entry (server-computed), each showing the
description (+ item_code if present) and Invoice/PO/GR quantity side by
side with a per-item Match/Mismatch pill (reusing the existing
`row-mismatch`/`row-quantity-alert`/`pill-match`/`pill-differ` CSS
classes — no new color language introduced). New TS helpers
`lineItemRowClass()`/`lineItemPillClass()`/`lineItemPillIcon()`/
`lineItemPillText()`, parameterized by `'po'|'gr'` side rather than
duplicated per side. A `missing_on_po`/`missing_on_gr` item shows
"⚠ Missing on PO"/"⚠ Missing on GR" in place of the pill+quantity, using
the existing `pill-differ` (red) styling. The document-level summary
rows (Vendor/PO Ref/Amount/Doc No) are UNCHANGED, per the request.

Why: line-item-level matching is what "audit-grade" 3-way matching
  actually requires — the whole point of a 3-way match is verifying that
  what was ordered, delivered, and billed agree PER ITEM, not just in
  aggregate (which, as the request notes, is exactly the kind of check a
  single-total or summed-quantity comparison cannot catch: two
  completely different item breakdowns can sum to the same total).

Testing (all offline, no live Gemini/network call):
  - `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on every changed backend
    file — compiles clean.
  - Direct test of `_extract_all_line_items()` against a realistic
    3-item document (qty 5000/8000/600, matching the request's example)
    — confirmed all 3 items extract with correct description/quantity/
    unit_price/amount, in order.
  - New test (scratchpad, not committed) of `_match_line_items()`/
    `_build_comparison()` via a mocked cursor covering exactly the 3
    requested scenarios: (1) all 3 items match -> `line_items_match`
    True, `overall_status` PASS; (2) item B's GR quantity is short
    (8000 ordered/received per invoice+PO, 7500 actually received) ->
    that item's `quantity_match` False, `line_items_match` False,
    `overall_status` FAIL (line-item quantity mismatch is a hard
    failure); (3) item C is on the invoice but was never ordered on the
    PO (and never received on the GR) -> `missing_on_po`/`missing_on_gr`
    both True, invoice_quantity still shown (600), po/gr_quantity None,
    `overall_status` FAIL ("critical audit finding" per the request).
    Also verified: item A (unaffected in scenarios 2/3) still correctly
    shows Match; a PO uploaded but with 0 extracted line items does NOT
    flood every invoice item as "missing" (the defensive guard);
    item_code-based matching takes priority over description even when
    descriptions differ (OCR wording); a genuinely clean single-item
    record still shows PASS (the fix doesn't make PASS unreachable).
  - Full browser-level verification with Playwright against the live
    dev server (scratchpad, not committed, screenshot taken and visually
    reviewed): the exact 3-item scenario above rendered end-to-end
    through a fully-mocked `/auditor/record/1/comparison` response (no
    real backend call, network fully intercepted) — confirmed the
    banner reads "Mismatch Detected" (red), the Line Items section
    header shows "(3)", no standalone "Item / Description"/bare
    "Quantity" rows remain, item A shows green Match pills with no
    row-mismatch styling, item B shows red `row-mismatch`+`row-quantity-
    alert` styling with both 8000 and 7500 visible, and item C shows
    "Missing on PO"/"Missing on GR" with its invoice quantity (600)
    still visible. A second, separate Playwright run specifically
    targeted the amount-mismatch-visibility bug found above: a
    REVIEW-only scenario (quantity matches, amount doesn't) — confirmed
    the banner reads "Review Required", the row gets `row-mismatch`
    WITHOUT `row-quantity-alert`, and the "💲 Amount/unit price differs"
    note is visibly present — closing the gap before this was ever
    treated as done.
  - Re-ran all six pre-existing offline test suites from prior entries
    — all still pass, no regression from the new extraction/matching
    logic sharing the same per-line loops and _build_comparison()
    query path.
  - `npx ng build --configuration=development` — passes clean both
    before and after the amount-mismatch-visibility fix.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend AND frontend TOGETHER — the frontend's
     Line Items section depends on the backend's new `comparison.
     line_items` array and `match_result.line_items_match`/
     `line_items_price_match` fields being present in the API response;
     the old fields it used to read (`item_match`/single `quantity`)
     are still returned but no longer drive what's displayed.
  2. The `document_line_items` migration runs automatically at startup
     (same as every other `_ensure_` function in this repo) — no manual
     SQL needed, but it only takes effect after the backend redeploys.
  3. Existing invoice/PO/GR records uploaded before this deploy have NO
     rows in `document_line_items` yet — their Line Items section will
     show "No line items extracted" until they're re-uploaded or
     Re-checked (Re-check re-runs the merged Gemini call, which now
     also returns `line_items`, but does not currently re-save them to
     `document_line_items` — that path only writes on upload; flagging
     this as a known gap for a follow-up if backfilling old records via
     Re-check turns out to matter).

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
2026-07-19 - Fix line-item matching failing to pair identical items
             extracted in different formats, producing duplicated
             "Missing on X" rows for the same real product

Root cause: the SAME product was extracted with a DIFFERENT item_code/
  description shape depending on which extraction path ran for each
  document — e.g. invoice: item_code="SLT-MOS-N60R", description="MOSFET
  N-Ch 600V TO-220" (code split out); PO/GR: item_code=null,
  description="SLT-MOS-N60R MOSFET N-Ch 600V TO-220" (code left inline).
  The previous entry's matching key was pure dict lookup (item_code if
  present, ELSE the RAW normalized description) — since the two sides'
  descriptions were literally different strings ("MOSFET N-Ch 600V
  TO-220" vs "SLT-MOS-N60R MOSFET N-Ch 600V TO-220"), they never
  produced the same key and were treated as two unrelated items, each
  reported as "Missing on X" on the document that had the OTHER format
  — a 4-item matched set rendered as "Line Items (8)".

FIX 1 — normalize item_code/description consistently at the SOURCE
(helpers/ocr_helper.py, routes/documents.py):
  - New `split_item_code_prefix()`: splits a leading item-code-shaped
    token off a description (requires a hyphen AND a digit in the
    token, e.g. "SLT-MOS-N60R", "MTC-IND-4R7M" — deliberately narrower
    than "starts with a hyphenated word", which would false-split an
    ordinary hyphenated product name like "Heavy-Duty Bracket").
  - New `normalize_line_item_code()`: applies that split uniformly to
    ONE line item dict — if item_code is already set (e.g. Gemini split
    it out itself) and description ALSO still starts with that same
    code (Gemini put it in both places on some rows), the duplicate is
    stripped from description too, so the displayed label is never
    "SLT-MOS-N60R MOSFET N-Ch 600V TO-220" when item_code is already
    "SLT-MOS-N60R" — the "one consistent label" part of the request.
  - Wired into `routes/documents.py`'s `_sanitize_line_items()` — the
    single choke point BOTH the regex fallback's and Gemini's
    line_items already pass through before persistence (established in
    the previous entry), so this one change point covers every
    extraction path × every document type without duplicating the
    logic three times.
  - Strengthened the shared `LINE_ITEMS_NOTE` Gemini prompt (used by
    all three of invoice/PO/GR) to explicitly instruct splitting a
    leading code token EITHER from a real separate code column OR from
    a single combined description cell, consistently across every row
    and every document type — reduces how often Gemini produces the
    inconsistent shape in the first place, though the ingestion-side
    fix above is what actually GUARANTEES consistency regardless of
    what Gemini does.

FIX 2 — make matching robust regardless of format, as defense-in-depth
(routes/auditor.py): the ingestion-side fix only helps NEW uploads —
records already in `document_line_items` from before this fix keep
their old inconsistent shape, so matching itself also needed to be
resilient:
  - Replaced the old pure-dict-key matching (`_line_item_key`) with
    `_line_item_tokens()` + `_find_line_item_match()`: for each
    candidate pairing, tries (in order) exact item_code match, exact
    normalized-description match, then a CONTAINMENT check (one
    normalized description contains the other — guarded to require at
    least 6 characters on each side, so short descriptions can't
    trivially "contain" everything). Description-based matching now
    also runs `split_item_code_prefix()` on-the-fly before comparing —
    "SLT-MOS-N60R MOSFET N-Ch 600V TO-220" and "MOSFET N-Ch 600V
    TO-220" reduce to the same comparison key even if neither side was
    ever normalized at ingestion (e.g. old data).
  - `_match_line_items()` rewritten around this: invoice items are
    matched first against not-yet-used PO/GR items (greedy, first-fit),
    then leftover PO-only items are matched against remaining GR items,
    then leftover GR-only items form their own rows — same
    invoice-then-PO-only-then-GR-only row ordering as before.
  - Canonical label selection: a matched row's displayed description/
    item_code now prefers whichever side ALREADY has item_code split
    out (the "clean" representation) over a side that still has it
    inline, rather than an arbitrary "whichever document happened to be
    checked first" pick — directly serves the "one consistent label,
    not two different formats" part of the request even for legacy
    unnormalized data.
  - Bug found and fixed while implementing this: a line item present on
    PO/GR but with NO invoice counterpart at all (e.g. a PO item that
    was included as a leftover, unmatched row) was previously never
    flagged as a hard mismatch — `missing_on_po`/`missing_on_gr` are
    computed as "this document exists but doesn't have this item",
    which is FALSE for an item that DOES exist on that same document (a
    PO-only row's `po_item` is, by definition, present). Added a new
    `missing_on_invoice` field (`True` when a row has no invoice-side
    item) and included it in `has_hard_mismatch` — the "PO item never
    received"/"invoice bills an item never ordered" cases from the
    original request were both about items missing FROM the invoice's
    perspective, but a PO/GR-originated extra item is symmetrically
    just as real a finding and wasn't being caught.

FRONTEND: the Invoice column's "Missing on Invoice" marker now reads the
new explicit `missing_on_invoice` field instead of inferring it from
`invoice_quantity === null` (the same signal, but explicit rather than
implied — and now also correctly drives the row's hard-mismatch styling
via the backend fix above, which the implicit check never did).

Why: line-item matching is only useful if it actually recognizes the
  same product across independently-extracted documents — an extraction-
  format inconsistency that makes every real match look like two missing
  items is worse than not having line-item matching at all, since it
  actively misleads the auditor into thinking documents disagree about
  more items than they actually do.

Testing (all offline, no live Gemini/network/DB call):
  - `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on every changed backend
    file — compiles clean. `npx ng build --configuration=development` —
    passes clean.
  - New test (scratchpad, not committed) covering, in order:
    (1) `split_item_code_prefix()`/`normalize_line_item_code()` directly
    — confirmed a real code prefix splits correctly, a plain description
    with no hyphen is left alone, and a hyphenated word with NO digit
    ("Heavy-Duty Bracket") is correctly NOT split (guards against false
    positives); confirmed a Gemini-already-split item and a regex-inline
    item for the SAME product normalize to the IDENTICAL shape.
    (2) `_sanitize_line_items()` directly against a raw, format-
    inconsistent 2-item Gemini-shaped list — confirmed both items end up
    with the same item_code/description shape.
    (3) THE exact reported bug, end-to-end through `_build_comparison()`:
    a 4-item set where invoice items are given as description-without-
    code + separate item_code (simulating Gemini's split behavior) and
    PO/GR items are given as "CODE description" in one string with
    item_code null (simulating the regex fallback/inconsistent Gemini
    behavior) — confirmed exactly 4 rows (not 8), and that the format
    inconsistency doesn't mask or fabricate findings: item 1 (fully
    matching across all 3 documents) correctly shows `quantity_match`
    True and neither missing flag; item 2's GENUINE short-receipt (5000
    ordered/invoiced, 4800 actually received) still correctly shows
    `quantity_match` False with the real 4800 figure visible; item 3
    (fully matching) shows True; item 4 (genuinely never ordered on the
    PO nor received on the GR — on the invoice only) correctly shows
    both `missing_on_po` and `missing_on_gr` True with its invoice
    quantity (600) still visible; `overall_status` is FAIL (driven by
    the two genuine issues, not the four format-inconsistent items that
    are NOT flagged as mismatched). Also confirmed the displayed
    description for the paired item has the code prefix stripped (one
    consistent label), not "SLT-MOS-N60R MOSFET N-Ch 600V TO-220" with
    the code duplicated in the text.
  - Full browser-level Playwright verification against the live dev
    server (scratchpad, not committed, screenshots taken and visually
    reviewed): a PO-only item with no invoice counterpart at all —
    confirmed the row gets `row-mismatch` + `row-quantity-alert` styling
    and visibly shows "Missing on Invoice", and the banner correctly
    reads "Mismatch Detected" (closing the `missing_on_invoice` gap
    found while implementing FIX 2, before treating it as done).
  - Re-ran all seven pre-existing offline test suites from prior
    entries — all still pass, no regression from the rewritten matching
    logic or the new normalization step.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render backend AND frontend together — the frontend's
     `missing_on_invoice` field read depends on the backend actually
     returning it.
  2. Existing `document_line_items` rows from before this fix keep their
     original inconsistent item_code/description shape (this fix
     doesn't retroactively rewrite stored data) — FIX 2's robust
     matching (description-stripping + containment fallback) is what
     makes those existing records match correctly without needing a
     re-upload; only NEWLY uploaded/re-checked documents get the

Date: 2026-07-19
What was changed:
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — colour palette + hover micro-interactions only:
    - Added a design-token palette (--bg-app, --bg-card, --bg-hover,
      --bg-active, --border, --border-hover, --text-primary,
      --text-secondary, --text-muted, --accent, --accent-soft,
      --accent-glow, --accent-bg, --success/-bg, --warning/-bg,
      --danger/-bg) to src/styles.css :root, moving the app from a
      light theme to a dark one (#0D0E15 app background, #6C4FFF violet
      accent).
    - Swept all 17 component .css files (~5400 lines), replacing every
      hardcoded hex/rgba colour with the matching token: old blue
      accent (#4A90D9/#1A5FAB) -> --accent, old grays/whites -> the new
      bg/text/border tokens, old green/amber/red status colours ->
      --success/--warning/--danger (kept strictly semantic, never
      reused for --accent). Old rgba() tints (e.g.
      rgba(220,38,38,0.15)) were converted to
      color-mix(in srgb, var(--token) N%, transparent) since a CSS
      variable holding a full colour can't be split into rgba()'s
      separate R/G/B arguments.
    - Kept the uploaded-document viewing surfaces on a WHITE/paper
      background as required: .image-panel (authenticity detail) and
      .modal-box (record detail's PDF quick-view), plus their direct
      children (.image-hint, .image-fallback, .legend,
      .modal-body, .modal-spinner-wrap, .modal-error-wrap) — these sit
      on the white surface, not app chrome, so they kept their original
      light-appropriate colours instead of the dark tokens. Everything
      surrounding them (headers, footers, buttons) follows the dark
      theme normally.
    - Added hover micro-interactions to existing elements only (no
      markup/layout changes): sidebar nav items translateX(5px) +
      background lift; cards/tiles translateY(-4px) + accent-glow
      shadow (card "border" hover implemented as an inset box-shadow
      ring rather than a literal `border` property, since
      box-sizing:border-box isn't applied everywhere and a real border
      would have shifted layout size); table/list rows
      translateX(3px) + background lift; buttons and filter pills get
      a `transition: all .2s ease` background lift. All motion wrapped
      in `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)`.
    - Fixed along the way (all pre-existing bugs surfaced by the dark
      background, not introduced by it):
        - Several status boxes had their border mapped to the same
          token as their background (e.g. success background + success
          background border), making 1px borders invisible; borders now
          use the solid status token instead of the `-bg` tint.
        - Three "combined selector, hover" CSS rules
          (auditor-dashboard, finance-ocr-review, finance-upload) were
          malformed as `.a, .b:hover { ... }`, applying the hover style
          to `.a` unconditionally; fixed to `.a:hover, .b:hover`.
        - `.note-input` (record detail's Remarks textarea) and
          `.date-range input[type="date"]` (report page) never had an
          explicit `background` — invisible on the old white theme,
          rendered as a jarring white box on the new dark one. Both now
          set `background: var(--bg-hover)`; the date input also gets
          `color-scheme: dark` so its native calendar popup matches.
        - ~50 usages of `color: var(--accent)` as small (11-15px) text
          only reached 3.2-3.9:1 contrast against the dark backgrounds
          (fails WCAG AA 4.5:1 for normal text). Swapped to the lighter
          `--accent-soft` (#8B72FF, 4.5-5.5:1) everywhere except
          `.brand-title` (32px/700 heading), which legitimately passes
          the 3:1 large-text threshold at full accent strength.

Why:
  Visual refresh requested: swap the light theme for a dark violet-accented
  one and add hover motion, with an explicit constraint to touch colour and
  hover state only — no layout, spacing, font, border-radius, markup, route,
  or logic changes, and the uploaded document image/PDF viewers must stay a
  white "paper" background so real documents and their overlay markers don't
  look wrong or lose contrast.

Testing:
  - `npx ng build --configuration=development` after each major batch of
    changes and once more as the final check — all passed cleanly, no
    template/markup touched.
  - Grep-based verification that no component .css file contains a raw hex
    value outside the deliberately-exempted white document-panel selectors
    (.image-panel/.image-hint/.image-fallback/.legend/.modal-box/
    .modal-body/.modal-spinner-wrap/.modal-error-wrap), each confirmed via
    file inspection to be within the exempted zone.
  - Computed WCAG relative-luminance contrast ratios (official formula) for
    every text/background token pairing and every `color: var(--accent)`
    usage; fixed the ~50 failing cases as described above.
  - Live Playwright verification against the running dev server (all
    backend calls intercepted/mocked, no real network calls): login,
    auditor dashboard (including nav-item and stat-card hover states
    captured mid-transition), record detail, exceptions, finance home, and
    finance upload pages — confirmed dark theme renders correctly, hover
    motion works, and caught the `.note-input` missing-background bug
    (which static analysis alone had missed) before it shipped.

Date: 2026-07-20
What was changed:
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — icon containers + icon set only, no
  layout/spacing/logic changes:
    - Fix 1 (icon container colour): the metric-card icon badges in
      finance-home, finance-report, and finance-ocr-review used bright
      pastel fills (e.g. background #EBF4FF with a dark-stroke icon) —
      these read as glaring white/pastel blocks against the dark theme.
      Replaced everywhere with the standard dark-UI treatment:
      `background: color-mix(in srgb, <colour> 12%, transparent)`,
      `border/box-shadow: 1px solid color-mix(in srgb, <colour> 25%,
      transparent)`, `color: <colour>` for a bright icon. Mapped by card
      meaning (primary -> --accent/--accent-soft, success -> --success,
      warning -> --warning, danger -> --danger), status colours kept
      strictly semantic. finance-home/finance-report drove their badge
      colour via an inline `--card-color`/`--card-bg` custom property
      pair set directly in the HTML template (hardcoded hex, missed by
      the previous restyle's CSS-file-only sweep) — switched
      `--card-color` to reference the design tokens and dropped the now
      -unused `--card-bg`. Also applied the same badge treatment to
      auditor-report's stat-icon (previously a semi-transparent white
      overlay on a coloured card — the same "bright block" bug) and to
      finance-ocr-review's/finance-upload's icon containers that had no
      badge at all before, for consistency across every metric card in
      the app.
    - Fix 2 (icon set): added the Phosphor Icons web font
      (@phosphor-icons/web, duotone weight primary, regular as fallback
      for the couple of icons with no duotone glyph) via
      node_modules-referenced entries in angular.json's global `styles`
      array (self-contained, no CDN). Replaced every icon usage across
      all 17 components — emoji glyphs (✅❌⚠️🚨📊🤖💡🛡️ etc.) and
      hand-rolled inline `<svg>` line icons alike — with
      `<i class="ph-duotone ph-{name}">` tags of matching size and
      colour, keeping the same semantic meaning for each (e.g. ✅ ->
      ph-check-circle, 🚨 -> ph-siren, the sidebar nav icons, form-field
      icons, table status markers, empty-state illustrations). Icon
      colour comes from the existing `color`/`currentColor` mechanism
      already in place, or an explicit design-token colour matching the
      icon's semantic role. TS helper methods that previously returned
      an emoji string for a computed icon (severityIcon, typeIcon,
      uploadSourceIcon, getBannerIcon, matchPillIcon, rowMatchIcon,
      lineItemPillIcon, actionLabel/Icon, getPOStatusIcon/getGRStatusIcon,
      etc.) now return a Phosphor class name instead, with the template
      rendering `<i class="ph-duotone" [ngClass]="...">` — same
      conditional logic, only the icon representation changed. Kept
      plain typographic characters (→ ← em dashes) that are page
      furniture rather than dedicated icon elements as-is.
    - Card hover "border" treatment (from the previous restyle) already
      used `box-shadow: 0 0 0 1px ...` instead of a literal `border` to
      avoid a box-model size shift where `box-sizing: border-box` isn't
      globally applied; applied the same discipline here — two files
      (finance-ocr-review, finance-upload) don't have that global reset,
      so their new icon-container "border" is a `box-shadow` ring
      instead of a literal `border`, to avoid growing those fixed-size
      icon boxes by 2px. Files that already have the reset (auditor-
      report, finance-home, finance-report) use a literal `border`
      safely.
    - Left untouched, deliberately: plain colour dots with no glyph
      (stat-dot, legend-swatch, feature-item dot — not icons), and a
      handful of pre-existing raw-hex TEXT colours unrelated to any icon
      (e.g. the "No GR"/"No PO" labels on the auditor dashboard, the
      upload-queue message column) — out of scope for this icon-and-
      container-colour-only pass.

Why:

Date: 2026-07-21
What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Authentication module upgraded from a
  4-signal Gemini-only checklist to an AI-powered visual verification
  engine (Claude Vision primary, Gemini fallback):
    - helpers/claude_extractor.py: added CLAUDE_AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT and
      analyze_document_authenticity(image, document_type) — a separate
      Claude Vision call (not OCR) that identifies the true supplier
      (ignoring Bill To/Ship To/Buyer), normalizes OCR-typo'd supplier
      names, and detects company logo/name/supplier address/stamp/
      signature each with confidence + a bounding box, plus a
      tampering/integrity risk assessment (LOW/MEDIUM/HIGH, never
      declares a document "fake"). Same fail-soft contract as the
      existing extract_with_claude() (returns None on any failure).
    - helpers/authenticity_check.py: rewrote run_authenticity_check() to
      call Claude first, fall back to the existing Gemini
      AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT if Claude fails, and fall back to the existing
      OCR-text heuristic as a last resort. Added
      _normalize_visual_result() so both engines' output lands in ONE
      unified schema (new _flatten_boxes() converts it into a named
      [{name,x,y,width,height}] list for the frontend overlay).
      stamp_required is derived from helpers/auth_rules.py's existing
      per-document-type config rather than asked of the model. Dropped
      the now-unused precomputed_result/skip_gemini parameters (the
      "reuse extraction's Gemini call" optimization no longer applies —
      see below).
    - app.py: added _ensure_authenticity_v3_columns() (ai_engine_used,
      ai_visual_result, document_consistency, risk_level, boxes — all
      new, purely additive columns on authenticity_checks).
    - routes/documents.py: REMOVED the 3 automatic run_authenticity_check
      calls from the invoice/PO/GR upload endpoints. The authentication
      check is now on-demand only (see below) — upload cost/latency and
      the extraction pipeline itself are completely unchanged.
    - routes/authenticity.py: GET /authenticity/<id> now runs the check
      on-demand the first time a document is viewed (instead of 404ing),
      mirroring the existing lazy PNG-render pattern used by
      GET /authenticity/<id>/image. Both this route and
      POST /authenticity/<id>/recheck now compute a "Document Consistency"
      result (vendor/PO-reference/line-items/amount match) by reusing the
      EXISTING 3-way matching engine (routes/auditor.py::_build_comparison,
      already used by the record-detail comparison view) rather than
      asking Claude to reason across Invoice/PO/GR itself.
    - tests/extraction/test_authenticity_ai.py (new): schema-
      normalization, box-flattening, and Claude-primary/Gemini-fallback/
      OCR-fallback engine-selection tests — no real API calls, no real
      DB writes (fake DB connection + monkey-patched call functions).
      Wired into tests/extraction/run_all.py.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — auditor-authenticity-detail component
  only:
    - New named-box overlay with a 5-color legend (Blue=Supplier Logo,
      Green=Company Name, Purple=Supplier Address, Red=Stamp/Chop,
      Orange=Signature) and a [Label] tag on each box, driven by the
      new check.boxes field.
    - Click a "Visual Evidence" row in the sidebar to highlight
      (pulse-outline) its matching box on the document image.
    - New 4-section results dashboard (Supplier Identity / Document
      Consistency / Visual Evidence / Integrity Risk) reading
      check.ai_visual_result / check.document_consistency.
    - The OLD 4-marker overlay and 4-signal checklist are kept as a
      fallback and still render exactly as before for any document that
      hasn't been re-checked yet under the new engine
      (check.ai_visual_result is null) — nothing breaks for existing
      authenticity_checks rows until they're re-checked.

Why:
  The Authentication page only checked 4 fixed booleans (chop/logo/
  name/signature) via a single Gemini prompt — too shallow for
  enterprise AP audit: it couldn't tell which party was the actual
  supplier (vs. Bill To/Ship To noise), couldn't cross-check Invoice/PO/
  GR consistency, couldn't flag tampering, and only ever returned 4
  fixed bounding boxes. Requested upgrade to an AI-powered verification
  system built on the same Claude-primary/Gemini-fallback pattern
  already used for field extraction. Per explicit direction, the new
  (heavier) check runs on-demand only rather than automatically at
  upload time, so upload cost/latency is unaffected and the existing
  Claude/Gemini extraction pipeline, OCR, and matching engine are
  completely untouched.

Testing:

    Anthropic/Gemini API calls (Claude/Gemini call functions and the DB

    — confirms _ensure_authenticity_v3_columns() runs cleanly alongside
    every existing migration; verified the 5 new columns exist via a
    direct information_schema query.
  - `git diff --stat -- routes/documents.py` reviewed line-by-line —
    confirms ONLY the 3 authenticity call sites were removed; extraction,

    zero diff on helpers/gemini_extractor.py, extraction_engine.py,
    ocr_helper.py, entity_normalizer.py, extraction_validator.py,
    gemini_cache.py, claude_cache.py, ai_extractor_router.py, and
    routes/matching.py.
  - `npx ng build --configuration development` — builds cleanly with no
    TypeScript/template errors.

Date: 2026-07-21
What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Authenticity Vision Accuracy Upgrade v2,
  three fixes to the AI Authentication engine added earlier the same day
  (Claude Vision primary, Gemini fallback):
    - routes/authenticity.py: FIX for "only Invoice shows up on the
      Authenticity page". Root cause found by reading the code (not
      assumed): the only frontend call to GET /authenticity/<id> is
      Record Detail's warning banner, and it never passes
      document_type — so PO/GR were simply never requested, on-demand
      or otherwise; no DB column was missing. Added
      _ensure_sibling_checks(document_id, primary_type), called at the
      end of GET /authenticity/<id>: for whichever of the OTHER two
      document types (of the same document_id) don't have a row yet and
      do have an uploaded file, it opportunistically runs the same
      Claude/Gemini engine for them too. Opening a record's Record
      Detail page once now produces independent Invoice + PO + GR
      authenticity_checks rows instead of only Invoice. Best-effort: a
      sibling failure is logged and never breaks the primary response.
      POST /authenticity/<id>/recheck is unchanged (still scoped to the
      one type the auditor explicitly re-checks).
    - helpers/claude_extractor.py: rewrote CLAUDE_AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT's
      bounding-box instructions with explicit per-category include/
      exclude rules (using the reported wrong/correct Coilcraft
      examples) — company_logo boxes must no longer include the company
      name/address, company_name boxes must no longer include ATTN/
      address/Ship To/Bill To lines, stamp boxes must no longer include
      nearby handwriting or table contents. Schema also gained:
      supplier_identity.status (verified/not_found/uncertain, replacing
      a bare boolean), each document_visual_evidence.<key>.status
      (detected/not_detected), and integrity_check became 3 independent
      risk axes (copy_paste_risk/font_consistency/alteration_risk, each
      low/medium/high) + a reason string, replacing the old flat
      boolean-flag list.
    - helpers/authenticity_check.py: _normalize_visual_result now maps
      either engine's output onto the v2 schema above (defensively
      still accepts a legacy boolean `detected` if a cached/older
      response used the pre-v2 shape) and adds a `required` flag per
      evidence key — signature is NEVER required (a missing signature
      on a computer-generated invoice must not read as a false
      negative), stamp requiredness still comes from the existing
      per-doc-type AUTH_RULES config. _flatten_boxes' output shape
      changed from {name,x,y,width,height} to
      {type,label,x,y,width,height,confidence} — `type` is a stable
      machine key (supplier_logo/company_name/supplier_address/
      company_stamp/signature) for the frontend to key color/click-
      highlight off of, `confidence` is normalized from Claude's 0-100
      scale to 0-1.
    - tests/extraction/test_authenticity_ai.py: updated for the v2
      schema (status enums, required flags, 3-axis integrity, new box
      shape) plus a case proving the legacy-boolean defensive fallback.
      New tests/extraction/test_authenticity_siblings.py: proves
      _ensure_sibling_checks checks a missing sibling with an uploaded
      file, skips one that's already checked, skips one with no file at
      all, checks both siblings in one call, and never lets a sibling
      failure propagate. Both wired into run_all.py.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — auditor-authenticity-detail component
  only:
    - Box overlay/color-legend/click-highlight now keyed by the stable
      `type` machine key instead of the display label string (so
      relabeling never silently breaks the color mapping).
    - Visual Evidence rows show a neutral "Not required" state (no red
      X) instead of a false-negative-looking "Not Detected" whenever
      the signal isn't expected for this document type (signature
      always; stamp depending on document type).
    - Supplier Identity section adds a Verified/Uncertain/Not Found
      status badge.
    - Integrity Risk section replaced the old boolean flag list with
      the 3 independent low/medium/high risk axes (copy/paste, font
      consistency, alteration) plus the AI's stated reason.

Why:
  Using the Authentication module surfaced 3 concrete problems: (1)
  uploading an Invoice+PO+GR only ever produced an Invoice authenticity
  result — traced to a genuine trigger-discoverability bug, not a
  schema gap; (2) Claude's bounding boxes were too loose, e.g. the
  "Supplier Logo" box also covering the company name and address; (3)
  a missing signature rendered identically to every other "not
  detected" signal even though most AP documents are legitimately
  unsigned, reading as a false negative to the auditor. Fixed all three
  without touching Claude/Gemini field extraction, OCR, the matching
  engine, 3-way matching, or the extraction database schema, per
  explicit instruction — only the Authenticity module's own files
  changed.

Testing:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 9 suites pass (7 prior +
    the updated test_authenticity_ai.py + new
    test_authenticity_siblings.py), zero real Anthropic/Gemini API

  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — no new migration
    this time (every column objective 1 asked for already existed from

  - Full end-to-end proof against the REAL dev Postgres DB (only the

    ai_visual_result/ai_engine_used/risk_level/box count) — then

  - `git diff --stat` confirmed zero changes to routes/documents.py,
    routes/auditor.py (matching engine), routes/matching.py,
    helpers/gemini_extractor.py, extraction_engine.py, ocr_helper.py,
    entity_normalizer.py, and app.py.
  - `npx ng build --configuration development` — builds cleanly.

      Coilcraft issues, Coilcraft's letterhead is the supplier and a
      "Ship To: EMITS..." block is only the receiving party), stricter
      per-category box exclusion rules (logo: no name/address/reg
      number; company name: no ATTN/address/Ship To/Bill To; address:
      never the Bill To/Ship To address; stamp: no printed "CHP" text,
      item codes, or handwritten AP notes), and a per-detection
      `label`/`reason` pair so every finding states what it saw and
      why. analyze_document_authenticity() gained an
      extracted_vendor_name parameter — the already-extracted
      vendor_name is passed to Claude as a hint ("verify, don't blindly
      trust") via a templated prompt section.
    - helpers/authenticity_check.py: added _resolve_supplier_status(),
      which cross-checks Claude's visually-detected supplier_name
      against the vendor_name the (separate) extraction pipeline
      already found, using the existing entity_normalizer.
      is_same_company() fuzzy matcher (already trusted for Invoice/PO/
      GR vendor matching elsewhere) — a match promotes supplier_identity
      to "verified" with vendor_name_matches_extraction=true; a mismatch
      surfaces as "uncertain" instead of silently trusting either source
      alone. _flatten_boxes() now carries `label`/`reason` through to
      the stored `boxes` column. run_authenticity_check() gained
      extracted_vendor_name (passed through) and use_cache (default
      True) parameters, and now checks/populates the new authenticity
      cache before calling Claude/Gemini, logging AUTH CACHE HIT / AUTH
      CACHE MISS.
    - helpers/authenticity_cache.py (new): DB-backed cache for the
      authenticity engine's raw output, keyed by (file_hash,
      document_type, authenticity_version) — mirrors helpers/
      claude_cache.py's pattern. Caches the RAW engine output, not the
      final normalized result, so a later extraction correction doesn't
      require invalidating it; only successful Claude/Gemini results are
      cached, never the OCR-text-only fallback.
    - app.py: added _ensure_authenticity_result_cache_table() (new
      authenticity_result_cache table, additive only).
    - routes/authenticity.py: added _extracted_vendor_name_for() (looks
      up the already-extracted vendor_name for a document_id/type) and
      threads it into all 3 run_authenticity_check() call sites (GET
      on-demand, sibling checks, recheck). POST /recheck passes
      use_cache=False — an explicit re-check must always be a fresh,
      live look, never served from cache.
    - tests/extraction/test_authenticity_ai.py /
      test_authenticity_siblings.py: updated for the new schema fields
      (label/reason, vendor cross-check) and extended with cache-hit /
      cache-miss / fallback-never-cached / use_cache=False test cases.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — auditor-authenticity-detail component
  only: shows each Visual Evidence row's `reason` as italic subtext, and
  a Supplier Identity match note ("Matches extracted vendor ..." /
  "Differs from extracted vendor ... — worth a second look") driven by
  the new vendor_name_matches_extraction field.

Why:
  Real testing surfaced two accuracy problems (Claude sometimes
  misclassified the BUYER's name/logo as supplier evidence, e.g. an
  EMITS-issued PO; bounding boxes were still catching adjacent
  text/whitespace) and a cost concern (every authenticity check — even
  of a document already analyzed — spent a live Claude/Gemini call).
  Fixed the accuracy problems with an explicit prompt rewrite plus a
  server-side cross-check against data the app already has (the
  extraction pipeline's vendor_name), and fixed the cost concern with a
  file-hash cache that a Re-check deliberately bypasses. Per explicit
  instruction, extraction and the matching engine are completely
  untouched — only the Authenticity module's own files changed.

Testing:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 9 suites pass, zero real
    Anthropic/Gemini API calls (mocked).
  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — confirms the new
    authenticity_result_cache table migrates cleanly.
  - Full end-to-end proof against the REAL dev Postgres DB (only the
    Claude call mocked): created a synthetic document_id with an
    Invoice (extracted vendor_name deliberately OCR-noisy,
    "COLCRAFT SINGAPORE PTE LTD") and a PO. Confirmed: (1) 3 Claude
    calls total for 3 distinct document_type checks (invoice + its 2
    siblings); (2) re-viewing the SAME invoice logged "AUTH CACHE HIT"
    and did NOT trigger a 4th Claude call; (3) the vendor cross-check
    correctly matched the noisy extracted name against Claude's clean
    "COILCRAFT SINGAPORE PTE LTD" at 97.3% similarity, setting
    vendor_name_matches_extraction=true; (4) every stored box carried
    type/label/reason/confidence. Then deleted every synthetic row.
  - `git diff --stat` / targeted diffs confirmed zero changes to
    routes/documents.py, routes/auditor.py, routes/matching.py,

Date: 2026-07-21

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Authenticity Vision v4: upgrades the
  Authenticity module from a visual-detection tool into an auditor
  decision engine:
    - helpers/claude_extractor.py: bumped
      CLAUDE_AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT_VERSION to 'v4'. Added a 4th integrity
      axis, alignment_consistency (abnormal spacing/misalignment
      suggesting a re-typed/inserted field, distinct from font
      mismatches), and reinforced "do not mark a normal scanned document
      as suspicious for ordinary scan noise/skew alone". Constrained the
      stamp's `type` field to an enum (company_chop / received_stamp /
      qc_stamp / approval_stamp / "" for not-detected) instead of free
      text, with explicit classification instructions.
    - helpers/authenticity_check.py: added
      _compute_auditor_score(visual) — a deterministic, explainable 0-100
      authenticity_score computed SERVER-SIDE from already-detected
      signals (not self-reported by Claude — an LLM's own numeric rating
      isn't reliably consistent enough to build an audit decision on,
      whereas a fixed formula is deterministic, free, and testable).
      Composition: supplier identity (0-40) + weighted required visual
      evidence (0-30, a key not required for this document type is
      excluded from both earned points and the max) + integrity
      (0-30, penalized per risk axis) + a signature-detected bonus
      (+5, never a penalty — signature stays always-optional). Derives
      risk_level and an APPROVE (>=85) / REVIEW (60-84) / REJECT (<60)
      decision with a one-line reason, plus itemized +/- reason bullets.
      Stored inside ai_visual_result.auditor_score at check time (no
      schema change) and now SUPERSEDES Claude's own self-reported
      risk_level for the stored `risk_level` column, so what's on disk
      matches what the auditor sees. _flatten_boxes() now includes
      stamp_type on the stamp box entry.
    - routes/authenticity.py: added
      _cross_document_authenticity_for(cursor, document_id) — v4's Cross
      Document Authenticity (objective 3). Computed FRESH at read time
      (never stored — it depends on sibling documents that can be
      re-checked independently after this was last computed), reusing
      EXISTING engines rather than re-implementing cross-document
      reasoning: supplier identity across Invoice/PO/GR is compared via
      routes/auditor.py's _vendor_match_all() (the same fuzzy, OCR-typo-
      tolerant comparator already trusted for vendor matching
      elsewhere); document number references, item consistency, and
      date-order ("Timeline") reuse _build_comparison() — the same
      3-way matching engine already powering the Record Detail Field
      Comparison table. Returns {cross_document_score, issues} or None
      until at least 2 document types have been checked. Attached to
      both GET /authenticity/<id> and POST /authenticity/<id>/recheck
      responses as a new `cross_document_authenticity` field.
    - tests/extraction/test_authenticity_scoring.py (new): covers the
      score engine's APPROVE/REVIEW/REJECT bands, the "not-required
      evidence is excluded from the denominator, not penalized" rule,
      and the cross-document function's 2-type minimum, matching
      suppliers, mismatched suppliers, and reference-number-mismatch
      cases. Wired into run_all.py.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — auditor-authenticity-detail component
  only:
    - "Integrity Risk" section renamed "Document Integrity", now shows
      the 4th Alignment Consistency axis.
    - Stamp/Chop evidence row shows its classified type (e.g. "Stamp /
      Chop — Received Stamp").
    - New "Cross Document Verification" section: cross_document_score
      plus a plain-language issues list (or "No cross-document issues
      found").
    - New "Final Risk Assessment" section: the authenticity_score (with
      color-coded value), an APPROVE/REVIEW/REJECT decision badge, the
      one-line decision reason, and the full +/- reasons list.

Why:
  The prior rounds could detect and locate evidence but gave an auditor
  no single number or recommendation to act on, no way to see whether a
  stamp was a real chop vs. a QC/received/approval stamp, and no way to
  check Invoice/PO/GR consistency beyond the existing raw match/mismatch
  booleans. This round turns the detected signals into an actual
  decision (score + APPROVE/REVIEW/REJECT + reasons an auditor can read
  in seconds), reusing the app's existing matching/fuzzy-comparison
  engines wherever possible instead of asking Claude to do cross-
  document reasoning it has no reliable way to verify. Per explicit
  instruction, extraction and the matching engine are untouched — only
  the Authenticity module's own files changed (confirmed via
  `git diff --stat` showing zero changes to routes/documents.py,
  routes/auditor.py, routes/matching.py, the extractor helpers, and
  app.py).

Testing:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 10 suites pass (9 prior +
    the new test_authenticity_scoring.py), zero real Anthropic/Gemini
    API calls.
  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — no new migration
    this round (auditor_score lives inside the existing ai_visual_result
    JSONB column).
  - Full end-to-end proof against the REAL dev Postgres DB (only the
    Claude call mocked): created a synthetic document_id with an Invoice
    (Coilcraft) and a PO whose OWN letterhead is EMITS (the buyer) but
    whose extracted vendor_name field was deliberately set to "EMITS
    TECHNOLOGY SDN BHD" to simulate a plausible extraction bug. Result:
    Claude correctly resolved the true supplier as Coilcraft on every
    document (buyer/supplier fix from the prior round holding up), so
    Cross Document Verification correctly scored 100/no issues across
    all three — while the PO's OWN per-document score dropped to
    75/REVIEW ("Supplier identity uncertain") specifically because that
    document's extracted vendor_name (EMITS) disagreed with what Claude
    saw (Coilcraft) — two distinct signals, both behaving correctly.
    Invoice/GR both scored 100/APPROVE with their RECEIVED stamp
    correctly classified as stamp_type='received_stamp'. Then deleted
    every synthetic row.
  - `npx ng build --configuration development` — builds cleanly.
  - Real-document verification against the actual Coilcraft/EMITS PDFs
    (score accuracy, stamp classification) needs a live
    ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, not present in this sandbox — same disclosed
