Date: 2026-07-21

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) only — Authenticity Vision v5 Precision
  Improvement, tightening real-world accuracy issues found on actual
  Coilcraft documents. No frontend changes this round (explicitly out
  of scope per the request):
    - helpers/claude_extractor.py: bumped CLAUDE_AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT_
      VERSION to 'v5'. The prompt is no longer document-type-agnostic —
      analyze_document_authenticity() now injects a
      {document_type_block} tailored to what's being analyzed:
        * Invoice: unchanged — the supplier issues an invoice, so its
          own letterhead is normally the supplier.
        * PO / GR (new): both are normally issued by the BUYER (a PO by
          the buyer ordering; a GR by the buyer's own receiving desk),
          so their own letterhead is the BUYER, not the supplier. Added
          an explicit priority order for finding the real supplier on
          these two types: (1) an explicit "Supplier Address"/"Vendor
          Address" section, (2) an explicit "Supplier:"/"Vendor:" name
          field, (3) the extraction hint cross-checked against a visible
          supplier field, (4) a supplier logo ONLY if distinct from the
          buyer's own header logo. This directly fixes the reported
          issue where a PO/GR's prominent buyer letterhead (e.g. "EMITS
          TECHNOLOGY SDN BHD") could get misread as the supplier.
      Also tightened company_name box rules to max 1-2 lines excluding
      ATTN/address/phone/email/any buyer info (previously it could drift
      into grabbing the whole header block); reinforced logo/stamp
      tightness wording; every evidence `reason` must now explain WHY
      something belongs to supplier evidence, not just describe it;
      added `source_section` to the supplier_address schema entry
      ("supplier_address_label" / "near_supplier_name" / "").
    - helpers/authenticity_check.py: _normalize_visual_result() carries
      `source_section` through for both engines (Claude's own value, or
      "" for Gemini/fallback which have no per-instance labeling).
      _flatten_boxes() exposes it on the supplier_address box entry too.
    - routes/authenticity.py: SEPARATED the PO->GR->Invoice date
      sequence out of cross_document_score entirely — it's a workflow-
      timing signal, not an authenticity/tampering signal, and blending
      it in meant a 100% genuine, fully-verified document set could
      still score lower for an unrelated timing quirk (e.g. an invoice
      billed before goods were logged as received). Added
      _workflow_consistency_for(cursor, document_id), returning its own
      {workflow_consistency_score, issues} — reuses the existing
      date_order_valid check from _build_comparison() rather than
      recomputing it. Both GET /authenticity/<id> and POST recheck
      responses now include a `workflow_consistency` field alongside
      the (now date-free) `cross_document_authenticity`.
    - tests: extended test_authenticity_ai.py (source_section
      normalization on both engines, document-type-block prompt
      injection, stamp_type box passthrough) and test_authenticity_
      scoring.py (cross_document_score no longer moves on date order;
      new _workflow_consistency_for cases for valid/invalid/not-
      applicable date sequences).

Why:
  Real testing against actual Coilcraft Invoice/PO/GR documents
  surfaced two precision problems: (1) the company_name box sometimes
  captured the whole header block (name + ATTN + buyer info) instead of
  just the legal name line, and supplier_address detection had no way
  to say WHERE it found the address or reject a Ship To/Delivery
  Address masquerading as one; (2) more importantly, the prior prompt
  treated "letterhead = supplier" as a universal rule, which is only
  true for Invoices — a PO/GR's own letterhead is normally the BUYER,
  so a prominent buyer logo (EMITS) could get misclassified as the
  supplier on those two document types specifically. Also, blending the
  PO->GR->Invoice date sequence into cross_document_score conflated two
  unrelated questions ("is this genuine and internally consistent?" vs
  "did the workflow happen in the expected order?"), so they're now
  reported separately. Per explicit instruction, extraction, Gemini
  routing, matching, the database schema, and the frontend layout are
  all untouched — only the Authenticity module's prompt/normalization/
  scoring files changed.

Testing:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 10 suites pass, zero
    real Anthropic/Gemini API calls.
  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — no schema change
    this round, confirmed clean boot.
  - Full end-to-end proof against the REAL dev Postgres DB (only the
    Claude call mocked): confirmed the document_type_block actually
    differs by type — direct inspection of
    _DOCUMENT_TYPE_GUIDANCE['po'/'gr'] contains the priority-order list,
    _DOCUMENT_TYPE_GUIDANCE['invoice'] does not; confirmed
    source_section flows correctly from the mocked Claude response
    through both the stored ai_visual_result and the flattened boxes
    column for all three document types; confirmed
    cross_document_authenticity and workflow_consistency are returned
    as independent fields that don't influence each other.
  - `git diff --stat` confirmed ZERO changes to any file under
    auditlens-frontend/, plus zero changes to routes/documents.py,
    routes/auditor.py, routes/matching.py, the extraction helpers,
    entity_normalizer.py, auth_rules.py, and app.py (no new migration).
  - Real box-tightness/supplier-resolution verification against the
    actual Coilcraft/EMITS PDFs needs a live ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, not
    present in this sandbox — same disclosed caveat as every prior
    round; for the user to verify post-deploy.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND only — no new migration, no frontend
     changes this round.

Date: 2026-07-21

What was changed:
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) only — auditor-authenticity-detail.
  component.ts: fixed the bounding-box overlay coordinate math for
  check.boxes (the newer Claude-generated evidence boxes). The
  component was scaling box x/y/width/height by
  renderedSize/1000 (treating them as 0-1000-normalized, matching what
  the Claude prompt asks for), but confirmed against real production
  data that Claude does not reliably follow that normalization
  instruction — the stored values are actually native pixel coordinates
  matching the rendered PNG's real dimensions. recomputeMarkers() now
  reads img.naturalWidth/naturalHeight (available once the <img> 'load'
  event fires) and scales with scaleX = displayWidth/naturalWidth (and
  the Y equivalent), instead of dividing by a hardcoded 1000. Added
  temporary "AUTH BBOX DEBUG" console logging (naturalWidth/
  naturalHeight/displayWidth/displayHeight/originalBBox/scaledBBox) per
  box to make the actual scale visually verifiable against a real
  document. The LEGACY overlay (check.signal_boxes, from the older
  Gemini-only AUTHENTICITY_PROMPT path) is untouched — Gemini's vision
  API does reliably honor 0-1000 normalization, so that path still
  scales by renderedSize/1000 as before.

Why:
  Auditors reported logo/stamp/supplier-address boxes appearing
  shifted, oversized, or in the wrong location on real Coilcraft
  documents, despite the backend's stored box data looking individually
  reasonable. Root-caused (with the user's confirmation, since this
  sandbox has no real authenticity_checks data to verify against) to a
  coordinate-system mismatch: the frontend assumed 0-1000-normalized
  values per the prompt's own instructions, but Claude's actual returned
  coordinates are native-pixel. No backend, extraction, OCR, matching,
  or database changes — this was purely a frontend coordinate-scaling
  bug, confirmed via code inspection (no AI calls made in the process).

Testing:
  - `npx ng build --configuration development` — builds cleanly.
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 10 suites still pass
    (backend untouched, so this just confirms no accidental collateral
    change); zero real Anthropic/Gemini API calls made anywhere in this
    task, no documents uploaded, no AI credits spent.
  - `git diff --stat` confirmed zero changes under auditlens-backend/ —
    exactly one file changed, the frontend component.
  - Live rendering verification against a real checked document (to
    confirm boxes now align pixel-for-pixel) requires the user's actual
    environment with real authenticity_checks data, not available in
    this sandbox; the temporary AUTH BBOX DEBUG console logs are there
    specifically to make that verification quick — safe to remove once
    confirmed.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render FRONTEND only.
  2. No new environment variables, no backend redeploy needed.

Date: 2026-07-21

What was changed:
  AuditLens Authenticity BBox Root-Cause Verification + Deterministic
  Fix. Backend (helpers/authenticity_check.py only) + frontend
  (auditor-authenticity-detail component only):
    - NEW canonical coordinate contract. Every evidence box's `boxes`
      field is now {coordinate_space: "normalized_0_1", x, y, width,
      height, source_image_width, source_image_height,
      localization_quality, raw_bbox, raw_coordinate_space} — computed
      by the new _normalize_box_to_unit_space(), which auto-DETECTS
      (not guesses) whether Claude's raw [ymin,xmin,ymax,xmax] output
      is 0-1000-normalized or native-pixel: a 0-1000-normalized value
      can never legitimately exceed ~1000, so any coordinate above that
      is a hard logical proof it's native-pixel, regardless of what the
      prompt asked for. Requires the EXACT pixel dimensions of the image
      Claude/Gemini actually analyzed — new _get_image_dimensions()
      reads them straight from the PNG bytes via PyMuPDF (already a
      project dependency; imported fresh in this file only, gemini_
      extractor.py untouched). _flatten_boxes() no longer does any
      coordinate math itself, only labeling — there is exactly one
      place coordinate normalization logic lives now.
    - NEW localization_quality ("exact"/"approximate"/"unreliable"),
      derived from the engine's own per-box confidence, so a genuine
      RENDERING bug (fixed by this canonical contract) is never
      conflated with genuine AI LOCALIZATION imprecision (a real but
      different problem the frontend now surfaces honestly instead of
      silently drawing a misleading rectangle).
    - company_logo is now OPTIONAL (not required) on PO/GR in
      _required_for() — a PO/GR's own letterhead is normally the BUYER
      (already established by the v5 prompt fix), so there's usually no
      distinct supplier logo to show at all; this no longer reads as a
      hard authenticity failure when supplier name/address are already
      verified.
    - Frontend: single convertBBoxToDisplay(box, img) function (now
      exported + unit-tested) replaces the previous single hardcoded
      native-pixel assumption — supports normalized_0_1 (canonical),
      normalized_0_1000 (Gemini legacy), and native_pixels (backward-
      compatible fallback for any row saved before coordinate_space
      existed at all). "approximate" boxes render dashed with an
      "Approximate AI area" label; "unreliable" boxes are never drawn as
      a rectangle — the sidebar shows "Detected, exact location
      unavailable" instead. Evidence labels are now document-type-aware
      ("Supplier Logo (Optional)" on PO/GR, "Receiving / QC Stamp" on
      GR). Renamed the prior "AUTH BBOX DEBUG" console log to the
      requested "AUTH BBOX TRACE" shape (documentType/evidenceType/
      coordinateSpace/source+natural+client dimensions/rawBBox/
      normalizedBBox/renderedBBox) — still temporary/development-only.

Why:
  The prior round's native-pixel fix improved alignment but left two
  real gaps: (1) the codebase still asserted "0-1000 normalized" in the
  prompt/comments while the frontend silently assumed native-pixel —
  an unresolved contradiction with no way to tell, from the stored data
  alone, which convention a given box actually used; (2) a PO/GR with no
  distinct supplier logo (the normal case, since PO/GR letterheads are
  the buyer) was scored as a hard authenticity failure. This round
  replaces the assumption with a self-describing, auto-detected
  contract every box carries with it, and separates "we don't know
  where this is" (localization_quality) from "we know exactly where
  this is" so the UI never overstates its own confidence.

Testing:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 10 backend suites pass;
    zero real Anthropic/Gemini API calls anywhere (all mocked/static
    fixtures), zero AI credits consumed, no authenticity endpoint
    invoked, no Re-check triggered, no documents uploaded.
  - New backend tests: coordinate-space auto-detection (both branches:
    values that stay ≤1050 vs. values that exceed it), clamping,
    missing-source-dimensions handling, localization_quality thresholds,
    _get_image_dimensions against a real (synthetically constructed)
    PNG plus graceful failure on garbage bytes, company_logo optional on
    PO/GR, and a full run_authenticity_check() end-to-end pass using
    real PNG bytes (not mocked dimensions) proving the whole pipeline
    measures the image and stores canonical boxes correctly together.
  - New frontend tests (auditor-authenticity-detail.component.spec.ts,
    `ng test`): all 3 coordinate spaces, the legacy-row backward-compat
    fallback, zero-dimension guarding, and correct scaling across a
    responsive resize — 6/6 pass. (One PRE-EXISTING, unrelated failure
    in app.spec.ts confirmed via `git diff` — zero changes to that file
    — a stale scaffold title assertion, not touched.)
  - `npx ng build --configuration production` — clean build (pre-
    existing bundle-size budget warnings only, unrelated to this
    change).
  - `git diff --stat` confirmed zero changes to routes/documents.py,
    routes/auditor.py, routes/matching.py, helpers/gemini_extractor.py,
    extraction_engine.py, ocr_helper.py, entity_normalizer.py,
    auth_rules.py, and app.py (no new migration — everything lives
    inside the existing `boxes`/`ai_visual_result` JSONB columns).
  - IMPORTANT DISCLOSURE: this sandbox's database has zero real
    authenticity_checks rows, zero cached authenticity images, and the
    three real Coilcraft/EMITS PDFs referenced mid-task did not reach
    this environment's filesystem (confirmed via repo-wide search) — so
    the root-cause table and this fix could not be cross-checked against
    the user's actual production screenshots/documents. The fix is
    grounded in direct source-code inspection, the PRIOR round's
    user-confirmed real-world finding (native-pixel, not 0-1000), and
    a hard logical constraint (values >1000 cannot be 0-1000-normalized)
    — not a guess — but real-document verification is still needed
    post-deploy.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND — no new migration, just updated
     normalization code.
  2. Redeploy the Render FRONTEND — picks up the new conversion function
     and quality-aware rendering.

  4. After deploy: open an authenticity detail page for a real Invoice/
     PO/GR, check the browser console's AUTH BBOX TRACE output against
     the visible box position, and confirm boxes now land tightly on
     the actual logo/name/stamp — then remove the temporary trace log.

    - Replaced the box overlay with four evidence-summary sections

      call-shape changes): Supplier Identity (name/address verified +
      an explicit Extracted Vendor Match row), Document Evidence
      (renamed from "Visual Evidence"; rows and wording now vary by
      document_type — Invoice shows Supplier Branding/Logo, Received
      Stamp, Signature; PO shows Buyer/Issuer Letterhead, Supplier
      Information Present, Supplier Logo (Optional); GR adds a QC/
      Receiving Stamp row), Document Consistency (unchanged — reads the
      existing matching-engine output), and Integrity Review (renamed
      from "Document Integrity"; unchanged fields — Copy/Paste Risk,
      Font Consistency, Alignment Consistency, Alteration Risk, AI
      reasoning).
    - New status vocabulary for evidence rows: 'yes' (green — detected/
      matched), 'na' (grey — optional/not required/not applicable),
      'warn' (amber — required signal not found, needs a human look),
      'no' (red — reserved for genuine contradictions only: a vendor-
      name mismatch against extraction, or a document-consistency
      mismatch). Previously, any required-but-undetected evidence
      (e.g. a missing stamp) rendered as a red X — now it renders amber
      "Needs Review" instead, since absence alone isn't proof of fraud.
      A missing supplier logo on PO/GR still never renders red (it's
      backend-flagged optional there already); a missing signature
      still never renders red (backend never requires it) — both now
      show the same neutral grey "Not Required"/"Optional" treatment.
    - Added a Final Recommendation section: the existing authenticity
      score/decision (APPROVE/REVIEW/REJECT) and risk level, plus an
      explicit disclaimer line ("AI-assisted assessment. The system
      found no obvious visual alteration. Final decision remains with
      the auditor.") so the UI never implies the AI has proven a
      document genuine.
    - Document preview: the full document image is still shown at full
      size, just without overlay rectangles, click-to-highlight, or a
      color legend — the auditor inspects the whole document directly.
    - Deleted auditor-authenticity-detail.component.spec.ts (its only
      tests were for convertBBoxToDisplay(), which no longer exists).
  Untouched, confirmed via `git diff --stat`: every file under
  auditlens-backend/ (Claude extraction, Gemini fallback, OCR, matching
  engine, three-way matching, authenticity AI analysis) and all other
  frontend files — this was a display-layer simplification of one
  component only. No `authenticity_checks` rows, `boxes`/
  `ai_visual_result` JSONB content, or any other existing database
  record was modified or deleted.

Why:
  The bbox overlay remained inaccurate even after the coordinate-space
  contract fix, and precise visual localization isn't required for the
  FYP's objective — a reliable AI-assisted evidence review page that an
  auditor can trust is more valuable than an imprecise rectangle on top
  of the document.

Date: 2026-07-21
What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - New table `send_back_cycles` (app.py::_ensure_send_back_cycles_
      table(), same idempotent auto-create-on-startup pattern as every
      other table in this repo — CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS, no
      migration runner) — ONE ROW PER SEND-BACK CYCLE, never a single
      mutable reason overwritten in place. Columns: cycle_number,
      return_reason_category, reason_other_note, auditor_instruction,
      required_actions (JSONB array), required_action_other_note,
      priority, response_due_date, sent_back_by/sent_back_at,
      finance_response, finance_responded_by/finance_responded_at,
      resubmitted_by/resubmitted_at, cycle_status (action_required ->
      resubmitted -> resolved), resolution (approved | returned_again),
      resolved_at. Documentation-only mirror added at migrations/2026-
      07-21_create_send_back_cycles_table.sql (force-added past the
      repo's `*.sql` gitignore rule, matching how every prior dated
      migration file in that directory was already tracked).
      documents.status keeps its EXISTING values (under_review/
      returned/resubmitted/approved/...) completely unchanged — no
      existing dashboard count, filter, or report was touched.
    - New helpers/send_back.py: pure validation/derivation functions,
      no DB/Flask/AI — validate_send_back_payload() (reason category,
      instruction, required_actions shape, priority, due-date-not-
      before-today, "other" requires a note, due date required for
      high priority), validate_finance_response_payload(),
      compute_activity_summary() ("Changes Since Send Back" — reports
      an activity ONLY when a real stored timestamp — extracted_
      fields.edited_at / purchase_orders.uploaded_at / goods_receipts.
      uploaded_at — is strictly after the cycle's sent_back_at, never a
      fabricated field-level diff, since no field-history/versioning
      table exists), is_overdue().
    - routes/reviews.py extended (no new parallel routes for the core
      transitions — the existing endpoints now own the richer
      behavior):
        - POST /reviews/return/<id>: accepts the new structured
          payload (reason_category, instruction, required_actions[],
          priority, due_date) and creates a send_back_cycles row; if
          the document already has a prior cycle (a repeat send-back
          after Finance responded), that prior cycle is marked resolved
          (resolution='returned_again') — never overwritten. The OLD
          {"remarks": "..."} payload shape still works exactly as
          before for backward compatibility (no cycle row is created
          for it, since there's no structured data to store).
        - POST /reviews/resubmit/<id>: when the document has an open
          cycle, a written Finance response is now REQUIRED and is
          saved onto that cycle (finance_response/finance_responded_by/
          finance_responded_at/resubmitted_by/resubmitted_at,
          cycle_status -> 'resubmitted'). Documents returned before this
          feature existed (no cycle row) fall back to the original
          optional-remarks behavior.
        - POST /reviews/approve/<id>: if the document has a cycle in
          'resubmitted' state, it's marked resolved
          (resolution='approved').
        - NEW: GET /reviews/send-back-cycles/<id> — every cycle ever
          created for the document, oldest first (full history,
          nothing dropped), each annotated with `activity_summary` and
          `is_overdue`.
    - tests/reviews/ (new): test_send_back_validation.py (17 pure
      unit-test cases for helpers/send_back.py — no Flask, no DB) and
      test_send_back_routes.py (10 cases against a REAL Flask test
      client + REAL JWT machinery hitting the REAL route functions, but
      a fully in-memory fake DB — role restrictions, invalid status
      transitions, missing-field/invalid-due-date rejection, the full
      send-back -> response -> resubmit -> approve happy path, MULTIPLE
      send-back cycles preserving prior cycle data unmodified, and the
      legacy remarks-only payload still working). Both added to
      tests/extraction/run_all.py's suite list so `python tests/
      extraction/run_all.py` runs everything in one command, matching
      this repo's existing convention.
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts/.html/.css: the old one-click
      "Send Back" (returnDocument(), an immediate POST with just a free-
      text note) is replaced by a modal (openSendBackModal() /
      submitSendBack()) collecting Return Reason Category, a required
      Auditor Instruction textarea, one-or-more Required Actions
      (checkboxes), Priority, and a Response Due Date — validated
      client-side via the exported pure function validateSendBackForm()
      (instruction required, ≥1 required action, due date not before
      today, "Other" requires an explanation, high priority requires a
      due date) before the network call, with the backend re-validating
      the same rules authoritatively. The button relabels itself "Send
      Back Again" once the record already has at least one prior cycle.
      Added a "Finance Response" panel (shown once the latest cycle has
      one) displaying the original reason/instruction, priority/due
      date/overdue state, Finance's response, and "Changes Since Send
      Back" (the cycle's activity_summary — real recorded activity
      only). Added a "History" timeline rendered directly from
      review_records (GET /reviews/history/<id>, already existed
      server-side but was never called from this page) — the EXISTING
      audit-log system, reused as-is rather than building a second
      competing log, so multiple send-back/resubmit/approve cycles all
      show correctly with no merging logic needed.
    - finance-ocr-review.component.ts/.html/.css: added a "Returned for
      Correction" section (reusing the existing document list/edit/
      resubmit flow — no separate document editor was built) showing
      every invoice with status='returned'; selecting one now fetches
      and displays a "View Auditor Request" panel (return reason,
      instruction, required actions, priority, due date/overdue) via
      the same GET /reviews/send-back-cycles/<id> endpoint. Added a
      required "Finance Response" textarea — canSubmit()/
      submitToAuditor() now require and send it (POST /reviews/
      resubmit/<id> with {response: ...}) whenever the selected document
      was returned; first-time submissions are unaffected. "Upload
      Supporting Document" links to the existing /finance/upload page
      rather than a new upload mechanism (this repo's upload endpoints
      are scoped to Invoice/PO/GR, not arbitrary attachments — no new
      upload system was built, per the task's explicit instruction).
    - New auditor-record-detail.component.spec.ts (18 cases) and
      finance-ocr-review.component.spec.ts (9 cases) — every HTTP call
      mocked via HttpTestingController, no real backend, no AI calls.

  Untouched, confirmed via `git diff --stat`: Claude extraction, Gemini
  extraction, OCR, regex extraction, three-way matching (routes/
  matching.py, routes/auditor.py's _build_comparison/_classify_

  other extraction/matching/authenticity helper file. documents.status
  values are unchanged; no existing dashboard/filter/report logic that
  reads them was modified.

Why:
  The existing "Send Back" button changed status on a single click with
  only a free-text note, Finance saw a generic "Returned" badge with no
  context anywhere, and resubmission sent an empty body — there was no
  way for Finance to explain what they fixed, and repeated send-backs
  had no concept of a "cycle," so nothing distinguished attempt #1 from
  attempt #2 beyond raw chronological order.

Tests run and results:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py`: 9/12 suites PASS. The 3
    failures (test_authenticity_ai.py, test_authenticity_siblings.py,
    test_authenticity_scoring.py) are PRE-EXISTING and unrelated to
    this change — they fail on `import fitz` (PyMuPDF is not installed
    in this venv), confirmed via `git diff --stat` showing zero changes
    to helpers/authenticity_check.py or helpers/claude_extractor.py,
    the files those suites import. Both new suites (test_send_back_
    validation.py: 17 cases, test_send_back_routes.py: 10 cases) PASS.
  - `npx ng build --configuration production`: clean build (same pre-
    existing bundle-size budget warnings as before, unrelated to this
    change).
  - `npx ng test --watch=false`: 29/30 tests pass; the 1 failure is the
    same pre-existing, unrelated app.spec.ts issue confirmed via `git
    diff --stat` showing zero changes to that file across this entire
    session.
  - Zero Claude API calls, zero Gemini API calls — no code path in this
    change calls either engine; this is a status-transition/form/
    display feature over already-loaded document data only.

Assumptions / deliberate deviations from the task's "Possible API
behaviour" suggestions (all disclosed, with reasoning):
  - The task suggested a separate `POST /auditor/records/<id>/send-back`
    route; this extends the EXISTING `POST /reviews/return/<id>`
    instead, to avoid two endpoints racing to both flip documents.
    status='returned' and insert into review_records for the same
    action — a real correctness risk, and the kind of "second
    competing architecture" the task itself warns against for the
    audit log.
  - The task suggested a separate `POST /finance/records/<id>/response`
    endpoint distinct from resubmit; this repo's existing UI already
    combines "write a response" and "resubmit" into one button click,
    so the EXISTING `POST /reviews/resubmit/<id>` was extended to
    validate+save the response and resubmit in the same atomic request,
    rather than requiring two round-trips for one user action.
  - "In Correction" (one of the task's recommended cycle statuses) is
    not a distinct value cycle_status ever takes — no existing action
    in this app triggers a "Finance started but hasn't finished"
    transition. It's derivable on the frontend from real data (editFields
    changes / extracted_fields.edited_at) if ever needed, but wasn't
    added as a stored state to avoid inventing a transition with no
    real trigger.
  - The "Need Review" button in the auditor UI has no click handler and
    no backing endpoint (confirmed by inspection) — per the task's own
    "if already supported" qualifier for that action, it was left
    untouched rather than newly implemented.
  - Report & Log (auditor-report.component / finance-report.component)
    was not modified — review_records (which already powers GET
    /auditor/report/audit-trail) automatically gains the new cycles'
    entries with no changes needed there; the richer structured detail
    lives in the new record-detail History/Finance-Response panels
    instead, satisfying the acceptance criterion's "Report & Log OR the
    existing audit history" wording.

  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND — the new send_back_cycles table is
     created automatically on next boot (no manual migration step).
  2. Redeploy the Render FRONTEND.
  3. No new environment variables.
  4. After deploy: send a real record back with the new form, confirm
     it appears in Finance's "Returned for Correction" list with the
     correct reason/instruction, submit a Finance response and
     resubmit, and confirm the auditor sees the Finance Response panel
     and History timeline correctly on the next review.

Date: 2026-07-22
What was changed:
  Backend only (auditlens-backend/) — no frontend changes:
    - routes/authenticity.py: added generate_invoice_authenticity_if_
      missing(document_id, file_bytes, file_name) — a new function, NOT
      a new engine. It reuses the exact same pieces GET /authenticity/
      <id> already calls on-demand: SELECT 1 FROM authenticity_checks
      WHERE document_id=%s AND document_type='invoice' (the same
      UNIQUE(document_id, document_type) constraint the table already
      enforces) to decide skip-vs-run, then the EXISTING
      _document_consistency_for()/_extracted_vendor_name_for() helpers
      and the EXISTING helpers/authenticity_check.py::
      run_authenticity_check() (unchanged: Claude primary -> Gemini
      fallback -> OCR-text-only, unchanged AI provider selection,
      unchanged scoring). run_authenticity_check()'s own use_cache=True
      default means the existing authenticity_result_cache (file_hash +
      document_type + prompt version) is inherited automatically — no
      new cache was built. Never raises: every failure (DB error,
      engine error, missing dependency) is caught, logged via
      `print(...)`, and returns None.
    - routes/documents.py: added ONE new call site, immediately after
      the existing `run_anomaly_detection(document_id)` call in the
      invoice upload handler (upload_document()) — wrapped in the same
      try/except pattern already used for anomaly detection, so an
      authenticity failure can never break the upload response, exactly
      like an anomaly-detection failure already couldn't. Passes the
      SAME file_bytes_data/safe_name already in scope from the upload
      itself (no extra DB read). PO/GR upload handlers (upload_po/
      upload_gr) and the manual Re-check endpoint are UNTOUCHED — this
      only adds the invoice-at-upload trigger the bug report and task
      scope asked for.
    - tests/extraction/test_authenticity_auto_trigger.py (new, 6 cases,
      15 checks): missing row -> engine called exactly once with the
      right args; existing row -> engine is NEVER called (zero AI
      calls, proving the skip-regeneration guarantee); standalone
      invoice with document_consistency=None (no PO/GR) still triggers
      correctly; engine returning None doesn't raise; engine raising an
      exception is caught; the existence-check DB query itself failing
      is caught. Added to tests/extraction/run_all.py's suite list.
  Untouched, confirmed via `git diff --stat`: helpers/claude_extractor.
  py, helpers/gemini_extractor.py, helpers/ocr_helper.py, helpers/
  extraction_engine.py, helpers/extraction_validator.py, helpers/
  entity_normalizer.py, helpers/anomaly_detector.py, helpers/
  authenticity_check.py (the engine itself — its internal AI-provider
  selection, fallback order, and scoring rules are all unchanged),
  helpers/auth_rules.py, routes/matching.py, routes/auditor.py, and
  requirements.txt. No new AI provider, no new authenticity engine, no
  new cache.

Why:
  documents 68-74 (7 standalone invoices, no PO/GR) had successful
  extraction but zero authenticity_checks rows, because the engine only
  ran the first time an auditor happened to open that specific
  document's Record Detail page — a queue of freshly-uploaded, not-yet-
  opened invoices had no trigger event at all, so the Authenticity page
  looked artificially empty for them. This closes that gap by adding
  the missing trigger at the one point in the pipeline where it's
  actually known extraction just succeeded — without touching the
  engine, its cache, or its provider fallback order in any way.

Cache / repeated-call protection (API cost):
  1. Idempotency check first: `SELECT 1 FROM authenticity_checks WHERE
     document_id=%s AND document_type='invoice'` — if a row already
     exists, the function returns immediately with ZERO further queries
     and ZERO calls to run_authenticity_check(). This is enforced twice
     over: by this explicit check, AND independently by the table's own
     UNIQUE(document_id, document_type) constraint, so even a
     hypothetical race can't produce a duplicate row.
  2. The existing authenticity_result_cache (helpers/authenticity_
     cache.py, keyed by file_hash + document_type + prompt version) is
     inherited for free via run_authenticity_check()'s own
     use_cache=True default — nothing new was added to reuse it.
  3. Only ONE new call site exists (invoice upload), so a single upload
     can trigger at most one authenticity attempt for that document;
     nothing loops, retries, or polls. The frontend was not touched —
     no page-refresh or repeated-view call was added anywhere.

Tests run and results:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py`: 13/13 suites PASS, including
    all 3 that failed in the prior investigation session
    (test_authenticity_ai.py, test_authenticity_siblings.py,
    test_authenticity_scoring.py) — that failure was a missing local-
    venv dependency (PyMuPDF/`fitz`), not a code issue; installing the
    already-declared requirements.txt packages (psutil, PyMuPDF,
    google-genai, anthropic, etc. — all pre-existing entries, nothing
    added to requirements.txt) fixed the environment and confirmed

Date: 2026-07-22
What was changed:
  New module: "Audit Workflow Calendar" — a shared page for Auditor and
  Finance to track review deadlines, correction due dates, and follow-up
  tasks. Not a generic calendar clone: every event type except the new
  Manual Audit Task is computed live from data that already exists;
  nothing about extraction, matching, authenticity, anomaly detection,
  or the send-back workflow's own logic was touched.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - NEW table `calendar_tasks` — the ONLY new stored data this task
      adds (title, description, event_date, assigned_to, priority,
      status, created_by/created_at/updated_at). Added via app.py's
      established idempotent `_ensure_*()` auto-create-on-startup
      pattern (CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS — same as every other table
      in this repo; no migration runner exists here). Documentation-
      only mirror at migrations/2026-07-22_create_calendar_tasks_
      table.sql (force-added past the repo's `*.sql` gitignore rule,
      matching how send_back_cycles' migration file was already
      tracked the same way).
    - NEW helpers/calendar_events.py: pure functions only (no DB, no
      Flask, no AI) — validate_task_payload() (title/date required,
      priority from the SAME vocabulary already defined in helpers/
      send_back.py's PRIORITIES, imported not redefined) and two small
      shape-only converters, exception_to_calendar_event()/anomaly_to_
      calendar_event(), that reformat an ALREADY-CLASSIFIED exception/
      anomaly row into the calendar's common event shape — they don't
      detect or classify anything themselves.
    - NEW routes/calendar.py (new `calendar_bp`, registered at
      `/calendar`): GET /calendar/events aggregates four event types
      per role:
        - pending_review: read directly from documents.status IN
          (under_review, resubmitted) — same status set the existing
          review queue already uses.
        - finance_correction_due: read directly from the EXISTING
          send_back_cycles table (created in the prior send-back-
          workflow task) — reason/priority/due_date/status come
          straight from that table's own columns; "Overdue" vs
          "Awaiting Finance correction" reuses the EXISTING
          helpers/send_back.py::is_overdue(), not reimplemented.
        - exception_followup: imports and calls routes/auditor.py's
          EXISTING _build_comparison()/_classify_exception() — the
          exact same three-way-matching-derived exception
          classification the Exceptions page already uses (same
          import pattern routes/authenticity.py already uses for the
          same two functions). A classification of type 'sent_back' is
          skipped here since finance_correction_due already represents
          that same situation with far richer detail — avoids showing
          the same underlying issue twice.
        - anomaly_followup: read directly from the EXISTING `anomalies`
          table (status='pending'), the same rows GET /anomalies
          already returns.
        - manual_task: the one new data source, from calendar_tasks.
      Role scoping: Auditor sees all four types (system-wide) plus
      their own tasks; Finance Executive sees ONLY finance_correction_
      due for THEIR OWN uploaded documents (same ownership scoping
      GET /reviews/finance-dashboard already uses) plus their own
      tasks — no pending-review/exception/anomaly data, matching every
      other endpoint that already restricts those to auditors.
      Also added: GET /calendar/assignable-users (a minimal {user_id,
      full_name, role} list for auditor/finance_executive accounts
      only — deliberately NOT the admin-only GET /admin/users, to
      populate the "assigned user" dropdown without exposing full user
      management), POST /calendar/tasks (create), and PATCH /calendar/
      tasks/<id>/complete (only the task's assignee or creator may
      complete it).
    - app.py: registered calendar_bp and added the one new
      _ensure_calendar_tasks_table() call, alongside the existing
      _ensure_* calls — no existing migration function was touched.
    - tests/calendar/ (new): test_calendar_events_validation.py (10
      pure unit-test cases for helpers/calendar_events.py) and
      test_calendar_routes.py (10 cases against a REAL Flask test
      client + REAL JWT machinery hitting the REAL route functions, a
      fully in-memory fake DB — role restrictions for both endpoints,
      the full four-event-type aggregation for an auditor, the
      'sent_back' exception-exclusion rule, finance-role scoping
      producing zero pending_review/exception/anomaly events, task
      creation validation/defaulting, and the complete-task ownership
      check). Both added to tests/extraction/run_all.py's suite list.
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - NEW shared component src/app/calendar/calendar.component.ts/
      html/css — ONE component used by both /auditor/calendar and
      /finance/calendar (role read from localStorage, the same pattern
      the layouts already use), rather than building two near-
      identical calendar UIs. Monthly grid (42-cell, leading/trailing
      days from adjacent months grayed out), event chips color-coded
      ONLY by priority (normal/medium/high — a deliberately small,
      restrained palette; event TYPE is distinguished by icon instead,
      per the "avoid too many colours" requirement), a Day Events list
      for days with more than 3 events, an Event Detail modal
      (document/vendor/type/priority/description/status + a role- and
      type-aware "related action" button: Open Document / Review
      Correction / Correct Document / View Exception / Mark Complete),
      and a New Task modal (title/description/date/assigned
      user/priority) reusing the same dark modal styling family as the
      Send-Back modal on Record Detail. Shows "No scheduled audit
      activities" when a month has zero events, never fabricated data.
    - app.routes.ts: added `calendar` as a child route under BOTH
      `/auditor` and `/finance`, pointing at the same component.
    - auditor-layout / finance-layout (.ts + .html): added a
      "Calendar" nav item (auditor order: Home, Authenticity,
      Exceptions, Anomaly Detection, Calendar, Report & Log — exactly
      as requested; finance: Home, Upload, OCR Review, Calendar,
      Report) with a new calendar icon case in each layout's existing
      icon-switch template. No other nav items changed.
    - NEW calendar.component.spec.ts (15 cases) — every HTTP call
      mocked via HttpTestingController, no real backend, no AI calls.
      Covers: the local-timezone-safe date formatter (a regression
      guard against the classic Date.toISOString() UTC-shift bug), the
      42-cell grid generation, event-to-day grouping, task-form
      validation, task creation/completion payloads, and role-aware
      related-action routing (confirming a Finance user is never
      routed into an /auditor/* page, since this app has no route
      guard and the API itself would just 403 them there).
  Untouched, confirmed via `git diff --stat`: every extraction/matching/
  authenticity/anomaly-detection helper file, routes/matching.py,
  routes/anomalies.py, routes/authenticity.py, routes/documents.py, and
  the send-back workflow itself (routes/reviews.py, helpers/send_back.py
  — send_back_cycles is only READ from, via a plain SELECT, never
  written to by this task).

Why:
  There was no central place to see review deadlines, correction due
  dates, and follow-up tasks together — an auditor had to separately
  check the review queue, the Exceptions page, the Anomalies page, and
  each record's Send-Back history to piece together "what needs
  attention and by when," and Finance had no due-date view at all
  beyond the Returned-for-Correction list (which has no date grouping).

Data sources used (existing unless noted):
  - pending_review: documents.status (existing).
  - finance_correction_due: send_back_cycles (existing table, created
    in the prior send-back-workflow task) + helpers/send_back.py::
    is_overdue() (existing, reused).
  - exception_followup: routes/auditor.py::_build_comparison()/
    _classify_exception() (existing, imported and reused, not
    reimplemented).
  - anomaly_followup: the `anomalies` table (existing).
  - manual_task: calendar_tasks — the ONE new table this task adds.
  - assignable-user list: a new minimal query over the existing `users`
    table (role IN auditor/finance_executive only).

Tests run and results:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py`: 15/15 suites PASS (13
    pre-existing + 2 new calendar suites, 20 new checks/cases total).
  - `npx ng build --configuration production`: clean build (same
    pre-existing bundle-size budget warnings as before, unrelated).
  - `npx ng test --watch=false`: 42/43 tests pass (15 new calendar
    tests all pass); the 1 failure is the same pre-existing, unrelated
    app.spec.ts issue seen throughout this project's history — confirmed
    via `git diff --stat` showing zero changes to that file.
  - Zero Claude API calls, zero Gemini API calls, zero extraction
    triggered, zero anomalies generated — every backend test mocks
    get_db_connection/_build_comparison/_classify_exception/
    get_user_by_id; the calendar aggregates only pre-existing data, it
    never calls any AI helper or detection function.

Assumptions:
  - Exceptions/anomalies have no due-date column in this schema, so
    their calendar event is anchored on the date the signal was first
    raised (the document's uploaded_at / the anomaly's created_at) —
    labeled as "outstanding since," never presented as an invented
    deadline. Only finance_correction_due (send_back_cycles.response_
    due_date) is a genuine due date.
  - pending_review's calendar date is documents.updated_at (falls back
    to uploaded_at) — the date the record most recently became
    reviewable, which also correctly reflects a resubmission, not just
    the original upload.
  - Manual Audit Task intentionally has no document_id/link field — the
    task only listed title/description/date/assigned user/priority as
    fields, so no unrequested field was added.
  - A minimal "mark complete" endpoint was added beyond the literal
    "allow creating a task" ask, since a task that can never leave the
    calendar would make the feature unusable in practice; delete/edit
    were NOT added (not requested, kept to the smallest usable
    lifecycle: open -> done).

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Date: 2026-07-22
What was changed:
  Malaysia business-calendar awareness added to the existing Audit
  Workflow Calendar — presentation and date-calculation only. NOT a UI
  redesign: the monthly grid, event chips, modals, and every existing
  event source/query are untouched; this only ADDS holiday markers and
  a working-day deadline indicator on top of what already existed.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - NEW helpers/malaysia_calendar.py (pure functions only — no DB, no
      Flask, no AI calls):
        - Timezone: MALAYSIA_TZ is a fixed UTC+8 `timezone` offset, used
          instead of `zoneinfo.ZoneInfo('Asia/Kuala_Lumpur')` deliberately
          — Malaysia has had a single, unchanging UTC+8 offset with NO
          daylight saving since 1982, so the fixed offset is exactly
          equivalent for every date, past or future, with zero new
          dependency (zoneinfo needs the `tzdata` PyPI package on
          Windows dev machines; the fixed offset needs nothing extra
          and works identically on Render's Linux too).
        - Public holidays: `_fixed_holidays(year)` (New Year, Labour
          Day, Merdeka Day, Malaysia Day, Christmas — exact for any
          year) and `_rule_based_holidays(year)` (Yang di-Pertuan
          Agong's Birthday = first Monday of June, computed exactly via
          a day-of-week rule, not guessed) are precise for any year.
          `_MOVABLE_HOLIDAYS_BY_YEAR` (Chinese New Year, Hari Raya
          Aidilfitri, Hari Raya Haji, Wesak Day, Awal Muharram, Maulidur
          Rasul, Deepavali — Islamic/lunar-calendar dates) is populated
          for 2025-2027 as best-effort estimates ONLY, with a prominent
          module-docstring disclosure that these must be reconciled
          against the official JPA government gazette before being
          relied on for real compliance decisions — no movable holiday
          is ever fabricated for an unpopulated year (get_public_
          holidays() for e.g. 2040 returns only the 6 exact fixed/rule-
          based entries).
        - Working-day calculation: is_working_day() excludes Saturday,
          Sunday, AND any known public holiday. working_days_until()
          counts working days strictly after a start date up to and
          including an end date (never negative). deadline_status(due_
          date, today=malaysia_today()) returns {working_days, overdue}
          — read as "Due in N working days" (0 = due today) or "Overdue
          by N working days" — or None when no due date was ever set
          (never fabricates a deadline).
    - routes/calendar.py (additive edits only — see `git diff`, zero
      lines removed from any existing function):
        - _finance_correction_events(): added `event['deadline'] =
          deadline_status(row['response_due_date'])` — computed from
          the send-back cycle's REAL due-date column only, not the
          sent_back_at fallback already used for grid placement, so a
          cycle with no due date correctly gets deadline=None rather
          than an invented one.
        - _manual_task_events(): added `event['deadline'] =
          deadline_status(row['event_date'])` — calendar_tasks.
          event_date is NOT NULL, so every manual task has one; the
          frontend decides whether to still show it once a task is
          marked done.
        - get_calendar_events(): added a SEPARATE `holidays` array to
          the response (Malaysian public holidays within the requested
          start/end range) — never merged into the existing `events`
          array, so pending_review/exception_followup/anomaly_followup
          (which have no due-date concept) are completely untouched and
          the existing event shape/sources are unmodified.
    - tests/calendar/test_malaysia_calendar.py (new, 15 cases / 66
      checks): fixed-date holidays exact for any year, Agong's Birthday
      computed correctly as a rule (not guessed) across several years,
      movable holidays present only for populated years (nothing
      fabricated for e.g. 2040), Sat/Sun + public-holiday exclusion,
      working_days_until() across a weekend AND across a public
      holiday, deadline_status() for due-in-future/overdue/due-today/
      string-input/no-due-date cases, holiday range queries including a
      year-boundary span, and the fixed UTC+8 offset.
    - tests/calendar/test_calendar_routes.py: added cases for the new
      `holidays` field (present and correctly separate from `events`
      when start/end are given, empty when they're not) and for
      `deadline` being None on a finance-correction event that never
      had a due date set (nothing fabricated).
    - tests/extraction/run_all.py: registered the new suite.
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/src/app/calendar/):
    - calendar.component.ts: added `holidays: PublicHoliday[]` state
      (populated from the new `holidays` field in loadEvents()'s
      response), a `holiday` field on each DayCell (matched by ISO
      date), a `deadline?: DeadlineInfo | null` field on CalendarEvent,
      and three new small helpers — showDeadline() (hides the badge for
      an event type with no deadline, or a manual task already marked
      done), deadlineLabel() ("Due in N working days" / "Overdue by N
      working days" / "Due today", singular/plural handled), and
      deadlineClass() (ok/soon/overdue color bucket). No existing
      method, grid-generation logic, or interface field was changed.
    - calendar.component.html: day cells now show a small, non-
      clickable, distinctly-styled (italic, amber, flag icon) holiday
      label when `day.holiday` is set — structurally separate from the
      priority-colored event chips beneath it, never part of
      `day-events`, so it can never be mistaken for an audit workflow
      task. The Event Detail modal gained a deadline chip next to the
      existing date chip; the Day Events list modal gained a small
      deadline line under each row. No existing element was removed or
      restructured — the calendar's overall layout is unchanged.
    - calendar.component.css: added .day-cell-holiday/.holiday-label,
      .deadline-chip (+ ok/soon/overdue variants), and .day-event-
      deadline. No existing selector was modified.
    - calendar.component.spec.ts: added 5 cases — the `holidays` array
      is captured and correctly attached to the matching day (and NOT
      to a day with no holiday), deadlineLabel()'s three wordings
      (including the 1-vs-N-working-days plural), showDeadline() hiding
      the badge for a completed task and for event types with no
      deadline concept, and deadlineClass()'s urgency-bucket mapping.
  Untouched, confirmed via `git diff --stat`: app.py, helpers/send_
  back.py, helpers/calendar_events.py, every extraction/matching/
  authenticity/anomaly-detection helper and route file, routes/
  documents.py, routes/reviews.py (send-back workflow), routes/
  auditor.py, and both layout files — no existing calendar event source
  query, the send-back workflow, anomaly logic, authenticity logic, or
  matching logic was modified in any way.

Why:
  A due date shown only as a calendar date doesn't tell a Malaysian
  auditor or Finance user how much real working time is actually left —
  a "3 days" gap that includes a weekend and Merdeka Day is materially
  different from 3 working days. Public holidays also weren't visible
  on the calendar at all, so a task due "tomorrow" that happened to be
  Hari Raya could look identical to any other day until it was too late.

Tests run and results:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py`: 16/16 suites PASS (13 pre-
    existing + 3 calendar suites, 20 previously-added + 15 new cases /
    66 new checks for malaysia_calendar.py alone).
  - `npx ng build --configuration production`: clean build (same pre-
    existing bundle-size budget warnings as before, unrelated).
  - `npx ng test --watch=false`: 47/48 tests pass (20 calendar tests,
    5 of them new, all pass); the 1 failure is the same pre-existing,
    unrelated app.spec.ts issue — confirmed via `git diff --stat`
    showing zero changes to that file.
  - Zero Claude API calls, zero Gemini API calls, zero extraction
    triggered, zero anomalies generated, zero matching logic invoked —
    every backend test mocks get_db_connection/_build_comparison/
    _classify_exception/get_user_by_id; the new module makes no network
    call of any kind (holiday/working-day logic is pure date
    arithmetic).

Assumptions / disclosures:
  - Movable Islamic-calendar and lunar-calendar public holidays (Hari
    Raya Aidilfitri, Hari Raya Haji, Awal Muharram, Maulidur Rasul,
    Chinese New Year, Wesak Day, Deepavali) for 2025-2027 are best-
    effort estimates, NOT sourced from a live government feed (none was
    available to call, and Islamic dates are only officially confirmed
    close to the date via moon-sighting) — clearly disclosed in the
    module docstring and MUST be reconciled against the official
    Malaysian government public holiday gazette (JPA) before being
    relied on for real compliance/deadline decisions. Fixed-date and
    day-of-week-rule holidays are exact.
  - Only FEDERAL-level public holidays are included — state-specific
    holidays (e.g. Thaipusam, individual state rulers' birthdays) are
    out of scope, since they don't apply uniformly nationwide and this
    system has no per-user state setting to key them off.
  - No "holiday falls on a weekend -> day-in-lieu on the following
    Monday" substitution logic was added — Malaysia's actual
    substitution rules vary by holiday type and aren't uniformly
    documented, so guessing would risk being wrong; holidays are listed
    exactly on their gazetted date only.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND — no schema change, no migration, no
     new environment variables (pure-Python date logic only).
  2. Redeploy the Render FRONTEND.
  3. No config changes needed.
  4. Recommended before relying on this for real audit deadlines:
     verify the 2025-2027 movable-holiday dates in helpers/malaysia_
     calendar.py against the official JPA public holiday gazette and
     correct any that have since been officially confirmed differently.

          'missing_document' and requiredActions=['upload_missing_
          document'] when the record's issue is a missing-document
          case (still fully editable; send-back submit/validation
          logic untouched).
    - auditor-record-detail.component.html:
        - New "Exception Summary" card below the status banner
          (Issue / Risk / Impact / missing-document checklist), shown
          only when there's an actual exception (hidden for PASS).
        - New "Audit Impact" and "Suggested Action" boxes inside the
          decision card, above the existing Audit Note/Decision
          buttons — short static sentences derived from the same
          classification, reusing the existing .subsection-title style.
        - Replaced every "Not Uploaded" instance (column headers, PO/GR
          table cells, Source Documents button titles/filenames) with
          "Missing" + an "Awaiting Finance Submission" hint; swapped
          the misleading upload-arrow icon for an hourglass icon since
          these cells were never clickable/interactive.
        - Send Back modal: added a small context note ("Reason: Missing
          supporting documents" / "Required Action: Upload ...") above
          the existing form fields for the missing-document case only.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.css:
        - New styles for .exception-summary-card, .es-*, .risk-chip
          (+ high/medium/low variants mirroring the existing
          .priority-chip pattern), .audit-impact-box/.suggested-
          action-box (reusing the .finance-response-box visual
          language), .sb-context-note (accent-colored, distinct from
          the danger-colored .error-box).

Why:
  The Exception Investigation workflow (Record Detail page) worked
  correctly but made auditors re-derive the same information already
  visible in the Field Comparison table every time: what's actually
  wrong, how serious it is, why it blocks approval, and what to ask
  Finance for. This was a frontend-only, presentation-layer pass to
  surface that same data more directly — no redesign, no new backend
  endpoints, no AI calls, no changes to extraction/OCR/three-way
  matching/authenticity/anomaly detection/send-back backend logic or
  the database schema. Every new UI element reads only the
  `comparison` object the page already fetches via the existing
  GET /auditor/record/<id>/comparison call.

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — new files:
    - helpers/ai_assistant.py: prompt templates + Claude-primary/Gemini-
      fallback orchestration for the AI Audit Assistant. Text-only calls
      (no image) — reuses the same two providers already wired up
      elsewhere, never a new SDK or AI provider. Every prompt is
      instructed to use ONLY the case data it's given, never invent a
      fact, and never declare an approve/reject/fraud verdict (assistant,
      not decision-maker).
    - routes/ai_assistant.py: new blueprint, 5 auditor-only POST
      endpoints — /ai-assistant/<id>/explain-exception, /explain-risk,
      /generate-remark, /prepare-send-back, /ask. Builds a structured
      case-context object by REUSING routes/auditor.py's existing
      _build_comparison/_classify_exception (three-way matching +
      exception classification — imported, not duplicated or modified)
      plus read-only queries against authenticity_checks/anomalies/
      review_records. Every response is cached in a new ai_assistant_
      cache table, keyed by a hash of (document_id, action, full case
      data, question) — an unchanged case + the same button/question
      never re-spends a Claude/Gemini call. AI is called ONLY from these
      endpoints, i.e. only when the auditor clicks a button — nothing
      here runs automatically.
    - migrations/2026-07-22_create_ai_assistant_cache_table.sql:
      documentation-only copy of the table app.py creates automatically
      at startup (this repo has no migration runner).
    - tests/extraction/test_ai_assistant.py: 25 checks — Claude-success/
      Claude-fail-then-Gemini/both-fail provider fallback, markdown-
      fence stripping, send-back enum clamping (invalid/hallucinated AI
      output falls back to a safe default derived from the case's own
      exception classification), cache-key determinism, case-context
      field mapping, and cache-hit-vs-cache-miss behavior of
      _run_action. No real DB, no real Claude/Gemini calls — every
      external call is monkey-patched with fakes/stubs, same style as
      test_authenticity_siblings.py. Registered in tests/extraction/
      run_all.py.

Why:
  Auditors reviewing an exception case (missing documents, a matching
  mismatch, an authenticity/anomaly flag) had to manually re-read the
  Field Comparison table, authenticity result, and anomaly findings
  every time to write a remark or decide what to tell Finance. The AI
  Audit Assistant is a contextual helper — NOT a general chatbot, NOT a
  decision-maker — that summarizes and explains data AuditLens already
  computed, drafts text the auditor can edit, and pre-fills the
  existing Send Back form, while every actual audit decision (approve/
  send back/what to tell Finance) stays a manual auditor action.

Date: 2026-07-22 (later same day)

What was changed:
  Bug fix: the AI Audit Assistant was describing a fully clean record
  (three-way matching PASS, authenticity PASS, no missing documents, no
  unresolved send-back) as a failed/incomplete audit whenever ANY
  anomaly record existed for it — even a historical duplicate finding
  an auditor had already reviewed and dismissed. The AI was left to
  infer PASS-vs-REVIEW-REQUIRED itself from raw fields, so an unrelated
  anomaly row could tip a case summary or risk explanation toward
  "failed" language.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — no new files, no schema/cache-structure
  change (routes, table, hashing, hit/miss mechanics are all unchanged):
    - routes/ai_assistant.py:
        - New _classify_anomaly(anomaly): a DETERMINISTIC (not AI-
          judged) blocking-vs-informational classifier per each
          anomaly's own status/severity/type — "informational" once an
          auditor has reviewed/dismissed it, or a low/medium-severity
          round/weekend pattern; "blocking" only for a still-pending
          high-severity, duplicate, or amount-type finding. Each
          anomaly in the context now carries this as a `classification`
          field.
        - New _compute_audit_status(...): computes "PASS" only when
          three-way matching is PASS, authenticity has no warning, no
          PO/GR is missing, the document isn't currently sent back
          ('returned'), AND no anomaly is classified "blocking" —
          otherwise "REVIEW REQUIRED", with an explicit
          `audit_status_reasons` list naming exactly which condition(s)
          failed. _build_case_context now includes `audit_status` and
          `audit_status_reasons` in the context every AI prompt reads.
        - New _clamp_explain_exception_result(result, context): the
          actual fix, not just better prompt wording — the AI's own
          audit_status guess for the "Explain Exception" action is
          ALWAYS discarded and replaced with the deterministic
          context['audit_status'], so the label shown to the auditor
          can never be wrong regardless of what the AI narrates. Blank
          reason/recommended_action fall back to audit_status_reasons /
          a PASS-or-REVIEW-appropriate default sentence. Wired into
          _run_action the same way _clamp_send_back_result already is.
        - explain-exception's response shape changed from {"answer":
          "..."} to {"audit_status", "reason", "recommended_action"} —
          matching the task's required "Audit Status / Reason /
          Recommended Action" format.
    - helpers/ai_assistant.py:
        - _SYSTEM_PREAMBLE gained an "AUDIT STATUS INTERPRETATION
          RULES" section instructing every action to treat the case's
          already-computed audit_status/audit_status_reasons and each
          anomaly's classification as authoritative, describe a PASS
          case as "validated"/"passed core checks", and never describe
          an "informational" anomaly as a reason for REVIEW REQUIRED.
        - explain_exception/explain_risk/generate_remark prompts
          updated to match (explain_risk: an informational anomaly
          alone must not raise the risk level; generate_remark: state
          "passed core checks" for a PASS case instead of writing a
          pending-review remark).
    - tests/extraction/test_ai_assistant.py: +22 new checks (47 total,
      up from 25) covering _classify_anomaly's blocking/informational
      rules, and the exact 4 scenarios the task asked to test: (1) a
      full PASS document, including the specific historical-reviewed-
      duplicate case from the bug report (stays PASS), (2) a missing
      PO/GR document (REVIEW REQUIRED), (3) a duplicate invoice
      document that's still pending (REVIEW REQUIRED, classified
      blocking), (4) a sent-back document (REVIEW REQUIRED) — plus
      _clamp_explain_exception_result tests proving the AI's own wrong
      verdict is always overridden by the deterministic value. The 4
      existing generic _run_action cache-mechanism tests were switched
      from action 'explain_exception' to 'ask' so they stay decoupled
      from the new explain_exception-specific response clamp.
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — Record Detail page only:
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts: aiExceptionAnswer (string)
      replaced with aiCaseSummary ({audit_status, reason,
      recommended_action}); explainException() reads the new response
      shape. New auditStatusClass() helper reuses the existing risk-
      chip color classes (PASS -> green, REVIEW REQUIRED -> amber) — no
      new color tokens.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.html: Case Summary box now shows
      an "Audit Status" chip plus explicit Reason/Recommended Action
      lines instead of one paragraph.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.css: +7 lines, one small
      flex-row rule for the new Audit Status chip line — reuses every
      other existing class.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.spec.ts: updated the
      explainException test to the new response shape, added a
      dedicated PASS-case test asserting the audit_status/color
      mapping.

Why:
  An AI narrative should never contradict a deterministic fact
  AuditLens already computed. Server-side clamping (not just better
  prompt wording) is what actually guarantees a clean record is never
  mislabeled — prompt instructions alone are advisory and the exact
  class of bug this task reports (over-eager anomaly-as-exception
  narration) was already evidence that prompting alone isn't reliable
  enough for a business rule with a precise definition.

Testing:
  - Backend: `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 17 suites pass
    (test_ai_assistant.py: 47/47 checks, up from 25), zero real Claude/
    Gemini calls.
  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — clean import.
  - Frontend: `npx ng build --configuration production` — succeeded
    (exit 0; same pre-existing budget warnings as prior tasks).
  - Frontend: `npx ng test --watch=false` — 56/57 pass; the 1 failure
    is the same pre-existing, unrelated app.spec.ts issue seen
    throughout this project's history.
  - `git diff --stat` confirms only auditlens-backend/{helpers,routes}/
    ai_assistant.py, its test file, and the 4 Record Detail frontend
    files changed — zero changes to extraction, matching, authenticity,
    or anomaly engine files, and zero changes to the cache table/
    hashing/hit-miss mechanics (only new fields added to the context
    dict those mechanics already hash and store).
  - Tested exactly the 4 scenarios the task named: full PASS document
    (incl. a historical/reviewed duplicate anomaly — stays PASS),
    missing PO/GR document (REVIEW REQUIRED), duplicate invoice
    document still pending (REVIEW REQUIRED), sent-back document
    (REVIEW REQUIRED) — all as automated checks in test_ai_assistant.py
    since no live database with these exact records exists in this
    sandbox.

     ai_assistant_cache table unchanged), no new environment variables.

    - finance/home/finance-home.component.html: Recent Uploads table
      header changed from Document/Upload Date/Type/OCR Status/Match/
      Action to Document/Vendor/Status/Audit Status/Required Action/
      Action; the Document cell now shows invoice_number (falling back
      to file_name), matching the convention already used in finance/
      corrections' own list; the Action button now calls
      actionLabel(doc)/onAction(doc) instead of always rendering "Open"
      + viewDocument(doc).
    - finance/home/finance-home.component.css: removed .type-badge —
      orphaned by this change since the Type column (which was the only
      thing using it) was replaced by Vendor/Audit Status/Required
      Action. Every other class the new columns use (.badge-returned/
      .badge-review/.badge-matched/.badge-pending) already existed.
    - finance/home/finance-home.component.spec.ts (new): 12 tests
      covering exactly the 3 scenarios the task named — returned shows
      "Fix Issue" and navigates to Correction Center detail with the
      right document_id; under_review shows "View" and navigates to
      OCR Review; approved shows "View" and does NOT navigate anywhere
      (opens the file directly) — plus Audit Status/Required Action
      label correctness for each status, the ocr_processing/ocr_done
      fallback to "Review" -> OCR Review, and loadCyclesForReturnedRows
      only ever requesting cycles for the returned rows actually shown
      (never for approved/under_review rows, never when nothing is
      returned).

Why:
  Recent Uploads' one-size-fits-all "Open" button sent Finance into a
  raw file preview for a returned invoice instead of the Correction
  Center workspace built specifically to resolve it — the exact
  friction the Correction Center task was meant to remove, just not
  yet reflected on the Home dashboard's own upload table. The action
  button, and the new Audit Status/Required Action columns, now route
  and summarize per status using only data/endpoints that already
  exist.

Why:
  OCR Review and Correction Center both contained a working path to
  resolve a returned invoice (Auditor Request card, Finance Response
  field, Resubmit to Auditor), which is exactly the duplicated-workflow
  confusion this task was raised to fix — a Finance user could start

  source instead of just hiding UI elements while leaving the document

Date: 2026-07-22 (later same day)

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — 1 new endpoint, 1 new file, purely
  additive changes to 2 existing files, ZERO schema/table changes:
    - routes/ai_assistant.py: _build_case_context() gained two new
      dict keys, uploaded_at and ocr_confidence (both already returned
      by routes.auditor._build_comparison() — just not previously
      copied into this context dict). Purely additive: every existing
      key is unchanged, so nothing about the AI Audit Assistant or AI
      Correction Assistant changed.
    - routes/documents.py: new GET /documents/<id>/timeline endpoint +
      two new pure functions:
        - _require_timeline_access(document_id): auditor role -> any
          document; finance_executive -> only documents they uploaded
          themselves (same ownership rule as serve_document_file,
          already in this file).
        - _build_timeline_events(context): a pure function (no DB
          access, no AI call) that reshapes the SAME case-context dict
          routes/ai_assistant.py::_build_case_context() already builds
          for the AI Audit Assistant (three-way matching via routes.
          auditor._build_comparison, authenticity_checks, anomalies
          with their existing blocking/informational classification,
          review_records, send_back_cycles) into an ordered list of
          Document Workflow Timeline events: Document Uploaded, OCR
          Extraction, Three-way Matching, Authenticity Verification,
          Anomaly Evaluation, Auditor Review, Finance Correction
          (omitted entirely for a document that was never returned),
          Final Approval. Each event carries status "completed" |
          "action_required" | "pending" per the feature's own rules
          (missing documents / a pending send-back / a blocking
          anomaly => action_required; a finished check => completed;
          otherwise => pending) plus a short detail string and, for a
          returned document, the auditor's actual reason.
        get_document_timeline() itself is a thin wrapper: check access,
        call _build_case_context(), call _build_timeline_events(),
        return JSON. No new table, no new AI call — the SAME cached
        authenticity/anomaly/matching results are just read again.
    - tests/extraction/test_document_timeline.py (new): 34 checks —
      the exact 4 scenarios the task named (fully approved invoice,
      missing PO/GR invoice, returned invoice, Finance-corrected/
      resubmitted invoice) plus edge cases (OCR/authenticity not yet
      checked -> pending, an authenticity warning or a blocking
      anomaly -> action_required, an informational-only anomaly does
      NOT block, a "need_review" auditor action -> action_required)
      and _require_timeline_access's role/ownership checks (auditor
      unrestricted with zero DB lookups, finance owner accepted,
      finance non-owner rejected 403, missing document 404, unknown
      role rejected 403). Registered in tests/extraction/run_all.py.
    - tests/extraction/test_ai_assistant.py: updated every hand-built
      `fake_comparison`/`_pass_comparison()` fixture to include
      uploaded_at/ocr_confidence in its invoice dict, matching the
      real contract of _build_comparison() now that _build_case_
      context() reads those two fields — a pure test-fixture fix, no
      behavior assertions changed.
  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — 1 new reusable component (4 files),
  wired into both target pages:
    - workflow-timeline/workflow-timeline.component.{ts,html,css,
      spec.ts} (new, top-level — same "shared component" placement
      convention as the existing calendar/ component, reused by both
      auditor and finance pages): fetches GET /documents/<id>/timeline
      whenever its documentId @Input() is set to a real value, renders
      a vertical timeline (marker + label + detail + optional reason/
      timestamp per event), and maps status -> icon/colour using
      exactly the 3-status palette the feature specifies (completed:
      ph-check-circle/success; action_required: ph-warning/warning;
      pending: ph-circle/muted) — no colours beyond the app's existing
      success/warning/muted design tokens.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts/html: imported the new
      component, added <app-workflow-timeline [documentId]="
      documentId"> inside the existing *ngIf="!isLoading && comparison"
      block, right after the Field-Comparison/Decision-Card content-row
      and before the Send Back modal.
    - finance-correction-detail.component.ts/html: same placement
      pattern, inside the existing *ngIf="!isLoading && document" block,
      after the Original-Invoice-Info/Finance-Resolution content-row.
    - finance-correction-detail.component.spec.ts: both describe
      blocks' afterEach now drain any outstanding GET .../timeline
      request before calling httpMock.verify() — this component calls
      this.cdr.detectChanges() directly inside its own HTTP handlers,
      which (already, before this task) renders the template as soon as
      `document` becomes truthy even without the test calling fixture.
      detectChanges(); now that a child component with its own request-
      firing ngOnChanges lives in that template, several existing tests
      would otherwise fail on an unexpected outstanding request that
      isn't what they're testing (the timeline component has its own
      dedicated spec). auditor-record-detail.component.spec.ts needed
      no such change — none of its existing tests happen to populate
      `comparison` (only auditor-record-detail.component.ts's actual
      loadComparison() does that, which none of its specs call).

Why:
  Understanding a document's full lifecycle — what happened, what
  checks ran, what's outstanding — currently means checking the Field
  Comparison table, the Authenticity/Anomaly pages, the Send Back
  history box, and the review history separately. A single timeline
  reusing data those pages already compute (rather than recomputing or
  storing it a second time) gives both auditors and Finance the same
  at-a-glance traceability without visiting multiple pages, and without
  touching a single line of the extraction/matching/authenticity/
  anomaly/send-back engines it summarizes.

Testing:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 18 suites pass
    (test_document_timeline.py: 34/34 checks, new; test_ai_assistant.py
    unaffected in behavior, only its fixtures updated).
  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — clean import (no
    circular-import issue from routes/documents.py importing routes/
    ai_assistant.py — the same cross-route-module import convention
    already used by routes/authenticity.py and routes/ai_assistant.py
    themselves, and confirmed acyclic: documents -> ai_assistant ->
    auditor, nothing imports back the other way).
  - `npx ng build --configuration production` — succeeded (exit 0;
    same pre-existing budget warnings as prior tasks).
  - `npx ng test --watch=false` — 100/101 pass (up from 94; +6 new
    WorkflowTimelineComponent tests, all passing, plus every previously
    passing Correction Detail test still passing after the afterEach
