Date: 2026-07-22 (later same day)

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Enterprise V3 Phase 1: Build
  Relationship-Based Document Architecture. 1 new table, 2 new files,
  additive-only changes to 2 existing files. Does NOT replace or touch
  the existing one-to-one matching engine.
    - New table document_relationships (app.py::
      _ensure_document_relationships_table(), same auto-create-on-
      startup pattern as every other table in this app; matching
      migrations/2026-07-22_create_document_relationships_table.sql
      for documentation parity). Polymorphic association design:
      parent_type/child_type ('invoice'|'po'|'gr') + parent_id/child_id
      (meaning documents.document_id / purchase_orders.po_id /
      goods_receipts.gr_id depending on type) — chosen because
      purchase_orders/goods_receipts rows have no independent row in
      `documents`, so a literal single-table FOREIGN KEY to
      `documents` can't express a PO or GR endpoint. CHECK constraints
      enforce valid types, that relationship_type matches its
      parent/child type pair, and no self-links; a UNIQUE constraint
      prevents duplicate relationships. Referential integrity for the
      polymorphic parent_id/child_id is enforced in the service layer
      (below), not the database, since Postgres FKs can't target three
      different tables from one column.
    - helpers/document_relationships.py (new): create_relationship(),
      delete_relationship(), get_relationship_by_id(),
      get_related_documents(), get_related_invoices(),
      get_related_purchase_orders(), get_related_goods_receipts().
      Compatibility layer: the three typed getters check
      document_relationships first, and fall back to the legacy
      one-to-one attachment (purchase_orders.document_id /
      goods_receipts.document_id, mirroring routes/auditor.py::
      _build_comparison()'s own PO/GR selection) whenever a document
      has zero explicit relationship rows — so pre-existing data keeps
      working through the new getters with no backfill migration
      required.
    - routes/document_relationships.py (new blueprint, registered
      under the same '/documents' url_prefix as routes/documents.py):
      GET /documents/<id>/relationships, POST /documents/relationships,
      DELETE /documents/relationships/<relationship_id>.
      _require_node_access(doc_type, doc_id) follows the same
      role-check pattern as routes/documents.py's
      _require_timeline_access() — auditor: any node; finance_
      executive: only an invoice/PO/GR they uploaded themselves
      (purchase_orders and goods_receipts both already carry their own
      uploaded_by column).
    - app.py: 2 new import/registration lines + 1 new _ensure_* call —
      no existing line changed.
    - tests/extraction/test_document_relationships.py (new): 18
      checks, fully offline (in-memory fake DB, no real Postgres
      connection) — the exact 4 scenarios the task named (one PO/one
      invoice/one GR; one PO/two invoices/two GR, i.e. the task's
      PO7710 example; two PO/one invoice/one GR; existing documents
      still working via the legacy fallback), plus create_relationship()
      validation branches (unknown type, mismatched type pair,
      nonexistent entity, duplicate) and _require_node_access() access
      control (auditor unrestricted, finance owner accepted, finance
      non-owner rejected, missing node 404, unknown role rejected).
      Registered in tests/extraction/run_all.py's SUITES list.

  Untouched, verified via `git diff --stat`: routes/auditor.py
  (_build_comparison and every other matching function), routes/
  matching.py (the legacy engine), routes/ai_assistant.py, routes/
  documents.py, extraction/OCR, the authenticity engine, the anomaly
  engine — zero lines changed in any of them. Zero new Claude/Gemini
  API calls anywhere in this feature (pure DB CRUD).

Why it was changed:
  Phase 1 of upgrading AuditLens from "one invoice -> one PO -> one GR"
  to "multiple PO -> multiple invoice -> multiple GR" support, per an
  architecture review done earlier the same day that found purchase_
  orders/goods_receipts rows have no independent identity in
  `documents` today — only a document_id FK to whichever invoice they
  were uploaded under — which is why a flexible, polymorphic
  many-to-many relationship table was needed rather than a literal
  parent_document_id/child_document_id FK pair. This phase is
  deliberately backward-compatible and additive only: the existing
  matching engine, AI assistants, authenticity/anomaly engines, and
  every existing frontend page keep working exactly as before, unaware
  this table exists.

Testing:
  - `python -c "import app; print('APP IMPORT OK')"` — clean import;
    "document_relationships table ready" printed alongside every other
    existing _ensure_* table, confirming the CREATE TABLE/CHECK/UNIQUE/
    index statements are valid and idempotent.
  - Live smoke test against the real local Postgres dev DB (temporary
    rows created and cleaned up): legacy fallback before any
    relationship rows exist, relationship creation, duplicate
    rejection, type-pair mismatch rejection, nonexistent-entity
    rejection, and deletion — all confirmed working against real
    Postgres constraint/ANY()/RETURNING/JOIN semantics, DB left exactly
    as found afterward.
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 19 suites pass
    (test_document_relationships.py: 18/18 checks, new; every other
    suite unaffected).
  - `npx ng build --configuration production` — succeeded (exit 0;
    same pre-existing bundle-size budget warnings as prior tasks, zero
    frontend files changed by this backend-only feature).
  - `git diff --stat` confirms the change is additive-only: 1 new
    table, 2 wholly new files (service layer + route blueprint), and
    purely-additive edits to app.py (+57 lines: 1 new _ensure_*
    function, 1 import, 1 blueprint registration, 1 function call) and
    run_all.py (+1 line registering the new test suite) — zero changes
    to any existing route, function, or table.

Risk assessment:
  - LOW risk to existing functionality: every change is additive (new
    table, new files, appended lines only); the matching engine, AI
    assistants, authenticity/anomaly engines, and every existing page
    are proven untouched via git diff and the full regression suite.
  - MEDIUM, documented trade-off: parent_id/child_id are polymorphic,
    so they cannot carry a real SQL FOREIGN KEY (Postgres FKs target
    exactly one table). Entity-existence validation happens in
    helpers/document_relationships.py::create_relationship() instead
    of the database — a direct INSERT bypassing this service layer
    (e.g. a future script, an admin tool) could create a dangling
    reference. Mitigated by: CHECK constraints on type validity/type-
    pair consistency, a UNIQUE constraint against duplicates, and the
    fact that this table currently has exactly one write path (the new
    API/service layer) with no other code touching it yet.
  - LOW risk from the legacy-fallback design: get_related_purchase_
    orders/goods_receipts/invoices() silently fall back to the old
    one-to-one attachment when no explicit relationship exists. This
    is intentional (STEP 4 compatibility requirement) but means a
    caller can't currently distinguish "no relationship data at all"
    from "using the legacy single attachment" except by checking
    whether relationship=None on the returned row.
  - No risk to AI cost/behavior: zero new Claude/Gemini calls.

Setup/config needed:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND — new table auto-creates on startup
     via the existing _ensure_* pattern, no manual migration needed
     (same as every other table in this app), no new environment
     variables.
  2. No Render FRONTEND redeploy needed — zero frontend files changed.
  3. No config changes needed.

Date: 2026-07-22 (later same day)

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Enterprise V3 Phase 2: Add Enterprise
  Many-to-Many Matching Engine. 2 new columns, 3 new files, additive-

  (_build_comparison) is completely unmodified and remains the default
  and permanent fallback.
    - document_relationships gained 2 additive columns:
      relationship_source ('manual'|'auto', default 'manual' so every

      nullable) — app.py::_ensure_document_relationships_v2_columns(),
      same auto-create-on-startup pattern as every other table/column
      in this app; matching migrations/2026-07-22_add_document_
      relationships_source_and_reason.sql for documentation parity.
    - helpers/document_relationships.py: new upsert_relationship() —
      insert-or-update for the builder only, always writes source=
      'auto'; if a relationship already exists with source='manual' it
      is left completely untouched (returned as-is, skipped=True).
      create_relationship() gained 2 optional params (relationship_
      source='manual', matching_reason=None) — every existing caller
      (Phase 1's POST /documents/relationships) is unaffected since
      the defaults reproduce its exact prior behavior.
    - helpers/enterprise_matching.py (new): pure, dependency-free
      cumulative calculators — compute_po_fulfilment() (ordered/
      invoiced/received quantities and amounts, remaining balances, a
      PO-level fulfilment status: OPEN_NOT_INVOICED/OPEN_PARTIALLY_
      INVOICED/FULLY_INVOICED/OVER_INVOICED plus an independent
      received_status axis with the same 4 tiers, and FULLY_FULFILLED
      when both axes are complete) and compute_invoice_result() (an
      invoice-level PASS/REVIEW_REQUIRED verdict: unsupported quantity/
      amount, vendor mismatch, over-invoicing, or no reliable PO force
      REVIEW_REQUIRED; missing GR support is a warning only, mirroring
      the legacy engine's existing PARTIAL-not-FAIL treatment of a
      missing GR). Decimal arithmetic throughout, never float.
    - helpers/relationship_builder.py (new): the deterministic (no
      LLM) relationship builder — find_candidate_purchase_orders()/
      find_candidate_goods_receipts() (system-wide search by exact
      normalized PO-reference match OR the legacy document_id
      attachment — never vendor/amount alone), score_po_invoice_
      candidate()/score_invoice_gr_candidate()/score_po_gr_candidate()
      (fixed numeric scoring: reference/attachment evidence gates
      whether a candidate is considered at all; vendor match, item
      description match, quantity/amount plausibility, and date
      sequence add or subtract from there), build_relationships_for_
      invoice()/rebuild_relationships_for_invoice()/build_
      relationships_for_all_documents() (orchestration + idempotent
      persistence via upsert_relationship, MIN_AUTO_CONFIDENCE=0.50).
      Allocation rule: exactly one qualifying PO candidate allocates
      the invoice's full quantity/amount to it; multiple qualifying PO
      candidates link every PO (discoverable) but leave matched_
      quantity/matched_amount as None rather than guess a split.
      invoice_gr attribution rule (found via manual testing against
      the real PO3006231 scenario, not assumed): goods_receipts has no
      invoice-specific field, only a shared po_reference, so when
      ANOTHER invoice also claims the same PO, multiple GR candidates
      are genuinely ambiguous between invoices and are skipped
      entirely for direct linking (PO-level receipt totals are
      unaffected — they come from po_gr relationships, which
      legitimately link a PO to every one of its GRs regardless); a
      single GR candidate, or multiple GR candidates when no other
      invoice claims the same PO (a real 1-invoice-2-GRs case), are
      linked normally.
    - routes/auditor.py: _build_comparison() is byte-for-byte
      unchanged. Added _build_comparison_v2() (loads the invoice, every
      related PO/GR/sibling-invoice via Phase 1's document_
      relationships helpers, computes per-PO cumulative fulfilment and
      the invoice-level verdict, and ALSO computes the exact legacy-
      shaped invoice/po/gr/match_result/line_items keys against the
      relationship-selected primary PO/GR — using the same _vendor_
      match_all/_amounts_equal/_match_line_items/etc. helpers as legacy
      — so every existing consumer of those keys, e.g. _classify_
      exception, keeps working unchanged even when V2 is active) and
      build_comparison() (the single shared dispatcher: both feature
      flags off -> legacy only, zero V2 code runs; shadow mode ->
      legacy stays user-facing, V2 is also computed only when this
      invoice has explicit relationships, logging a concise status-only
      diff, never full document content, never an extra AI call; V2
      enabled -> V2 is used when relationships exist, any exception
      during V2 computation is caught, logged, and falls back to
      legacy rather than ever 5xx-ing a page). This file's own 4
      internal call sites (get_record_comparison, get_exceptions,
      get_report_summary x2) were switched from _build_comparison() to
      build_comparison() — the only way V2 can reach the Exception
      page, Report, and Record Detail without duplicating any of their
      logic.
    - routes/ai_assistant.py: 1-line change — _build_case_context()
      now calls build_comparison() instead of _build_comparison()
      directly, which is what lets V2 reach the AI Assistant and the
      Workflow Timeline (both built on _build_case_context) through
      the same single dispatcher, with no changes to either feature's
      own logic.
    - helpers/anomaly_detector.py: detect_duplicate_suspicion() gained
      an optional invoice_number param and a new _shares_linked_
      purchase_order() check — two invoices with the SAME vendor/
      amount/close-date but DIFFERENT invoice numbers that are both
      linked (via document_relationships) to a common PO are legitimate
      split invoices, not a duplicate, and the flag is now suppressed
      for exactly that case. A duplicate still fires whenever the
      invoice numbers match (or either is unknown), or when there's no
      shared-PO evidence — invoice number remains the deciding signal.
      No other anomaly-detection logic changed.
    - routes/document_relationships.py: added GET /documents/<id>/
      enterprise-matching (STEP 12) — exposes build_comparison()'s full
      result (legacy shape, or the additive V2 shape when applicable)
      directly, since Phase 1's GET /<id>/relationships only returns
      raw links, not a cumulative matching result. Same _require_node_
      access() control as every other route in this file.
    - config.py: 2 new env-driven flags, both default false —
      ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_ENABLED, ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_SHADOW_MODE.
    - scripts/backfill_document_relationships.py (new): manual CLI for
      the builder — always dry-run unless --apply is passed, supports
      --document-id (single invoice) or batch with --limit, never runs
      automatically (no caller anywhere in app.py), never overwrites a
      manual relationship (inherited from upsert_relationship).
    - tests/extraction/test_enterprise_matching.py (new, 30+ checks,
      fully offline/pure): locks in the exact PO3006231 acceptance-
      scenario numbers (both the full state — 30,000/30,000 invoiced
      and received, RM 7,710.00 cumulative, FULLY_FULFILLED, both
      invoices individually PASS, no false duplicate/partial/amount
      mismatch — and the intermediate state — 15,000 remaining,
      RM 3,855.00 remaining, OPEN_PARTIALLY_INVOICED/OPEN_PARTIALLY_
      RECEIVED, invoice A still PASSes) directly against the pure
      calculator, independent of any database. Plus partial invoice/
      partial GR/fully-fulfilled/over-invoicing/over-receipt/quantity-
      or-amount-exceeds-remaining/vendor-mismatch/no-reliable-PO/
      multi-PO-no-double-counting/ambiguous-split-not-guessed/missing-
      GR-is-a-warning-not-blocking scenarios.
    - tests/extraction/test_relationship_builder.py (new, 33 checks):
      pure scorer tests (reference-match gating, vendor/quantity/date
      penalties, legacy-attachment scoring) plus integration tests
      against the real local Postgres dev DB (this phase's own Safety
      Requirement 12 explicitly permits "database test data" — only
      live Claude/Gemini calls are prohibited; two real design bugs,
      both around invoice-to-GR attribution ambiguity, were caught by
      running against the real DB during development, which a hand-
      rolled fake cursor would likely not have caught) — covering 1
      PO/1 invoice/1 GR, 1 PO/2 invoices/2 GRs (the PO7710-style
      example, including via the real V2 engine end-to-end), 2 POs/1
      invoice, 1 invoice/2 GRs, multiple invoices sharing a GR reached
      via the PO level, re-running the builder creates no duplicates,
      an existing invoice with zero relationship rows still works via
      the legacy fallback, a manual relationship is never overwritten
      by the builder, dry-run never writes, and 3 anomaly-compatibility
      cases (split invoices sharing a PO are NOT flagged as duplicate;
      a genuinely repeated invoice number IS still flagged even with a
      shared PO; different invoice numbers with NO shared PO are still
      flagged).
    - tests/extraction/run_all.py: registered both new suites.
    - tests/extraction/test_ai_assistant.py / test_document_
      relationships.py: updated to match the (purely additive) new
      shape of routes.ai_assistant's import (_build_comparison ->
      build_comparison) and create_relationship()'s extended INSERT
      params — no behavioral change to either test file's own logic.

  Untouched, verified via `git diff --stat`: routes/matching.py (the
  legacy/dead engine), routes/documents.py (upload/OCR pipeline),
  extraction/OCR, the Claude/Gemini extraction prompts, the
  authenticity engine, three_way_matches/record_matches/exceptions/
  ledger_records (legacy tables, untouched and undeleted) — zero lines
  changed in any of them. _build_comparison() itself is untouched byte-
  for-byte (confirmed via diff: every change to routes/auditor.py is
  either a new import, a new function appended after it, or a 1-line
  name swap at 4 call sites).

Why it was changed:
  Phase 2 of the Enterprise V3 upgrade (Phase 1 built the underlying
  document_relationships table and service layer) — teaches AuditLens
  to understand and calculate multi-PO/multi-invoice/multi-GR
  relationships: partial invoicing, partial receipt, cumulative
  invoicing/receipt, remaining PO quantity/amount, over-invoicing,
  over-receipt, and duplicate-allocation prevention — while the
  existing one-to-one production workflow (Exception page, Report,
  Record Detail, AI Assistant, Workflow Timeline) keeps working exactly
  as before, completely unaware anything changed, until the new engine
  is explicitly turned on.

Relationship scoring rules:
  Every scorer gates on either an exact normalized PO-reference/PO-
  number match OR the legacy one-to-one document_id attachment first —
  a candidate with neither scores exactly 0 and is never created ("do
  not create a high-confidence relationship using vendor and amount
  alone"). From that gate, vendor match (+), vendor mismatch (-), item
  description match (+), quantity/amount plausibility against the
  counterpart (+/-), and date sequence validity (+/-) adjust the score,
  clamped to [0, 1]. MIN_AUTO_CONFIDENCE = 0.50 — below that, a
  candidate is never auto-created.

Allocation rules:
  matched_quantity/matched_amount on document_relationships are the
  allocation. A single qualifying PO candidate for an invoice gets the
  invoice's full quantity/amount; multiple qualifying PO candidates
  leave the allocation as None (ambiguous, never guessed) but still
  link every PO so it's discoverable. Cumulative PO totals sum every
  linked invoice's matched_quantity/matched_amount exactly once (a
  UNIQUE DB constraint already prevents a duplicate relationship row
  from existing at all). All arithmetic uses Decimal, never float.

Legacy fallback behavior:
  An invoice with zero explicit document_relationships rows is served
  entirely by the untouched _build_comparison() (build_comparison()
  short-circuits to it before even checking the feature flags' cost).
  Phase 1's get_related_purchase_orders/get_related_goods_receipts/
  get_related_invoices already fall back to the legacy one-to-one
  attachment when no explicit relationship exists, so even a request
  that does reach the V2 engine for a still-legacy invoice degrades
  gracefully to the same PO/GR legacy would have picked.

Feature-flag behavior:
  ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_ENABLED=false, ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_SHADOW_
  MODE=false by default (both). With both off, build_comparison() is a
  direct passthrough to _build_comparison() — no relationship lookup,
  no V2 code path, identical behavior and cost to before this phase
  existed. Shadow mode computes V2 alongside legacy purely for a
  concise DEBUG-level log line (never changes what's returned, never
  calls AI, never creates a duplicate exception). V2 enabled uses V2
  only for an invoice with explicit relationships, always with an
  exception-safe fallback to legacy.

API usage confirmation:
  Number of Claude calls added: 0. Number of Gemini calls added: 0. The
  entire matching engine (scoring, allocation, cumulative fulfilment)
  is deterministic field comparison and arithmetic — no LLM is called
  anywhere in helpers/relationship_builder.py or helpers/enterprise_
  matching.py, and none was added to anomaly detection's compatibility
  fix either.

Test results:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 21 suites pass (2 new:
    test_enterprise_matching.py 30+/30+, test_relationship_builder.py
    33/33; every pre-existing suite still green after fixing the 2
    fixture/import updates test_ai_assistant.py and test_document_
    relationships.py needed for the additive signature changes).
  - Live verification against the real local Postgres dev DB
    (temporary rows created and cleaned up, DB left exactly as found):
    the full PO3006231 acceptance scenario end-to-end through the real
    V2 engine, both the full state and the literal intermediate state
    (only invoice A + GR A uploaded) — every number matches the task's
    expected values exactly. Two real bugs (ambiguous invoice-to-GR
    cross-linking when multiple invoices share a PO; the same fix
    initially over-corrected and broke the legitimate 1-invoice-2-GR
    case) were found and fixed via this live testing before being
    locked into the automated suite.
  - `python -c "import app"` — clean import; "document_relationships
    v2 columns ready" printed, confirming the additive ALTER TABLE is
    idempotent.
  - `npx ng build --configuration production` — succeeded (exit 0,
    same pre-existing bundle-size budget warnings, zero frontend files
    changed).
  - `git diff --stat` confirms the change is additive-only: 3 wholly
    new files, 2 new columns, purely-additive edits to 8 existing
    files (new imports/functions/params/call-site swaps only), zero
    changes to routes/matching.py, routes/documents.py, extraction/
    OCR, the Claude/Gemini prompts, the authenticity engine, or any
    legacy table.

Known limitations:
  - document_line_items has no po_id/gr_id column (only invoice
    document_id + a type tag), so line-item-level detail in V2's
    legacy-shaped keys is only available when the primary PO/GR is
    co-located under the invoice's own document_id — a genuinely
    cross-invoice-shared PO/GR gets line_items=[] (not computed) rather
    than a guessed/potentially-wrong comparison.
  - invoice_gr direct links are intentionally NOT created whenever
    another invoice also claims the same PO and there's more than one
    GR candidate (see the allocation rule above) — PO-level received
    totals are unaffected (they come from po_gr instead), but a
    per-invoice "matched_gr_count" in that specific situation falls
    back to "does the PO have any receipt evidence at all" rather than
    a direct per-invoice receipt record, since the schema has no way to
    express that distinction more precisely.
  - The relationship builder is not wired into the upload pipeline in
    this phase (routes/documents.py is completely untouched, by
    design, to keep the highest-risk file at zero risk) — relationships
    are built via the new backfill script or the existing Phase 1 API
    only. A future phase can add an opt-in, failure-isolated hook after
    extraction if desired.
  - Real Claude/Gemini interaction with this feature (e.g. whether the
    AI Assistant's prompts read naturally once V2 fields are exposed to
    it) has not been exercised with a live API key in this sandbox —
    no AI Assistant prompt/context changes were made in this phase at
    all, so no new interaction exists to verify.

Deployment instructions:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND — the 2 new columns auto-add on
     startup via the existing _ensure_* pattern, no manual migration
     step, no required new environment variables (both new flags
     default to their off/false state if unset).
  2. Confirm startup logs show "document_relationships v2 columns
     ready" and that existing invoices still display normally (V2
     stays disabled by default).
  3. Optional, once ready to validate further: set
     ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_SHADOW_MODE=true and watch the Render logs
     for the "DEBUG shadow-mode diff" lines on invoices that have
     document_relationships rows (created via the backfill script or
     the Phase 1 API) — legacy stays user-facing throughout.
  4. Only after shadow-mode comparison looks correct: set
     ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_ENABLED=true.
  5. No Render FRONTEND redeploy needed — zero frontend files changed.

Rollback instructions:
  Set ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_ENABLED=false (and ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_
  SHADOW_MODE=false) and redeploy — build_comparison() immediately
  reverts to being a direct passthrough to the untouched _build_
  comparison(), with no code changes required. The 2 new columns and
  the document_relationships rows a builder run may have created can
  be left in place indefinitely (inert, read by nothing when V2 is
  off) or removed with a manual DELETE if ever desired — nothing else
  in the app depends on their existence.

Confirmation that Finance Upload UI was not redesigned: correct — zero
frontend files were changed in this phase; routes/documents.py (the
upload pipeline) is completely untouched.

Confirmation that _build_comparison() legacy behavior remains
available: correct — its function body is byte-for-byte unchanged, it
is still directly callable, and it is the unconditional fallback
whenever V2 is disabled, an invoice has no explicit relationships, or
V2 raises any exception.

Date: 2026-07-22 (later same day)

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Enterprise V3 Phase 3: Add Enterprise
  Matching Shadow Validation. Observation-only: no matching table, no
  workflow status, no auditor decision, and no user-facing result is
  ever modified. 1 new file, additive-only changes to 3 existing files.
    - routes/auditor.py: added _shape_shadow_comparison() (pure
      formatting, no DB access — turns an already-computed legacy_
      result/v2_result pair into the structured {document_id, legacy:
      {status, matching_summary}, enterprise_v2: {status, matching_
      summary}, differences: [{field, legacy_value, v2_value, reason}]}
      shape), build_shadow_comparison() (the public, self-contained
      entry point used by the new debug endpoint — computes legacy via
      the untouched _build_comparison(), and V2 via _build_comparison_
      v2() only when the invoice has explicit document_relationships
      rows), and _log_shadow_comparison() (prints ONLY document_id,
      timestamp, legacy status, enterprise status, and difference
      field-name TYPES — never a reason string, never a matched
      quantity/amount, never a vendor name or any other extracted
      field). build_comparison()'s existing shadow-mode branch (from
      Phase 2) was refactored to call _shape_shadow_comparison() on the
      legacy/V2 results it already computes for its own dispatch
      purposes, instead of the previous ad-hoc one-line diff print —
      this is a pure refactor with no added DB calls (STEP 6: "avoid
      repeated expensive queries" — confirmed via git diff that this
      only replaced the old print block, no new query was introduced
      to the per-request dispatch path). _build_comparison() and
      _build_comparison_v2() themselves are byte-for-byte unchanged
      (confirmed via git diff — zero lines removed from either).
    - routes/document_relationships.py: added GET /documents/<id>/
      matching-comparison (STEP 4) — returns build_shadow_comparison()'s
      full structured result, working regardless of the current
      feature-flag state (so an auditor can inspect a comparison
      without needing shadow mode enabled first). New _require_auditor_
      only() access check — deliberately stricter than this file's
      existing _require_node_access() (which allows Finance for a
      document they own): the shadow-comparison debug endpoint excludes
      Finance entirely, since it's an internal engine-validation tool,
      not a document-review feature.
    - tests/extraction/test_shadow_comparison.py (new, 21 checks): the
      5 scenarios named by the task — (1) simple 1 PO/1 invoice/1 GR
      case where legacy and V2 agree with zero recorded differences;
      (2) the PO3006231-style 1 PO/2 invoices/2 GR case, verified live
      against the real dev DB — legacy reports FAIL (it can only ever
      compare an invoice's total against the PO's FULL amount, with no
      concept of "this invoice covers half the PO"), V2 correctly
      reports PASS, and a matching_status difference is recorded with a
      reason naming the actual cause ("Enterprise engine detected
      multiple related invoices") — a concrete demonstration of
      exactly the gap V2 exists to close; (3) an invoice with zero
      document_relationships rows resolves via the legacy fallback with
      no error and enterprise_v2/differences empty; (4) a genuinely
      multi-PO invoice is calculated correctly end-to-end through both
      _build_comparison_v2() directly and the shadow comparison; (5)
      every Claude/Gemini/AI-assistant call function is monkey-patched
      to raise if invoked, then shadow mode is run through both build_
      comparison() and build_shadow_comparison() — confirming neither
      code path ever touches an AI helper. Plus a pure (no DB) test
      that captures _log_shadow_comparison()'s actual stdout output and
      asserts a real amount value from the input never appears in it.
      Registered in tests/extraction/run_all.py.

  Untouched, verified via `git diff --stat`: routes/matching.py,
  routes/documents.py (OCR/upload pipeline), helpers/claude_extractor.py,
  helpers/gemini_extractor.py, helpers/anomaly_detector.py, helpers/
  authenticity_check.py, config.py (both feature flags already existed
  from Phase 2, still default false, no changes needed), every frontend
  file — zero lines changed in any of them.

Why it was changed:
  Phase 3 of the Enterprise V3 upgrade — before ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_
  ENABLED can ever be safely flipped on in production, there needs to
  be a way to observe how the V2 engine's results would actually differ
  from the live legacy engine's results, on real data, with zero risk
  to what auditors currently see — shadow mode already existed
  structurally from Phase 2, but only produced a single unstructured
  debug print line with no way to inspect a specific comparison on
  demand. This phase makes that comparison a first-class, structured,
  safely-loggable object, and adds an on-demand debug endpoint so an
  auditor doesn't have to grep server logs to validate the engine.

Shadow flow diagram:
  Request for invoice X (any of: Record Detail comparison, Exception
  page, Report, AI Assistant, Workflow Timeline)
    -> routes/*.py calls build_comparison(cursor, X)
         -> both flags false (default): _build_comparison(X) -> return
            legacy result. [V2 code path never runs.]
         -> SHADOW_MODE=true: _build_comparison(X) -> legacy_result
                               (if X has document_relationships rows)
                               _build_comparison_v2(X) -> v2_result
                               _shape_shadow_comparison(...) -> comparison
                               _log_shadow_comparison(comparison) -> DEBUG log
                               return legacy_result  [ALWAYS legacy — the
                               response the browser receives is identical
                               to shadow mode being off.]
         -> V2_ENABLED=true (X has relationships): _build_comparison_v2(X)
                               -> v2_result, with an exception-safe
                               fallback to legacy_result if V2 raises.

  On-demand inspection (independent of the flags):
    Auditor calls GET /documents/<id>/matching-comparison
      -> _require_auditor_only() (Finance always 403, even for an owned doc)
      -> build_shadow_comparison(cursor, id) -> {legacy, enterprise_v2, differences}
      -> JSON response (never touches build_comparison()'s dispatch/flags)

Test results:
  - `python tests/extraction/run_all.py` — all 22 suites pass (1 new:
    test_shadow_comparison.py 21/21; zero regressions in any
    pre-existing suite, including test_ai_assistant.py and test_
    document_relationships.py which needed no further changes this
    phase since Phase 2 already updated them for the build_comparison
    rename).
  - `npx ng build --configuration production` — succeeded (exit 0,
    same pre-existing bundle-size budget warnings, zero frontend files
    changed).
  - Live verification against the real local Postgres dev DB (rows
    created and cleaned up, DB left exactly as found): the PO3006231-
    style scenario end-to-end through build_shadow_comparison(),
    confirming the exact JSON shape and a genuinely meaningful
    difference reason (see the example below).
  - `git diff --stat` confirms the change is additive-only: 1 new file,
    purely-additive edits to 3 existing files (new functions, a
    refactor that replaces an old print block, and one new endpoint) —
    zero changes to routes/matching.py, routes/documents.py, OCR, the
    Claude/Gemini extraction/authenticity/anomaly modules, config.py's
    existing flags, or any frontend file.

Example comparison output (from the live PO3006231-style verification):
  {
    "document_id": 134,
    "relationship_mode": true,
    "legacy": {
      "status": "FAIL",
      "matching_summary": {
        "vendor_match": true, "amount_match": false,
        "po_reference_match": true, "line_items_match": null,
        "po_present": true, "gr_present": true
      }
    },
    "enterprise_v2": {
      "status": "PASS",
      "matching_summary": {
        "matched_po_count": 1, "matched_gr_count": 1,
        "allocated_quantity": 15000.0, "allocated_amount": 3855.0,
        "related_invoice_count": 1
      }
    },
    "differences": [
      {
        "field": "matching_status", "legacy_value": "FAIL", "v2_value": "PASS",
        "reason": "Enterprise engine detected multiple related invoices"
      },
      {
        "field": "related_invoices", "legacy_value": 0, "v2_value": 1,
        "reason": "Enterprise engine detected multiple related invoices sharing a purchase order"
      }
    ]
  }

API usage confirmation:
  Number of Claude calls added: 0. Number of Gemini calls added: 0.
  Confirmed both by code inspection (no import of claude_extractor/
  gemini_extractor/ai_assistant anywhere in this phase's new/changed
  code) and by test (Scenario 5 monkey-patches every AI call function
  to raise if invoked, then runs both build_comparison() and build_
  shadow_comparison() through shadow mode — zero exceptions raised).

Known limitations:
  - _log_shadow_comparison() only fires from build_comparison()'s
    dispatch path when SHADOW_MODE is actually enabled — with both
    flags at their default false, the new logging code exists but
    never executes on a live request, by design (shadow mode is opt-in
    diagnostics, not always-on overhead).
  - The debug endpoint (GET /documents/<id>/matching-comparison) always
    computes both engines live on each call (no caching) — acceptable
    at this app's current invoice volume (same reasoning already
    documented for /auditor/report/summary's own per-request
    recomputation), flagged for a real cache if volume grows.

Deployment instructions:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND — no schema change, no new
     environment variables (both feature flags already existed from
     Phase 2 and keep their current values unless explicitly changed).
  2. No Render FRONTEND redeploy needed — zero frontend files changed.
  3. Recommended validation sequence before ever enabling V2: set
     ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_SHADOW_MODE=true, watch Render logs for
     "DEBUG Matching Shadow Comparison" lines on invoices with
     document_relationships rows, and/or have an auditor hit GET
     /documents/<id>/matching-comparison directly for specific
     invoices of interest — legacy stays user-facing throughout. Only
     after that comparison looks correct, set ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_
     ENABLED=true (per Phase 2's own deployment instructions).

Rollback instructions:
  Set ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_SHADOW_MODE=false (already the default)
  and redeploy — the new logging/comparison code simply stops running
  on the dispatch path; the debug endpoint remains available (it's
  read-only and flag-independent) but can be ignored. No data was ever
  written by this phase, so there is nothing to clean up.

Both feature flags remain at their safe defaults after this phase:
  ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_ENABLED=false
  ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_SHADOW_MODE=false

Date: 2026-07-22 (later same day)

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) — Enterprise V3 Phase 4: wired the
  already-built Enterprise V2 engine (Phases 1-3) into every auditor-
  facing surface, without rewriting the V2 engine/relationship builder/
  allocation engine, and without touching OCR, Claude/Gemini extraction,
  the authenticity engine, the anomaly engine, or the send-back/Finance
  Correction workflow (confirmed via git diff: helpers/relationship_
  builder.py and helpers/enterprise_matching.py are byte-for-byte
  unchanged; _build_comparison_v2()'s own body has zero removed lines).
    - routes/auditor.py: added _matching_status_for_comparison() — the
      single normalized status ('PASS'|'REVIEW'|'FAIL'|'PARTIAL') every
      V2-aware consumer now reads from, preferring V2's own invoice_
      result.status when V2 ran, else legacy's match_result.
      overall_status. _classify_exception() now branches on comparison
      ['engine_version']: under V2, ALL matching-related exception
      candidates (mismatch/review/missing_document) come from V2's own
      invoice_result.status/issues instead of the legacy fields — this
      is the actual fix for "do not create false exceptions from legacy
      logic" (the PO3006231 example: legacy alone reports a hard Amount
      mismatch because it can only ever compare an invoice against a
      PO's FULL total; V2 correctly resolves it as fully allocated and
      PASS, so no exception is created at all under V2). A V2 REVIEW_
      REQUIRED case produces one 'mismatch'-type exception (same type
      as legacy, so the existing Exceptions page filter chip needs no
      changes) labeled "Enterprise Matching Review Required", with a
      detail string that includes real allocation evidence (PO number,
      invoiced/received/remaining quantities) pulled from po_
      fulfilment. get_report_summary()'s match_pass/match_review counts
      now use _matching_status_for_comparison() instead of the raw
      legacy field, so Report accuracy is preserved once V2 is enabled;
      added the optional 'enterprise_matching_coverage': {single_
      document_matches, multi_document_matches} stat, computed from the
      SAME comparison dicts already in the existing loop (no new query,
      no fabricated numbers — relationship_mode is only ever true when
      V2 actually ran with real document_relationships data).
    - routes/ai_assistant.py: _compute_audit_status() now branches on
      comparison['engine_version'] — under V2, its contribution to
      "reasons" comes from invoice_result.issues instead of legacy's
      overall_status + missing_documents, which is what stops a
      missing-GR-only warning (non-blocking under V2) or an unrelated
      PO's own partial-fulfilment state from incorrectly forcing REVIEW
      REQUIRED once V2 already resolved the invoice as PASS.
      _build_case_context() now computes matching_status via
      _matching_status_for_comparison() (was: raw match_result.
      overall_status) and adds 10 new additive context fields via a new
      _v2_ai_context_fields() helper: matching_engine_version,
      relationship_mode, related_document_count, related_invoice_count,
      related_gr_count, cumulative_po_quantity, cumulative_invoice_
      quantity, cumulative_received_quantity, remaining_quantity,
      fulfilment_status — all None/False/'legacy' when V2 didn't run,
      so existing (non-V2) cases are completely unaffected.
    - helpers/ai_assistant.py: added one paragraph to the existing
      "AUDIT STATUS INTERPRETATION RULES" section of the system
      preamble (the same mechanism already used for the anomaly-
      classification rule) instructing the AI: when matching_engine_
      version is "v2" and audit_status is "PASS", describe matching as
      "Validated through enterprise three-way matching" or "Passed
      core matching checks", never "Invoice mismatch"; and that
      fulfilment_status describes the related PO's own cumulative
      state (which can legitimately be partial) rather than a problem
      with the specific invoice under review. No new AI call, no new
      provider, no new action — same Claude-primary/Gemini-fallback
      call flow, same ai_assistant_cache, same 6 existing action types.
    - routes/documents.py: _build_timeline_events()'s three_way_
      matching step's completed/action_required/pending bucketing
      needed NO logic change (matching_status was already fed from
      _build_case_context, which is now V2-aware) — only the detail
      text is adjusted when context['relationship_mode'] is true:
      "Enterprise three-way matching completed" (PASS) / "Enterprise
      matching flagged for review" (REVIEW/FAIL), falling back to the
      unchanged original "Status: PASS"/"Status: REVIEW REQUIRED"
      wording whenever V2 didn't run for that invoice. No timeline
      redesign — same 8 steps, same status/label/event contract.
    - tests/extraction/test_phase4_integration.py (new, 39 checks):
      the dispatcher's exact 4 required scenarios (flag off -> legacy;
      flag on with relationships -> V2; flag on with no relationships
      -> legacy fallback; flag on but V2 raises -> legacy fallback, no
      5xx), exception classification (V2 PASS produces zero exceptions
      even though legacy alone would flag one; V2 REVIEW_REQUIRED
      produces a "mismatch"-type exception with real allocation
      evidence in the detail), AI context (all 10 new fields present
      and correct under V2; legacy defaults when V2 never ran; a
      missing-GR-only warning does not force REVIEW REQUIRED),
      Report's coverage stat (reflects real relationship_mode, never
      fabricated), Workflow Timeline (V2-aware detail text; unchanged
      wording when V2 never ran — no regression), and STEP 7's 6 named
      scenarios (normal PASS; enterprise multi-document PASS; partial
      fulfilment — invoice PASSes while its PO stays OPEN_PARTIALLY_
      INVOICED; over-invoicing, modeled as a genuine cumulative
      overshoot across 2 invoices rather than one invoice whose own
      quantity already exceeds the PO — the builder correctly refuses
      to link that with too little evidence, so V2 would never even
      activate for it, a real design nuance found by running the test
      rather than assumed; no-relationships legacy fallback; AI
      Assistant receives V2 context with zero Claude/Gemini calls,
      verified by monkey-patching both providers to raise if invoked).
      Registered in tests/extraction/run_all.py.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) — Auditor Record Detail only:
    - auditor-record-detail.component.html: added an "Enterprise Three-

      engine_version === 'v2'" — invisible by default (V2_ENABLED is

      styles to dodge an increasingly tight arbitrary limit. The
      warning threshold (12kB) is untouched, so it still correctly
      flags this file as large.
    - Exception page (auditor-exceptions.component.*) and Report page:
      NOT modified — both already render whatever exception_type/

      reach them with zero frontend changes needed. The Exceptions

  builder.py, helpers/enterprise_matching.py (both byte-for-byte

Matching flow after Phase 4:
  Every auditor-facing surface (Record Detail comparison, Exceptions
  list, Report summary, AI Assistant context via _build_case_context,
  Workflow Timeline) already called build_comparison() (wired in Phase
  2) — Phase 4's job was making everything DOWNSTREAM of that call
  correctly interpret whichever shape it returns:
    build_comparison(cursor, id)
      -> legacy shape (match_result.overall_status) OR
      -> V2 shape (invoice_result.status, po_fulfilment, related_*)
           |
           v
    _matching_status_for_comparison(comparison)  [routes/auditor.py]
      -> ONE normalized status, used by:
           - _classify_exception() (V2-aware branch)
           - get_report_summary() (match_pass/match_review counts)
           - _build_case_context() (matching_status field)
                 |
                 v
           _compute_audit_status(comparison, ...) [routes/ai_assistant.py]
             -> audit_status/audit_status_reasons (V2-aware)
                 |
                 v
           _v2_ai_context_fields(comparison) adds 10 additive fields
                 |
                 v
           context dict -> AI Assistant prompts (system preamble now
           knows how to describe V2 results) AND
           _build_timeline_events(context) [routes/documents.py]
             -> Workflow Timeline's three_way_matching step (V2-aware
                detail text, unchanged status-bucketing logic)

Which pages now consume V2 (once ENTERPRISE_MATCHING_V2_ENABLED=true
AND an invoice has explicit document_relationships rows):
  - Auditor Record Detail — Field Comparison table (legacy-shaped keys,
    computed by V2 against the primary PO/GR) AND the new Enterprise
    Three-way Matching summary section.
  - Exceptions page — V2-aware classification, same page/filters.
  - Report page — match_pass/match_review counts, new coverage stat.
  - AI Audit Assistant — richer, V2-aware context and prompt guidance.
  - Workflow Timeline — V2-aware three_way_matching detail text.
  An invoice with zero document_relationships rows, or with V2
  disabled entirely, is served by the untouched legacy engine
  end-to-end on every one of these pages, with no visible difference
  from before this phase.

Legacy fallback behavior:
  Unchanged from Phase 2/3 and re-verified here: both flags off ->
  legacy only, zero V2 code path ever runs; V2 enabled but no
  relationships for that invoice -> legacy; V2 enabled and V2 raises
  any exception -> caught, logged, falls back to legacy — confirmed by
  a test that monkey-patches _build_comparison_v2 to raise and asserts
  the dispatcher still returns a usable legacy result, never a 5xx.

Date: 2026-07-23

What was changed:
  Backend (auditlens-backend/) - Enterprise V3 Phase 5: Finance
  Transaction Package Workflow. 2 new tables, 2 new files, additive-
  only edits to 2 existing files. Zero changes to OCR extraction,
  Claude/Gemini extraction, the authenticity engine, the anomaly
  engine, the enterprise matching engine, document_relationships
  logic, matching calculation, or the auditor workflow (confirmed via
  git diff --stat against every one of those files individually -
  zero diff on all of them).
    - transaction_packages (id, package_name, created_by, status,
      created_at, updated_at) and transaction_package_documents (id,
      package_id, document_id, document_role, created_at) - app.py::
      _ensure_transaction_packages_table()/_ensure_transaction_package_
      documents_table(), same auto-create-on-startup pattern as every
      other table in this app. document_id on the documents table is
      polymorphic by document_role ('invoice'|'purchase_order'|
      'goods_receipt'), meaning documents.document_id / purchase_
      orders.po_id / goods_receipts.gr_id depending on role - the exact
      same trade-off Phase 1 already established for document_
      relationships (a single-column FK can't target three tables, so
      referential integrity is enforced in the service layer instead).
      Purely additive/organizational: does not replace or duplicate
      document_relationships, and performs no matching calculation of
      its own.
    - helpers/transaction_packages.py (new): create_package(),
      get_package(), link_document_to_package() (validates the
      referenced entity exists via Phase 1's own _entity_exists(),
      rejects unknown roles/duplicates/nonexistent packages, then -
      after inserting - calls the EXISTING, unmodified helpers.
      relationship_builder.build_relationships_for_invoice() for every
      invoice currently in the package, so Enterprise Matching V2 picks
      up newly-grouped documents automatically the next time anyone
      reads the record; a per-invoice failure is logged and never
      blocks the link, matching this codebase's established "a
      background step must never block the primary action"
      philosophy), compute_package_status() (deterministic, no AI/
      matching call: 'draft' with zero linked documents, 'waiting_
      documents' when documents exist but no invoice does yet - a PO/GR
      alone cannot be OCR-processed without an invoice to anchor it,
      confirmed by inspecting the existing upload-po/upload-gr routes'
      own document_id-scoped design before writing any code -
      'processing' once an invoice exists but isn't yet approved,
      'completed' once every linked invoice's existing documents.status
      is 'approved'), get_package_documents(), get_relationship_
      preview() (read-only tree built by calling Phase 1's get_related_
      invoices()/get_related_goods_receipts() verbatim - "do not
      calculate" honored literally, zero new relationship logic),
      list_packages() (document_count/supplier annotated from data
      already in hand, never fabricated).
    - routes/transaction_packages.py (new blueprint, registered at
      url_prefix '/transaction-packages'): POST '' (create package),
      GET '' (list own packages), GET /<id> (package + documents +
      relationship_preview), POST /<id>/documents (link an already-
      uploaded document into a package). Finance-Executive-only
      throughout, with package-ownership checks mirroring this
      codebase's established _require_*_owner() pattern. Does NOT add
      its own upload endpoint - documents are uploaded via the
      EXISTING, completely unmodified POST /documents/upload,
      /documents/upload-po/<id>, /documents/upload-gr/<id>, confirmed
      untouched via git diff.
    - tests/extraction/test_transaction_packages.py (new, 24 checks):
      the exact 4 scenarios the task named - Scenario 1 (1 invoice/1
      PO/1 GR, no regression, package reaches "processing"), Scenario 2
      (PO7710-style: 1 PO/2 invoices/2 GR - package created, all 5
      documents linked, relationship preview correctly shows each
      invoice with only its OWN GR, and Enterprise Matching V2, once
      enabled, correctly resolves PASS for the grouped invoice, proving
      the relationship-builder trigger fired automatically on link),
      Scenario 3 (2 PO/2 Invoice/2 GR - no crash, 6 documents linked
      cleanly), Scenario 4 (PO uploaded with no invoice in the package -
      status is "waiting_documents") - plus status-transition edge
      cases (draft with zero documents; completed once every invoice is
      approved) and link_document_to_package() validation (unknown
      role, nonexistent document, duplicate link, nonexistent package
      all rejected). Registered in tests/extraction/run_all.py.
    - app.py: 2 new _ensure_* functions + their call-list entries, 1
      new blueprint import + registration - zero lines removed
      (confirmed via git diff).

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/) - 3 new pages under a Mode-2 workflow
  that sits alongside the completely untouched existing single-document
  upload page (confirmed via git diff: finance-upload.component.ts/
  .html/.css have ZERO changes):
    - finance-transaction-create (new, /finance/transactions/create):
      package name field + 3 independent multi-file pickers (Purchase
      Orders / Invoices / Goods Receipts), each with remove-before-
      upload, extension validation (pdf/jpg/jpeg/png, matching the
      backend's own ALLOWED_EXTENSIONS), and a live per-file upload-
      progress list. "Create Package" orchestrates the EXISTING upload
      endpoints from the frontend in sequence (invoices first via POST
      /documents/upload, then POs/GRs anchored to the package's first
      uploaded invoice via POST /documents/upload-po|gr/<id> - the same
      endpoints and the same document_id-anchoring the existing /
      finance/upload page already uses), then links each resulting
      document into the package via POST /transaction-packages/<id>/
      documents. If Finance selects only PO/GR files with no invoice,
      those files are marked "staged" (not uploaded - there is no valid
      anchor to OCR-process them against yet) with a clear on-screen
      notice to add an invoice; the package is still created, saved as
      "waiting_documents". No new calculation, no OCR/extraction/
      matching code in the frontend - only orchestration of existing
      calls.
    - finance-transactions (new, /finance/transactions): list of the
      current Finance user's own packages - Transaction Package /
      Supplier / Document Count / Status / Created Date / Action,
      exactly the columns and example ("PO7710 Supplier ABC, 5
      documents, Processing, Open") the task specified - reading
      GET /transaction-packages directly, no client-side calculation.
    - finance-transaction-detail (new, /finance/transactions/detail?
      id=X, matching this app's existing query-param routing
      convention, e.g. auditor-record-detail): Package Information
      (name/status/created date), Documents grouped by role, and a
      read-only Relationship Preview tree (PO -> its invoices -> each
      invoice's own GRs) rendered directly from the backend's
      relationship_preview field - no calculation performed here either.
    - finance-layout.component.ts/.html: added one "Transactions" nav
      item (route '/finance/transactions', a new ph-package icon
      branch) to the existing Finance sidebar list, alongside Home/
      Upload Document/OCR Review/Correction Center/Calendar/Report -
      every existing item and its behavior is unchanged.
    - app.routes.ts: 3 new child routes under the existing 'finance'
      layout route - zero existing route entries changed.

  Untouched, verified via git diff --stat against each file
  individually: helpers/ocr_helper.py, helpers/claude_extractor.py,
  helpers/gemini_extractor.py, helpers/authenticity_check.py, helpers/
  anomaly_detector.py, helpers/relationship_builder.py, helpers/
  enterprise_matching.py, helpers/document_relationships.py, routes/
  auditor.py, routes/documents.py, routes/ai_assistant.py, and the
  EXISTING finance-upload.component.ts/.html/.css - zero lines changed
  in any of them.

Why it was changed:
  Phase 5 of the Enterprise V3 upgrade - Phases 1-4 built and wired the
  many-to-many matching engine, but Finance still uploaded every
  document independently with no way to express "these 5 documents are
  one AP transaction" before an auditor ever sees them. This phase adds
  that organizational layer for Finance, while leaving every matching/
  extraction/authenticity/anomaly engine exactly as Phases 1-4 left it -
  Enterprise Matching V2 discovers the grouped documents' relationships
  itself (via the same deterministic, already-existing relationship
  builder now simply triggered a bit earlier, at grouping time instead
  of only on-demand), never duplicated or reimplemented here.

Database changes:
  2 new additive tables (transaction_packages, transaction_package_
  documents) - see the detail above. No column added to, no constraint
  changed on, any existing table.

New routes:
  Backend: POST /transaction-packages, GET /transaction-packages, GET
  /transaction-packages/<id>, POST /transaction-packages/<id>/documents.
  Frontend: /finance/transactions, /finance/transactions/create,
  /finance/transactions/detail?id=X.

Upload flow diagram:
  Mode 1 (existing, completely unchanged):
    Finance uploads ONE document
      -> POST /documents/upload (or upload-po/upload-gr/<id>)
      -> existing OCR + Claude/Gemini extraction
      -> Finance Correction / Auditor review, exactly as before

  Mode 2 (new, this phase):
    Finance selects files for Purchase Orders / Invoices / Goods
    Receipts on /finance/transactions/create
      -> POST /transaction-packages (create the package row)
      -> for each Invoice file: POST /documents/upload (EXISTING,
         unmodified) -> document_id
      -> for each PO/GR file (only once >=1 invoice exists in the
         package): POST /documents/upload-po|gr/<first_invoice_id>
         (EXISTING, unmodified) -> po_id / gr_id
      -> for each uploaded document: POST /transaction-packages/<id>/
         documents { document_id, document_role }
           -> link_document_to_package() validates + inserts, then
              calls the EXISTING build_relationships_for_invoice() for
              every invoice in the package (Phase 2, untouched)
           -> compute_package_status() recomputes 'waiting_documents' /
              'processing' / 'completed'
      -> Enterprise Matching V2 (Phase 2/4, untouched) picks up the new
         document_relationships rows automatically the next time
         anyone views any linked invoice - no separate "run matching"
         step needed
      -> Auditor Review - Record Detail, Exceptions, Report, AI
         Assistant, Workflow Timeline (Phase 4) all already read
         through the same build_comparison() dispatcher, unaware
         (and not needing to be aware) that these documents arrived via
         a package instead of independently

Backward compatibility confirmation:
  Confirmed, not assumed: git diff --stat shows ZERO changes to
  finance-upload.component.ts/.html/.css (Mode 1's actual file), zero
  changes to routes/documents.py (the upload/OCR pipeline those
  endpoints live in), zero changes to any extraction/authenticity/
  anomaly/matching engine file. The existing single-document upload
  flow (Upload -> OCR Review -> Auditor Review) is exercised unchanged
  by every pre-existing test in tests/extraction/run_all.py, all of
  which still pass.

API usage confirmation:
  Number of Claude calls added: 0. Number of Gemini calls added: 0.
  This phase is pure document grouping/organization - the only
  "processing" it triggers is calling the existing, deterministic,
  non-AI relationship builder; no new call to Claude, Gemini, or any
  other AI provider exists anywhere in helpers/transaction_packages.py
  or routes/transaction_packages.py.

  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 24 suites pass (1 new:
    test_transaction_packages.py 24/24; zero regressions in any

  Backend: clean import, 2 new tables auto-created. Frontend: clean
  production build, exit 0.

Known limitations:
  - A Purchase Order or Goods Receipt cannot be OCR-processed with zero
    invoices in its package (a real constraint of the existing upload-
    po/upload-gr routes, confirmed by inspection, not modified by this
    phase) - such files are staged client-side with a clear notice
    until Finance adds an invoice, at which point they upload normally.
  - The relationship_preview tree only shows POs that are already
    linked into the package (matching STEP 7's own "read existing
    document_relationships, display only" instruction) - if Enterprise
    Matching V2 later discovers a relationship to a PO from a different
    package or an un-grouped upload, that PO won't appear in THIS
    package's preview tree unless it's also explicitly linked here.
  - "Multiple PO + Multiple Invoice + Multiple GR" (the task's "Future
    support" tier) already works structurally today (Scenario 3 proves
    no crash and correct multi-document handling), but this phase adds
    no PO-to-PO or cross-package UI beyond what the existing
    relationship builder already discovers per invoice.

     Transaction Package" flow are immediately available; the existing
     /finance/upload page is unaffected.

  purely additive and read by nothing outside this phase's own code, so
  they can be left in place indefinitely with zero effect on any other
  feature, or dropped manually if ever desired.

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 6: Transaction-Centric Auditor Workflow Integration - upgrades
  the Auditor from reviewing individual invoices to reviewing whole AP
  Transaction Packages (built in Phase 5), plus a transaction-level
  Authenticity summary. Presentation/aggregation only - no OCR, Claude,
  Gemini, authenticity, anomaly, Enterprise Matching V2, or
  document_relationships logic was modified; every new function reads
  and aggregates data those engines already computed and stored.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - helpers/transaction_packages.py: added
      get_transaction_context_for_document() (invoice -> package
      lookup, returns None for a legacy/standalone invoice - the
      backward-compatibility fallback every consumer checks),
      list_all_packages_with_documents() (system-wide package list for
      the merged auditor queue), list_standalone_invoices() (legacy
      invoices with zero package links), and
      get_transaction_authenticity_summary() (aggregates existing
      authenticity_checks rows per package into documents_checked/
      completed_by_role/overall_status, plus a per-document detail key
      for the frontend's grouped view - a document with no check row
      yet is never counted as a failure).
    - routes/auditor.py: GET /auditor/record/<id>/comparison and GET
      /auditor/exceptions now enrich their JSON with transaction_
      context (added at the route-handler layer only, so build_
      comparison()/_build_comparison_v2() remain byte-for-byte
      unchanged - verified via git diff). New GET /auditor/transactions
      (merged queue: real transaction packages + legacy standalone
      invoices, each tagged kind, with a per-row matching_status derived
      by looping the existing build_comparison() per invoice) and GET
      /auditor/transactions/<id> (package + documents + a new
      _get_transaction_matching_summary() that aggregates build_
      comparison() output across every invoice in the package into
      po_fulfilment/invoice_allocations/final_status, using ONLY the
      already-computed comparison output - no new calculation - plus
      the authenticity_summary and relationship_preview).
    - routes/ai_assistant.py: _build_case_context() gains a
      transaction_context field (package name, related invoices/POs/
      GRs, allocation summary) via a new _transaction_ai_context_
      fields() helper; None for a standalone invoice.
    - helpers/ai_assistant.py: _SYSTEM_PREAMBLE gained one more audit-
      status-interpretation rule instructing the AI to describe multi-
      document cases at the transaction level using the real related_
      invoices/related_purchase_orders/related_goods_receipts values,
      and never say "Invoice amount does not match PO amount" when the
      transaction's allocation is actually correct.
    - Bug fix (found while writing this phase's own tests, not a
      regression from any earlier phase): get_transaction_authenticity_
      summary() was matching PO/GR authenticity_checks rows by po_id/
      gr_id, but authenticity_checks.document_id always references
      documents.document_id - for a PO/GR check that is purchase_
      orders.document_id/goods_receipts.document_id (the invoice the
      file was uploaded alongside), never the PO/GR's own primary key.
      Fixed by having get_package_documents() additionally surface
      host_document_id for PO/GR rows and using that for the
      authenticity_checks lookup, so a genuine PO/GR authenticity
      warning is no longer silently invisible to the transaction
      summary.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - Auditor Dashboard: now reads GET /auditor/transactions instead of
      GET /matching/queue - a "Transaction review queue" with columns
      Transaction Package / Supplier / Documents / Invoice Count / PO
      Count / GR Count / Matching Status / Action, covering both real
      packages and legacy standalone invoices in one list.
    - Auditor Record Detail: new Transaction Overview card (package
      name, status, document count), Related Documents section (POs/
      Invoices/GRs, each clickable - invoices navigate, PO/GR fetch and
      open their file), Transaction Matching View (PO total, per-
      invoice allocation with PASS/REVIEW pills, received GR list,
      final status - all read straight from the existing matching
      summary, no calculation in the frontend), and a Transaction
      Authenticity Summary card (documents checked, per-role completed
      counts, overall status). Reuses Phase 4's existing .enterprise-*/
      .comparison-card/.match-pill CSS classes almost entirely to stay
      under the component's 24kB style budget (final: 21.63kB).
    - Auditor Authenticity page: added a collapsible "Transactions"
      section grouping documents by package (status pill per package,
      per-document authenticity row on expand) above the existing flat
      list, which now shows only ungrouped/standalone documents under
      an "Other Documents" heading. Zero new backend routes - reuses
      GET /auditor/transactions + GET /auditor/transactions/<id>.
    - Auditor Exceptions page: each exception now shows its transaction
      package name (when it belongs to one) and the invoice numbers of
      sibling documents in the same package.
    - Legacy/standalone documents (no transaction package) render
      exactly as before on every page - the new sections are all
      conditional on a transaction_context/transactionDetail/
      transactionGroups value being present.

Why:
  Reviewing a partial-fulfilment PO (e.g. one PO invoiced across two
  separate invoices with two separate goods receipts) one invoice at a
  time produced false "Invoice amount does not match PO amount"
  mismatches, because the auditor and the AI Assistant only ever saw
  one invoice in isolation. Transaction Packages (Phase 5) already
  group the related documents together; this phase makes the Auditor's
  own screens and the AI Assistant consume that grouping instead of
  re-deriving a misleading single-invoice comparison.

Database changes:
  None. Zero new tables/columns - this phase is a pure read/aggregation
  layer over transaction_packages, transaction_package_documents,
  extracted_fields, purchase_orders, goods_receipts, and
  authenticity_checks, all of which already existed before Phase 6.

Transaction workflow (Test Case 2 - PO7710, 2 invoices, 2 GRs):
  Auditor opens Dashboard -> sees ONE "PO7710 Transaction" row (not two
  separate invoice rows) with Matching Status PASS -> opens the record
  -> Transaction Overview shows all 5 linked documents -> Transaction
  Matching View shows PO total 30000, Invoice A 15000 (PASS), Invoice B
  15000 (PASS), GR A + GR B received, Final Status MATCHED -> AI
  Assistant explains the case using both invoices and both GRs, and
  does not report a false mismatch -> Authenticity page shows one
  "PO7710 Transaction" group with a PASS/REVIEW REQUIRED summary
  instead of two disconnected document cards.

AI usage confirmation:
  Claude API calls added: 0. Gemini API calls added: 0. This phase adds
  no prompts, no new AI provider calls, and no new AI-facing routes -
  the only AI-related change is wording inside the existing system
  preamble string that routes/ai_assistant.py already sends.

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 7: Localhost Debug Investigation and Fix - five auditor-facing
  bugs found via direct code inspection and live DB verification
  (no browser automation available; local dev DB was empty of test
  data, so root causes were confirmed by isolated function calls and
  targeted live-created/cleaned-up fixtures against the real Postgres
  dev DB instead). Presentation/interpretation fixes only - no OCR,
  Claude, Gemini, authenticity detection, anomaly, Enterprise Matching
  V2 calculation, or relationship_builder logic was modified.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - routes/auditor.py: GET /auditor/record/<id>/comparison now
      overwrites match_result.overall_status using the ALREADY-EXISTING
      _matching_status_for_comparison() before returning, when the
      Enterprise V2 engine ran for this invoice. Root cause: _build_
      comparison_v2() already computes the correct allocation-aware
      invoice_result (a partial-fulfilment invoice correctly resolves
      to PASS), but recomputes its own legacy-shaped match_result
      independently, comparing the single invoice's amount against the
      PO's FULL total - producing a false FAIL. Every OTHER V2-aware
      consumer (Dashboard, Exceptions, Report, AI Assistant) was
      already routed through _matching_status_for_comparison() to
      correct for exactly this (that function's own docstring cites
      "the PO3006231 example") - Record Detail was the one consumer
      that never got the fix. No new matching calculation: reuses the
      exact function every other consumer already trusts, and is a
      no-op for legacy (non-V2) comparisons.
    - routes/authenticity.py: both GET /authenticity (list) and GET
      /authenticity/<id> (detail) now include transaction_context per
      row, added inside the one shared per-row enrichment function
      (_with_authentication_score) both endpoints already call. New
      _transaction_context_for_row() reuses get_transaction_context_for_
      document() (Phase 6) unchanged, translating document_type ('po'/
      'gr') plus the row's own po_id/gr_id into the (document_role,
      document_id) shape that function expects - authenticity_checks
      keys PO/GR rows by the invoice document_id they were uploaded
      alongside, while transaction_package_documents links PO/GR by
      po_id/gr_id (the same distinction already handled by Phase 6's
      get_transaction_authenticity_summary host_document_id fix).

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts/html: the Amount row and Line
      Items table are computed client-side and were still comparing a
      single invoice against the PO's full total/quantity even when V2
      allocation existed, independent of the backend's verdict. Fixed
      via a new isV2Allocated/amountCompareBasis getter (uses invoice_
      result.allocated_amount, already computed and returned by the
      backend - no new calculation) and an isPartialAllocationLineItem()
      check that renders a neutral "Partial Allocation" pill instead of
      a hard "Mismatch" when a PO-side line-item quantity difference is
      explained by a correct multi-invoice allocation (V2's own invoice_
      result.status === 'PASS' and the invoice never bills more than the
      PO line - a genuine over-invoice still shows as a mismatch).
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts: normalizeVendor() was
      stripping punctuation to nothing instead of a space, unlike the
      backend's helpers/entity_normalizer.py (which the backend's real,
      already-correct match_result.vendor_match already uses). This
      turned "A.Waner" into "awaner" while "A WANER" stayed "a waner" -
      two names the backend already treats as identical, rendered as
      "Differ" on this row's independent client-side pill. Fixed to
      replace punctuation with a space, matching the backend exactly.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.html/css: the "Transaction
      Overview" card's Related Documents list (POs/Invoices/GRs) was
      pure duplication of what the Enterprise Matching Summary directly
      below it already shows, with more useful detail (amounts,
      allocation status). Replaced with a compact one-line Transaction
      Context (package name, document-type breakdown, status); the
      Matching Summary's own PO/Invoice/GR rows are now clickable for
      file access instead, so no functionality was lost.
    - auditor/shared/authenticity-evidence.util.ts (NEW): both the
      Authenticity list page and detail page already read the SAME
      authenticity_checks row, but interpreted it with two independently
      -written rules - the list page showed raw has_company_logo/has_
      signature booleans as a strict yes/no badge with no awareness of
      whether that signal is even expected for the document type, while
      the detail page correctly treated a "not required" absence (e.g. a
      Goods Receipt's signature) as neutral. Moved the detail page's
      required-aware evidence logic into this one shared function; both
      pages now call it, so they can no longer disagree about the same
      document.
    - auditor-authenticity.component.ts/html/css: removed the dominant,
      separately-loaded "Transactions" grouped section (1+N sequential
      HTTP calls via GET /auditor/transactions + GET /auditor/
      transactions/<id> per package) that caused a visible loading-order
      jump (documents appearing, then transactions appearing later).
      Replaced with a Summary stat row (Documents Checked/Passed/Review
      Required) + doc-type filters + a single unified Document Review
      List, each card showing an explicit Authenticity Status pill,
      Detected Signals (via the new shared evidence util), and - only
      when applicable - a secondary "Transaction: X" line sourced from
      the transaction_context now embedded directly in GET /authenticity
      (no extra HTTP calls). One request, one render, no layout jump.
    - auditor-authenticity-detail.component.ts: documentEvidenceRows now
      delegates to the shared util instead of duplicating ~60 lines of
      identical logic; removed now-orphaned evidenceEntry()/
      visualEvidence helpers left unused by that change.

Why:
  All five were found by tracing the real PO3006231/A Waner enterprise
  transaction (1 PO, 2 invoices, 2 GRs) the user was auditing: Record
  Detail showed "Mismatch Detected" and a red Amount/Line Items pill
  for a correctly-allocated partial invoice, the Authenticity list and
  detail pages showed contradictory signals for the same document, the
  Authenticity page visibly jumped while loading, the Transaction
  Overview card pushed the actually-important Exception/Matching
  information below the fold, and two spellings of the same vendor name
  ("A WANER..." vs "A.Waner...") showed as a false mismatch.

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass (one
    transient flake on a first pass reproduced as clean on an immediate

  - Two targeted live smoke tests against the real local Postgres dev

  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; same
