----------------------------------------------------------------------

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Two workflow bugs found after Phase 7, traced to a single upstream
  root cause: transaction package membership had no protection against
  the same real invoice being linked into two different packages.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - helpers/transaction_packages.py: link_document_to_package() only
      ever checked whether a document was already linked to the SAME
      package - nothing prevented it from also being linked into a
      DIFFERENT package. New find_existing_package_for_invoice()
      matches an invoice against every OTHER package's invoices by
      invoice_number (normalized-exact) + vendor (existing fuzzy is_
      same_company()) + amount (existing AMOUNT_TOLERANCE) + invoice_
      date (3-day tolerance) - all four must agree, deliberately strict
      so two genuinely different invoices are never blocked. When
      linking a document with document_role='invoice', a match in a
      different package now returns a clear error identifying that
      package instead of silently creating a fragmented duplicate
      grouping. No new matching engine: reuses the exact vendor/amount
      comparators already trusted elsewhere in this app.

Why:
  Fixed matching calculation caused false mismatch in Record Detail
  comparison using allocation-aware matching. The Phase 7 fix (compare
  against Enterprise V2's allocated_amount instead of the PO's full
  total) only engages when engine_version === 'v2', which requires the
  invoice to have document_relationships rows. _rebuild_relationships_
  for_package() only ever runs the relationship builder for invoices
  that are members of THAT specific package - so an invoice fragmented
  into a second, PO/GR-less package (nothing previously stopped this)
  never gets a chance to link to its real PO/GR, engine_version stays
  legacy for it, and Record Detail falls back to the old single-invoice-
  vs-full-PO comparison regardless of the Phase 7 display fix already
  being correct. Root cause traced to duplicate invoice transaction
  creation causing incorrect "Missing PO and GR": with the membership
  guard in place, an invoice can no longer be split across two
  packages, so this class of false mismatch can no longer occur going
  forward. Improved transaction grouping consistency: one invoice now
  belongs to exactly one transaction package, enforced at link time.

  helpers/relationship_builder.py and helpers/enterprise_matching.py
  were read to confirm they already handle multiple sibling invoices
  sharing one PO correctly (each gets its own full allocation against a
  single matching PO candidate) - neither needed a change; the gap was
  entirely in package membership, not matching calculation.

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass, including
    test_transaction_packages.py (existing single-invoice-per-package
    linking scenarios still pass unaffected by the new guard).
  - Live smoke test against the real local Postgres dev DB (rows
    created and cleaned up): a duplicate invoice (same invoice_number/
    vendor/amount/date, a different document_id simulating a re-upload)
    attempting to link into a second package is now rejected with an
    error naming the original package - confirmed blocked.
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; same
    pre-existing bundle-size warnings, no new errors; no frontend files
    changed this round).

Build result:
  Backend: all 25 test suites pass. Frontend: clean production build,
  exit 0 (no frontend changes needed this round).

AI usage confirmation:
  Claude calls: 0. Gemini calls: 0.

Known limitation:
  This fix is preventive - it stops the duplicate-package scenario
  from happening again, but does not retroactively merge or clean up
  any transaction package already fragmented by this bug before the
  fix was deployed. Any already-created duplicate ("Testing"-style)
  package would need a manual one-off cleanup if it exists in a live
  environment.

Deployment instructions:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND - no migration step, no new
     environment variables.
  2. No frontend redeploy needed this round.
  3. No config changes needed.

Rollback instructions:
  Redeploy the previous backend build - this change only adds a guard
  check before an INSERT that already existed; rolling back removes
  the guard but affects no existing data.

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 7.1: corrected the previous fix, which was built on the wrong
  assumption. The earlier change blocked linking an invoice into a
  second transaction package (treating it as an accidental duplicate
  re-upload). That was wrong: the real scenario is two GENUINELY
  DIFFERENT, legitimate invoices (different invoice numbers) that both
  belong to the same real PO transaction, which simply never converged
  into one package. Blocking is gone; replaced with auto-grouping.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - helpers/transaction_packages.py: removed find_existing_package_
      for_invoice() (the invoice-number/vendor/amount/date duplicate
      BLOCKER from the previous fix) and its call site inside link_
      document_to_package(), which is back to its original, unmodified
      Phase 5 shape. Replaced with three new functions: _lookup_po_
      reference_and_vendor() (an invoice/GR's own po_reference, or a
      PO's own po_number, plus vendor), _find_package_with_matching_po()
      and _find_package_with_matching_invoice_po_ref() (search this same
      Finance user's OTHER existing packages for one already anchored on
      the same PO, matching by normalized PO reference + fuzzy vendor -
      the mirror-image pair covers both upload orders: PO-uploaded-first
      and invoice-uploaded-first), and resolve_package_for_document()
      (the public entry point combining them, falling back to the
      originally-requested package_id whenever no match is found).
      _normalize_po_reference() mirrors routes/auditor.py's own
      _normalize_ref() (strips a leading "PO"/"PO-" prefix so "3006231"
      and "PO3006231" compare equal) - duplicated rather than imported,
      since helpers/ modules never import from routes/ (routes/auditor.py
      already imports from this module).
    - routes/transaction_packages.py: POST /transaction-packages/<id>/
      documents now calls resolve_package_for_document() before linking,
      scoped to the requesting Finance user's own packages only (no
      ownership leak), and reports redirected_from_package_id in the
      response when the document landed in a different package than
      requested, so Finance can see why.

Why:
  Fixed duplicate invoice transaction creation causing incorrect
  "Missing PO and GR": when Finance links two sibling invoices for the
  same PO into two different packages (in either order - PO first or
  invoice first), the relationship builder only ever runs for invoices
  that are members of THAT specific package
  (_rebuild_relationships_for_package), so the fragmented invoice never
  gets a chance to link to its real PO/GR - engine_version stays legacy
  for it and Record Detail falls back to the single-invoice-vs-full-PO
  comparison regardless of the Phase 7 allocation-aware display fix.
  Improved transaction grouping consistency: two invoices referencing
  the same PO number (by po_reference/po_number, fuzzy vendor match)
  now always converge into the SAME package automatically, without
  ever blocking or erroring - Finance can still explicitly link a
  document into more than one package if they choose to.

  helpers/relationship_builder.py and helpers/enterprise_matching.py
  were not touched - confirmed (again) that they already correctly
  give each sibling invoice its own full allocation once both are
  members of the same package; the gap was entirely in which package
  each one ended up in.

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 9: fixed the "Testing 1"/"Testing 2" empty-package regression
  reported after Phase 7.1/8's transaction auto-grouping changes.

  Root cause (confirmed by live reproduction, not assumed): the
  auto-grouping added in Phase 7.1 was working exactly as designed —
  when Finance created a brand new package and uploaded a document
  whose PO reference matched an ALREADY-EXISTING package (e.g. a
  package created during earlier testing of the same PO3006231 fixture
  data), the document correctly and silently redirected into that
  existing package. The bug was that the FRONTEND never surfaced this:
  it navigated Finance to the ORIGINAL, now-empty package_id regardless,
  and never told them where their documents actually went. Reproduced
  directly: creating package "A Waner" with PO3006231 + an invoice,
  then creating a brand new package "Testing 1" and uploading a second
  invoice referencing the same PO, showed "Testing 1" ending with 0
  documents while "A Waner" silently grew from 2 to 3 — exactly the
  reported symptom, with nothing actually lost.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - routes/transaction_packages.py: the auto-grouping resolution call
      in POST /transaction-packages/<id>/documents is now wrapped in
      try/except, falling back to the originally-requested package_id
      on any unexpected failure — matching this module's own
      established "best-effort convenience must never block the
      primary action" philosophy (_rebuild_relationships_for_package,
      _ensure_sibling_checks). New DELETE /transaction-packages/<id>
      (Finance-only, owner-only) for the "do not create empty draft
      packages" cleanup described below.
    - helpers/transaction_packages.py: new delete_empty_package() -
      deletes a package ONLY if it has zero linked documents; refuses
      (returns False, no delete) for any package with even one document,
      so it can never be used to remove a package Finance is actually
      using.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - finance-transaction-create.component.ts: uploadAndLink() now
      returns the package the document ACTUALLY landed in (already
      present in the existing link response, just not read before).
      After the upload batch, if the anchor invoice's documents landed
      in a different, pre-existing package, the newly created (now
      empty) package is deleted via the new DELETE endpoint, Finance is
      navigated to the CORRECT package instead, and a clear message
      explains the auto-grouping ("...automatically grouped into the
      existing transaction package "X"") instead of silently leaving
      them looking at an empty "Draft" package with Supplier: Unknown.

Why:
  This directly satisfies the two explicit Phase 9 requirements: "If no
  existing package exists, documents must still attach to the newly
  created package" (already true; confirmed by re-testing the exact
  5-document PO3006231 scenario from a clean state) and "Do not create
  empty draft packages" (the new package is deleted once Finance is
  shown where their documents actually are). Phase 8's business logic
  (auto-group matching invoices into the same PO's package) is fully
  preserved — nothing about the matching/redirect decision itself
  changed, only its visibility and the empty-shell cleanup.

  helpers/relationship_builder.py, helpers/enterprise_matching.py, OCR,
  Claude/Gemini extraction, and the authenticity engine were not
  touched - this was entirely a package-linking/UX gap, not a matching
  or extraction bug.

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass.
  - Live smoke tests against the real local Postgres dev DB (rows
    created and cleaned up):
    (1) Reproduction: pre-existing package "A Waner" (PO3006231 +
        invoice) + a brand new package "Testing 1" + a second invoice
        referencing the same PO -> confirmed "Testing 1" ends with 0
        documents and "A Waner" grows to 3, with the response's
        redirected_from_package_id correctly identifying this - proving
        the auto-grouping itself was never broken, only invisible.
    (2) The exact 5-document PO3006231 scenario from a clean state (no
        pre-existing package) -> ONE package, 5 documents, PO=1
        Invoice=2 GR=2 - confirms "no existing package" case still
        attaches to the newly created package as required.
    (3) DELETE /transaction-packages/<id> refuses a non-empty package
        (400) and succeeds on a genuinely empty one (200).
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; same
    pre-existing bundle-size warnings, no new errors).

Build result:
  Backend: all 25 test suites pass. Frontend: clean production build,
  exit 0.

AI usage confirmation:
  Claude calls: 0. Gemini calls: 0.

Known limitation:
  This fix prevents new empty "Draft" packages from being left behind
  going forward. Any "Testing 1"/"Testing 2"-style empty packages
  already sitting in a live environment from before this fix are

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 10: fixed "Object of type memoryview is not JSON serializable"
  on Record Detail's Open button.

  Root cause (confirmed by reproducing with real bytea content, not
  assumed): helpers/document_relationships.py's get_related_purchase_
  orders(), get_related_goods_receipts(), and get_related_invoices()
  each ran a bare SELECT * (or documents d.*) against purchase_orders/
  goods_receipts/documents - all three of which have a file_bytes BYTEA
  column (the durable, DB-stored copy of the original uploaded file,
  used because Render's disk is ephemeral). psycopg2 returns a BYTEA
  value as a Python memoryview, which Flask's jsonify() cannot
  serialize. These three functions are called directly by _build_
  comparison_v2() (routes/auditor.py) and their raw output is returned
  verbatim as related_purchase_orders/related_invoices/related_goods_
  receipts in GET /auditor/record/<id>/comparison's JSON response -
  the exact endpoint Record Detail's Open button loads.

  This bug is NOT new - it has existed in helpers/document_
  relationships.py since Phase 1, before this session's work began.
  It stayed silently dormant because Enterprise Matching V2 (which is
  the only code path that calls these three functions) wasn't
  successfully engaging until Phase 9.1/the user's own environment fix
  - the moment V2 started actually running, this pre-existing leak
  surfaced for the first time.

  The rest of this codebase already handles this correctly in every
  other place BYTEA columns get read for a JSON response (routes/
  documents.py's get_po_list/get_gr_list/get_supporting_documents all
  explicitly `row.pop('file_bytes', None)`) - document_relationships.py
  was the one place that had never been audited for it, since its
  SELECT * queries predate the file_bytes column's introduction.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - helpers/document_relationships.py: all 6 SELECT sites across the
      three functions now strip file_bytes from the returned dict
      before it's used, matching the exact convention already
      established in routes/documents.py. No other columns touched -
      every other metadata field (file_name, file_type, vendor_name,
      amounts, etc.) is preserved exactly as before. The actual file
      content remains available exactly as before, through the
      existing, unmodified file-serving endpoints (GET /documents/
      <id>/file, /documents/po/<po_id>/file, /documents/gr/<gr_id>/
      file) - nothing about file download/view changed.

Why:
  Auditors could not open a Record Detail page for any invoice whose
  Enterprise Matching V2 relationships included a PO/GR/sibling invoice
  with its file bytes stored in the database (i.e. essentially every
  real uploaded document) - the comparison API 500'd before any data
  reached the page.

  enterprise_matching.py and relationship_builder.py were not touched -
  this was purely a JSON-serialization bug in how already-fetched
  rows were shaped for the API response, not a matching calculation
  issue. OCR, Claude/Gemini extraction, and the authenticity engine
  were not touched either.

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass, including
    test_document_relationships.py (no regression in the existing
    relationship-lookup behavior).
  - Live smoke test against the real local Postgres dev DB, this time
    with file_bytes ACTUALLY populated (psycopg2.Binary, matching a
    real uploaded document - my earlier tests had always left it NULL,
    which coincidentally serializes fine and would never have caught
    this) for the PO3006231 scenario (PO + 2 invoices + 2 GRs, V2
    relationships already established): GET /auditor/record/<id>/
    comparison now returns HTTP 200 with engine_version "v2", and
    related_purchase_orders/related_invoices/related_goods_receipts
    confirmed to contain no file_bytes key at all.
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; no
    frontend changes this round, same pre-existing warnings only).

Build result:
  Backend: all 25 test suites pass. Frontend: clean production build,
  exit 0 (no frontend changes).

AI usage confirmation:
  Claude calls: 0. Gemini calls: 0.

Deployment instructions:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND - no migration step, no new
     environment variables.
  2. No frontend redeploy needed this round.
  3. No config changes needed.

  Redeploy the previous backend build - this fix only removes one key

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 11: fixed false "Missing on PO"/"Missing on Invoice" line-item
  labels for a genuinely-matched item whose wording differs completely
  across documents.

  Root cause (confirmed via a live reproduction using the exact
  PO3006231 item text): routes/auditor.py's _find_line_item_match()
  pairs line items across Invoice/PO/GR by (in order) item_code, exact
  normalized description, then a substring-containment check. For this
  real item, no item_code was stored on any side, and the descriptions
  share no substring relationship at all ("Zipper Bag 205*275mm with
  Logo" on the PO/GR vs "PRINTING: RECYCLE LOGO (BASE: PE TRAN)(BLACK
  1+0) - ZIPLOCK BAG 205MM X 275MM..." on the invoice - genuinely the
  same physical item, described completely differently by each
  document). All three pairing strategies legitimately failed, so
  _match_line_items() produced TWO separate unpaired rows instead of
  one matched row: the invoice's own line with missing_on_po=True, and
  the PO's line (also pulled in via the GR-pairing pass) with missing_
  on_invoice=True - exactly the false red labels reported.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - routes/auditor.py: _match_line_items() gained a "sole-line-item
      fallback" - when the invoice has exactly one line item and the
      document being compared against also has exactly one, they are
      paired unconditionally, even when item_code/description matching
      both come up empty. This only applies when there is exactly one
      unambiguous candidate on each side, so it can never mis-pair one
      of several genuinely different items - the existing item_code and
      description matching remain the primary, tried-first signals for
      the multi-line-item case. Each row also now carries invoice_
      description/po_description/gr_description (additive) alongside
      the existing single canonical description, so the frontend can
      show what each document actually called the item.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts/html: Line Items PO/GR cells
      now show the other document's own wording as small italic context
      text ("PO Item: ...", "GR Item: ...") whenever it genuinely
      differs from the canonical description shown in the row's
      field-name column - informational only, never styled as a
      mismatch.

Why:
  Once a line item is correctly paired on one row, the EXISTING
  allocation-aware display logic (Phase 7/8's isPartialAllocationLineItem/
  lineItemPoDisplayQuantity) already renders it correctly as an
  allocation Match with the PO's full quantity shown as context - no
  further frontend changes were needed for that part. The only actual
  gap was that the item never got paired into one row in the first
  place.

  enterprise_matching.py and relationship_builder.py were not touched -
  this was a line-item pairing issue local to routes/auditor.py, not a
  matching-calculation or relationship-building issue. OCR, Claude/
  Gemini extraction, and the authenticity engine were not touched
  either.

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 12: fixed a false red "Mismatch" on the GR column of a Line
  Items row that was already correctly matched, and the row's red
  background persisting even when the invoice's overall matching
  status was PASS.

  Root cause (confirmed by tracing the exact rendering logic): the GR
  column's pill/icon/text (auditor-record-detail.component.ts) read
  li.quantity_match — a single BLENDED 3-way flag ("are invoice, PO,
  and GR quantities ALL equal at once") — instead of comparing the
  invoice's quantity against the GR's OWN quantity specifically. For
  the real PO3006231 case, invoice=15000 and GR=15000 (an exact match),
  but PO=30000 (a correct partial allocation, already softened for the
  PO column in Phase 11/8) made the BLENDED flag false, and that false
  value leaked into the GR column's pill even though GR and invoice
  agreed perfectly. The row's red background had the same root cause
  one level up: it fell back to a plain row-mismatch class whenever
  li.amount_match was false, without checking whether that too was
  just the PO's full amount vs the invoice's allocated share (already
  known to be a valid allocation from the Amount row directly above it
  in the same page).

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts: new lineItemSideQuantityMatch
      (li, side) does a genuine PAIRWISE comparison (invoice vs THIS
      side's own quantity only) instead of relying on the blended flag.
      lineItemPillClass/Icon/Text and lineItemRowClass now use this for
      both the PO and GR columns (the PO column keeps its existing
      allocation-aware override from Phase 8/11 layered on top - a PO
      quantity difference explained by a valid partial allocation still
      shows Match). lineItemRowClass also no longer shows a red
      background for a soft amount_match difference when V2's own
      invoice_result already confirmed this row is a correct allocation
      - the SAME reasoning already applied to quantity. lineItemPo
      DisplayQuantity's allocation-detection condition was updated to
      match (a small new showPoAllocationContext() helper, replacing a
      duplicated inline condition in the template).

Why:
  A completely genuine GR match (15000 received == 15000 invoiced) was
  showing as a hard "Mismatch" purely because an unrelated column's
  (the PO's) raw, un-allocated total happened to differ - a false
  signal an auditor could easily misread as "goods weren't fully
  received," when in fact the goods receipt was exactly correct. The
  row's persistent red background compounded this: once every
  individual field genuinely matched (Vendor, PO Ref, Amount, and now
  GR), there was no remaining reason for the row to still read as a
  problem.

  enterprise_matching.py and relationship_builder.py were not touched -
  this was purely a rendering/interpretation issue in how the ALREADY-
  correct backend comparison data (unchanged since Phase 11) gets
  turned into pills and row styling. No backend changes were needed
  this round at all. OCR, Claude/Gemini extraction, and the
  authenticity engine were not touched either.

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass (no backend
    changes this round; run to confirm nothing else regressed).
  - Manually traced the fixed logic against the exact reported case
    (invoice=15000, po_quantity=30000, gr_quantity=15000, invoice_
    result.status="PASS"): PO column -> Match (allocated, 15000 shown
    with PO Ordered context 30000, unchanged from Phase 11); GR column
    -> now correctly Match (15000 == 15000, was previously Mismatch);
    row class -> no hard issue, amount_match softened by the same
    allocation reasoning -> empty class list, no red background at all.
    A genuinely under-received GR (a real quantity shortfall) still
    correctly flags as a hard Mismatch, confirming the fix doesn't mask
    real problems.
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; same
    pre-existing bundle-size warnings, no new errors).

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 14 (frontend display fix only): Record Detail's Source
  Documents section now shows every related Invoice/PO/GR, not just
  one of each.

  Root cause: the Source Documents buttons bound to comparison.invoice/
  comparison.po/comparison.gr - singular objects holding only the
  "primary" PO and "primary" GR (the first related one selected by
  _build_comparison_v2, or the legacy co-located one) - never the full
  related-documents arrays. For a transaction with 2 invoices, 1 PO,
  and 2 GRs, this meant only 1 invoice/1 PO/1 GR button could ever
  render, no matter how many documents actually existed - the section
  had no way to loop over more than one of each type.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - auditor-record-detail.component.html: when this invoice belongs
      to a Transaction Package, Source Documents now renders one button
      per Invoice/PO/GR from transactionDetail.documents - data ALREADY
      loaded by the existing loadTransactionDetail() call for the
      Transaction Overview card above (no new API call). Falls back to
      the exact previous single-document behavior (unchanged) for a
      standalone/legacy invoice with no package, so nothing regresses
      for that case.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.ts: new openSourceInvoice(
      documentId) - opens the CURRENT invoice's own file in the
      existing in-page preview modal (openDocModal, unchanged), or
      navigates to a SIBLING invoice's own Record Detail page
      (openTransactionDocument, already existing and already used by
      the Transaction Overview's Matching Summary rows since Phase 7).
      PO/GR buttons reuse openTransactionDocument() directly, exactly
      as already used elsewhere on this page - no new fetching/opening
      logic was written anywhere in this change.
    - auditor-record-detail.component.css: two small additive rules
      for the new per-type group labels (Invoices / Purchase Orders /
      Goods Receipts headings above each button row).

Why:
  An auditor reviewing a transaction with multiple invoices sharing one
  PO, or multiple goods receipts against one PO, previously had no way
  to open every document from Record Detail - only whichever one
  happened to be selected as "primary" was reachable via Source
  Documents (the sibling documents were only viewable by first
  navigating to their own transaction context elsewhere on the page).

  No backend files were touched - OCR extraction, Claude/Gemini
  extraction, transaction package logic, relationship_builder,
  Enterprise Matching V2, three-way matching calculation, and the
  authenticity engine are completely unmodified; the API response
  structure did not change at all.

Test results:
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; the
    record-detail component's CSS budget usage stayed comfortably
    under the 24kB error threshold at 21.75kB; same pre-existing
    bundle-size warning, no new errors).
  - No backend changes this round, so python tests/extraction/run_all.py
    was not re-run (nothing in it could have been affected) - git diff
    --stat against auditlens-backend/ confirmed empty.

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 15: added a Delete management feature for Transaction Packages
  (Finance's Transaction Packages page).

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - helpers/transaction_packages.py: new delete_package(package_id) -
      deletes a package and every document EXCLUSIVELY owned by it. A
      document also linked to a DIFFERENT package (checked per
      (document_role, document_id) pair via transaction_package_
      documents) is left completely untouched - only this package's
      own membership link disappears. Also accounts for the legacy
      "co-located" PO/GR case (purchase_orders/goods_receipts.
      document_id -> documents is ON DELETE NO ACTION, not CASCADE, so
      an un-linked co-located PO/GR would otherwise block deleting its
      host invoice) - unless that co-located PO/GR is itself
      independently linked to a different package, in which case the
      invoice is left untouched too rather than risking an incorrect
      delete. Every statement runs on ONE transaction (commits only
      once every delete has succeeded; any failure rolls back the
      entire operation, so a package can never be left half-deleted).
      No matching/relationship CALCULATION logic is touched anywhere -
      every delete is a plain row removal of already-computed data, in
      FK-safe order (verified against the actual live schema's FK
      constraints before writing a single line).
    - routes/transaction_packages.py: new DELETE /transaction-packages/
      <id>/force route (Finance-only, package-owner-only) calling
      delete_package(). Deliberately a SEPARATE route from the existing
      DELETE /transaction-packages/<id> (which stays completely
      unmodified) - that route is called automatically and silently by
      the create-package flow to clean up an empty "ghost" package
      (Phase 9) and must keep refusing anything non-empty; this new
      route is the explicit, user-confirmed "delete everything" action,
      only ever reachable from a confirmation modal.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - finance-transactions.component.ts/html/css: added a Delete button
      beside the existing Open button in the Transaction Packages
      table, and a confirmation modal ("Delete this transaction package
      and all related documents? This action cannot be undone.") before
      calling the new endpoint. On success: the package list refreshes
      automatically and a success message is shown; on failure, the
      error is shown inside the modal without closing it.

Why:
  Gives Finance a way to remove a transaction package (e.g. one created
  by mistake, or a test/duplicate) along with its documents, without
  needing direct database access - while guaranteeing a document shared
  with another package (Phase 7.1 explicitly allows this) is never
  deleted out from under that other package.

  helpers/relationship_builder.py, helpers/enterprise_matching.py, OCR
  extraction, Claude/Gemini extraction, and the authenticity engine
  were not touched. Transaction package CREATION logic, auto-grouping
  logic (resolve_package_for_document), and document LINKING logic
  (link_document_to_package) are all completely unmodified - this
  phase only adds a new deletion path alongside them.

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass, including
    test_transaction_packages.py (existing package creation/linking
    behavior unaffected).
  - Live smoke test against the real local Postgres dev DB (rows
    created and cleaned up), covering every requirement explicitly:
    (1) deleted Package A (PO3006231, 2 invoices, 2 GRs, all
    exclusively owned) via the real DELETE .../force endpoint - package
    disappears from the list, and all 5 documents are confirmed gone
    from documents/purchase_orders/goods_receipts; (2) a completely
    separate Package B (unrelated invoice) is confirmed untouched -
    still listed, its document still in the DB; (3) an invoice
    deliberately linked into BOTH Package C and Package D - deleting
    Package C reports 0 deleted invoices / 1 kept-shared-document, the
    shared invoice is confirmed still in the DB, and Package D still
    shows it - the safety rule holds. Package C itself was still
    correctly removed from the list.
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; same
    pre-existing bundle-size warnings, no new errors).

Build result:
  Backend: all 25 test suites pass. Frontend: clean production build,
  exit 0.

AI usage confirmation:
  Claude calls: 0. Gemini calls: 0.

Deployment instructions:
  1. Redeploy the Render BACKEND - no migration step, no new
     environment variables.
  2. Redeploy the Render FRONTEND - the Delete button and confirmation
     modal are immediately available.
  3. No config changes needed.

Rollback instructions:
  Redeploy the previous backend/frontend build - the new DELETE .../
  force route and delete_package() are purely additive; the existing
  DELETE /transaction-packages/<id> (empty-only) route and its
  behavior are completely unchanged, so rolling back only removes the
  new deletion capability, nothing else.

Date: 2026-07-23
What was changed:
  Phase 16: authentication flow hardening + a real Admin login
  destination.

  Backend (auditlens-backend/):
    - routes/auth.py: POST /auth/register's allowed_roles no longer
      includes 'admin' (was ['admin', 'finance_executive', 'auditor'],
      now ['finance_executive', 'auditor']) - the actual security fix.
      Previously any client could self-register with role: 'admin' and
      receive a working admin account. POST /admin/users/create
      (routes/admin.py, unmodified) still allows an EXISTING admin to
      create another admin, since that action already requires an
      admin's own JWT - only the PUBLIC, unauthenticated registration
      path was closed.
    - app.py: new _ensure_admin_seed_account() - the one initial admin
      account (loylth910@gmail.com), inserted directly into the
      database with the exact same bcrypt hashing routes/auth.py's own
      register()/login() already use (no new hashing/auth mechanism).
      Idempotent and safe to run on every boot, same auto-run-on-
      startup pattern as every other _ensure_ function in this file
      (CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS, etc.) - a no-op once the account
      exists, so redeploying never duplicates or errors. Runs
      automatically the next time the backend deploys; no manual
      database access was used or needed to create it.

  Frontend (auditlens-frontend/):
    - register.component.ts: removed the "Admin" option from the role
      dropdown entirely (now only Finance Executive / Auditor).
    - New admin/admin-layout + admin/dashboard components - a real
      landing page for role === 'admin' after login (previously
      login.component.ts already routed admin to /admin/home, but
      that route didn't exist at all, so it 404'd). A genuine
      placeholder as scoped: reads the EXISTING, unmodified GET
      /admin/statistics endpoint (routes/admin.py, already built with
      a full set of admin endpoints - users, documents, exceptions,
      audit logs - none of which had a frontend consumer yet) for a
      few summary numbers, with a note that fuller admin screens are a
      future phase. No hardcoded admin login logic anywhere in the
      frontend - the ONLY thing that determines admin access is the
      role value the backend returns after a normal password check.
    - app.routes.ts: registered /admin (layout) and /admin/home
      (dashboard) - additive only, every existing route unchanged.

Why:
  Fixed the actual vulnerability: public registration could mint an
  admin account for anyone who simply POSTed role: "admin". Also
  completed the admin login path that was already half-wired
  (login.component.ts's redirect existed, but had nowhere to land).

  Document upload, OCR, transaction packages, Enterprise Matching V2,
  the auditor workflow, and extraction/authenticity/anomaly logic were
  not touched at all - confirmed via git diff --stat against those
  files/directories (empty).

Test results:
  - python tests/extraction/run_all.py - all 25 suites pass (no
    matching/extraction/authenticity logic was touched, run to confirm
    nothing else regressed).
  - Live smoke test against the real local Postgres dev DB: Finance
    Executive registration succeeds (role finance_executive); Auditor
    registration succeeds (role auditor); registering with role=admin
    is correctly rejected with 400 and no row is created; the seeded
    admin account (loylth910@gmail.com / admin123) logs in successfully
    and the response's role is "admin"; both newly-registered Finance
    and Auditor users can also log in normally (existing login() path
    confirmed unaffected).
  - Confirmed the admin seed function is idempotent: importing app.py
    twice creates the account once ("Admin seed account created"),
    then reports "Admin seed account already exists" on the second run.
  - npx ng build --configuration production - succeeded (exit 0; same
    pre-existing bundle-size warnings, no new errors).

Build result:
  Backend: all 25 test suites pass, admin account seeded successfully
  on import. Frontend: clean production build, exit 0.

  Claude calls: 0. Gemini calls: 0.
